# ISLAM
*Source: KASHKOLE, Binder 36 (ISLAM IMAN IHSAN), Chapter 175. 19 topics. Language: ur.*

<!-- section 1 (id=5768, raw_sort=1): Islam as an experience -->

## Islām as an Experience (Phenomenology of Submission)

***Your non-muslim friend comes to you and asks: What is Islam? How would you define Islam for her?***

There is a hadees in which Jabraeel AS comes to Rasul Allah(S) in the form of a man, and asks him 4 questions. He asks him what is ISLAM; what is IMAN; what is IHSAN and he asks about the signs of the end of time. So when he asks, What is Islam, Rasul Allah(S) replies.....
⟪ar-quote:الْإِسْلَامُ أَنْ تَشْهَدَ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَیْهِ وَسَلَّمَ⟫

He says, Islam is to witness that there is no God but Allah, and Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is the Messenger of Allah;
⟪ar-quote:وَتُقِیمَ الصَّلَاةَ⟫

And that you establish the prayer
⟪ar-quote:وَتُؤْتِیَ الزَّکَاةَ⟫

that you give the alms;
⟪ar-quote:وَتَصُومَ رَمَضَانَ⟫

that you fast the month of Ramadan;
⟪ar-quote:وَتَحُجَّ الْبَیْتَ إِنْ اسْتَطَعْتَ إِلَیْهِ سَبِیلًا⟫

and you perform pilgrimage to the House if you are capable of travel.

Now what's so interesting about this HADEES, is that rather than giving a definition of ISLAM, Rasul Allah(S) describes it as a set of practices. He says, the first is to SHAHDAH; the second is prayer; third is zakaat; fourth is fasting and fifth is HAJJ. The question is, why describe ISLAM as a practice instead of an experience? Because religion as a human phenomenon, has to be more related to experience in its initial stages, than to anything intellectual. Religion is not initially housed within an *intellectual* frame of reference; it is housed within an experiential one. But these five practices are not where ISLAM begins; but rather where it ends. ISLAM begins with an experience, and culminates in practice.

So the first question is, how can we understand ISLAM within the framework of experience? Because as far as our prophet (S) is concerned, ISLAM began with a direct experience of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). That does not negate the medium of the angel JIBRAEEL (A). By direct experience what I mean, is that for him, ISLAM was not a rational, or a congnitive, or an intellectual process. To him it was a direct experience of the noumenal realm!

Phenomena are what we call appearances, or the "seen" world which constitute our experiences; noumena are the presumed "unseen" things, that constitute the metaphysical realities, such as god, afterlife etc.

So before we can understand what the experience of ISLAM means for us; we must first understand Rasul Allah(S)'s phenomenal experience of the noumenal realm; which he describes as seeing the horizons filled with the presence of JIBRAEEL (AS). In other words, if all of us stepped outside right now and if we could see from one horizon to the other, and as far up in the sky, as we could see; if we all saw JIBRAEEL (AS) standing right in front of us, how would that affect our practice as Muslims? See, when I tell you that the Prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) saw the entire horizon, this celestial sphere, fill up with an angelic being, that is simply information to you. But it was not information to him. For him it was an incredible experience! And the interesting thing about experience is that it is not a logical proposition. You cannot prove or disprove experience! You can discuss it; you can interpret it; but you cannot say it is true or false. Experience is always "real" for the one experiencing it. The challenge then, is to determine whether or not that experience has an objective reality or a subjective reality. In other words, is that experience a true experience, or is it something that is happening to this individual as a type of psychosis. Because we do have a lot of people in the psychic wards speaking to god directly. They will tell you that they speak to god, and they can hear god speaking to them. And these people are not lying, because even though they are in delusional states, they actually believe what they're experiencing. Their delusions are very real to them.

So lets begin by understanding how Rasul Allah(S) experienced ISLAM. In fact he had two divine experiences in his life. The first was in the cave of HIRA, and the second was the night of the ISRA or MERAAJ

The first experience of IQRA

As for the first experience, it is narrated that Rasul Allah(S) used to practice TAHANNUS (⟪ar:تَحَنُّث⟫), which was a type of devotional practice. HINS in Arabic means shirk! In Surah WAQIAH, Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) says:
⟪ar-quote:وَكَانُوا۟ يُصِرُّونَ عَلَى ٱلْحِنثِ ٱلْعَظِيمِ⟫

and they insist on a great SHIRK. So the word "HINS" means SHIRK. TAHANNUS is from the ⟪ar:باب التَّفَاعَل⟫, and its purpose in morphology is to avoid something. So if HINS means SHIRK, TAHANNUS means the avoidance of SHIRK.
- JANB means "side or nearness", so ⟪ar:تَجَنُّب⟫means to avoid nearness to somebody.
- JAHAL means "ignorance", so ⟪ar:تَجَاھُل⟫means "to pretend to be ignorant"
- HUJOOD means to sleep, so ⟪ar:تَحَجُّد⟫means to avoid sleep.

These are all words on the same pattern in morphology.

And so Rasul Allah at this early stage of his life, would go to this cave called HIRA at night, to perform ⟪ar:تَحَنُّث⟫; what we would call "meditation" today. He would go in and then get into a deep contemplative state. His desire was the attempt to empty out forms; to disconnect himself from this exterior "physical" world. He wanted to free himself from all of these "forms" of attachments or SHIRK. Because the greatest of all SHIRK, is the worship of the self. Idolatry has nothing on self-worship or egocentricity. Worship of the self is the most destructive thing there is for the soul. In the Quran, Allah talks about people who worship their desires and passions.
⟪ar-quote:أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ⟫

he took his desires as his God

And so Rasul Allah(S) as a practice, would go to this cave, in order to reflect on himself and empty his heart out of these attachments. Because this emptying of the self is important, in order to prepare oneself for the journey towards Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). For any journey, you have to pack provisions before you set out; and in order to pack provisions, you need empty space in the bag; and so emptying out, is really the preparation for this divine joureny. The soul has to be emptied of all forms, before it can gain knowledge of the one who has no form; because forms impinge on that understanding.

So one night he was at this cave, and Jibraeel (AS) comes to him and says, "Muhammad, I am Jibraeel and you are the messenger of Allah!". He raises his head to see who was speaking, and he sees JIBRAEEL (AS) in the form of a man filling up the horizon. Rasul Allah(S) naturally gets scared, and turns his face away from him; but no matter where he turns, he sees JIBRAEEL (AS) in the exact same form. JIBRAEEL then says to him, "Recite" (⟪ar:أقرأ⟫); and Rasul Allah(S) replies, "⟪ar:ما أنا بقاری؟⟫"(What should I recite?). At that point JIBRAEEL (AS) wraps his wings around him and squeezes him three times; and according to Rasul Allah(S) himself, the squeeze was so hard, that he felt stifled to the point where he thought he would die.

Scholars say, that the squeezing was a physical manifestation of a spiritual reality; which was removing any and all remanant of his soul from this world. He had to be emptied out, because he was later going to be filled with three divine vessels. He was going to be filled with ISLAM, IMAN and IHSAN. And so there had to be a complete emptying out, before the filling could take place. And this is what the companions used to say about the Prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), that he would empty us out of ignorance (of JAHILIYYAH), and then fill us up with ISLAM. And so even for Rasul Allah(S), ISLAM was actually a complete emptying, before it was a filling; and this in Arabic is called TAKHLIYAH. The Arabs say:
⟪ar-quote:التَّخلِیَّۃُ تَسبِق التَّحلِیَّۃ⟫

The emptying out must preceed the ornaments. In other words you have to be stripped of what is ugly, before you can be ornamented with the beautiful.

---

ng out must preceed the ornaments. In other words you have to be stripped of what is ugly, before you can be ornamented with the beautiful.

And then Jibraeel (AS) said to him:

ٱقْرَأْ بِٱسْمِ رَبِّكَ ٱلَّذِى خَلَقَ ‎

Read in the name of your Lord who created -

‏خَلَقَ ٱلْإِنسَنَ مِنْ عَلَقٍ ‎

Created man from a clinging substance.

‏ٱقْرَأْ وَرَبُّكَ ٱلْأَكْرَمُ ‎

Recite, and your Lord is the most Generous -

‏ٱلَّذِى عَلَّمَ بِٱلْقَلَمِ ‎

Who taught by the pen

‏عَلَّمَ ٱلْإِنسَنَ مَا لَمْ يَعْلَمْ

Taught man that which he knew not.

https://ismailignosis.com/2014/07/03/iqra-muhammad-meditated-upon-the-name-of-god-as-the-quran-was-revealed/#more-1116

---

And so this is at the essence of our religious experience. It is this conscious attempt of TAHANNUS; of being emptied out of evil; of the desires of this world; of the passions of this physical realm; and only then can we begin to get a sense of the noumenal realm.

### Divine vs Demonic Experience

Now here is something I find very fascinating. How do you differentiate between a true divine experience, and a demonic experience?

A demonic experience, is always accompanied with an expansion of the self. In other words it is a very exciting and joyful experience, but then it is always followed with despair. On the contrary, a true spiritual experience is exactly the opposite. The initial experience is incredible constriction and fear and dread; but then it is followed by a sense of expansion and joy.

Now in this experience of our Prophet, and the experience of all prophets before him, we find the same reaction to revelation. The Quran tells us that the first divine words for MOOSA (AS) were:
⟪ar:لا تخاف⟫..... Allah said to him, Don't be afraid! Because his first experience of Allah was filled with fear. IBRAHEEM (AS) also had the same experience. And so this is something we find consistent in the Quran, and in also what the Jews and Christians believe in their traditions; that this religious experience is overwhelming. It incapacitates the self.

So when Rasul Allah(S) received the first revelation of IQRA, it was a very painful process for him. Because JIBRAEEL (AS) did not feed him the words that he later on blindly repeated to the QURAISH. What was being delivered to him, were the meanings; and these meanings were being directly breathed into him. The Arabic word for "breath" and "spirit" are the same: ROOH. So the idea of the "spirit" being "breathed" into us is actually built into the language. So when this WAHEE (these meanings) were being breathed into him, it was a very painful experience. Imagine being given mouth-to-mouth resuscitation by a giant. What do you imagine that would feel like? It would feel like every cell of your body is taken over by the immense pressure of that air, accompanied by this feeling of complete helplessness. So even as it gives you life, it feels like its squashing the life out of you, suffocating you under its enormous weight, until it feels useless to even attempt to fight against it. This is why according to narrations, in the early period of Islam, he would start convulsing when he would get WAHEE; because it was a very painful experience for him. And the disbelievers would use that as an excuse to say that he has been posessed by a jinn. And in his words he described the process "as though it was being engraved in my heart". Imagine the agonizing pain of a sharp blade carving deep inside your heart, as you lie helplessly beneath it. You are completely conscious of the pain, but unable to struggle against it. That is how difficult this process was for him initially. Later on it got much easier, to the point where people wouldn't even know when revelation came upon him.

And so after the prophet had this very first angelic experience, he went into a state of extreme shock. Lezley Hazelton wrote a book called "The First Muslim", in which she beautifully portrays his emotions after this first encounter with JIBRAEEL (AS). She writes, "He did not come floating off the mountain as though he was walking on air. He did not run down shouting, 'Hallelujah" and "Bless the Lord! I am your new prophet" He did not radiate light and joy. There were no choirs (quire) of angels, no music from the heavens. No elation, no ecstasy, no golden aura surrounding him. He did nothing that might seem as the natural reaction of a man who just crossed the border between this world and the spiritual world. On the contrary: he was convinced that what he had encountered could not be real. He thought it was a hallucination; or a trick of the senses; he thought he had been posessed by an evil jinn. So the man who fled down the mountain of Hira, trembled not with joy, but with a stark primordial fear. He was overwhelmed, but not with conviction! He was overwhelmed by doubt."

*And if you think about it, this is exactly our initial encounter with Islam; a feeling of constriction; a feeling of doubt. Is this all real? Is there really a god? Is there an afterlife? Is there a  heaven and a hell? and its followed by the discomfort of practice. Every Islamic practice is an uncomfortable process.*

So scholars say that whatever happened up there on Mount Hira, just the sheer humanness of Rasul Allah(S) reaction, is the strongest argument for its historical reality. Whether you believe that the words he heard, came from inside himself or from outside, it is clear that he experienced them, and with a force that shattered his sense of himself and his world. Now what makes this so interesting, is that we know about the vastness of his soul. Because as scholars explain, the soul of the prophet is greater than this cosmos! So we understand that the mag-nanimity of his soul is beyond our comprehension. But what's amazing is that even though he was going through this incredible shock, his mind was completely focused and present!

Normally when people go into shock they lose their ability to think, but with the Messenger of Allah(S), it was qutie the opposite. He was able to maintain his focus and presence of mind. And the proof of that consciouslness is in what he said to his wife Hazrat Khadeeja (AS) when he returned home. He said: ZAMMILOONEE ZAMMILOONEE, which means means, "Wrap me up". Now we know that patients who experience shock, one of the first things you do, is wrap them up. You're actually told to wrap them up, to create some sort of containment. Because part of the shock, is a loss of self. It is when the outward and the inward crash. There is just a massive crash that occurs, and so the experience of the psychic integrity of the self being whole, is completely shattered, because something has forced itself in on the soul. And the prophet realized this, and so he asked his wife to wrap him up. So this feeling of intense constriction that he experienced, and his response to that experience, in terms of his perfect consciousness, is the first proof of that experience being a divine spiritual experience, and not a demonic one.

The Second Experience of ISRA
https://essentialismaili.com/2016/05/03/miraj-spiritual-ascension-of-prophet-muhammad-in-ismaili-thought-ismaili-gnosis/

His second divine experience, was that of ISRAA or the MERAAJ. It was a migration in which he was taken by the night. ISRA is a the night journey; whereas MERAJ is the actual ascension to the heavens. The word ⟪ar:سَارَا⟫in Arabic, means to travel in the night; and ⟪ar:أَسری⟫is used  when someone takes you by night. Allah says in the Quran:
⟪ar-quote:سُبْحَنَ ٱلَّذِىٓ أَسْرَىٰ بِعَبْدِهِۦ لَيْلًۭا مِّنَ ٱلْمَسْجِدِ ٱلْحَرَامِ إِلَى ٱلْمَسْجِدِ ٱلْأَقْصَا⟫

Glorified  is the one who took his slave by night, from the sanctuary in Mecca to the sanctuary in AQSA.

One of the benefits of using the word, "night" in that verse is that for the Arabs it took them about 40 nights to make that Journey from Mecca to Jerusalem. So the verse is reemphasizing that this journey took place in one night. In some of the narrations, it is said that his bed was still warm when he returned. So it was obviously a metaphysical Journey, and it was not in the time-space continuum that we are in. In modern physics today there are things like wormholes, where you can be in one part of the universe and then you go through this wormhole and you're instantly transported to another part of the universe. These ideas at that time were  unthinkable.

Now interestingly this migration had two aspects. The first was a physical aspect, because a steed named BURAAQ was brought for the prophet. BURAAQ is descibed as a steed, that was smaller than a horse but bigger than a mule. BURAAQ comes from the word BARQ which means lightning; it also means BARAAQA meaning illuminous. So this was a luminous steed that moved at the speed of light. Because it went from one horizon to the other in one step. So even though it was a physical journey from Mecca to Jerusalem, it took place almost instantaneously. It was at the fastest speed that is physically possible.

But then, once he reaches AQSA, the actual ascension, which is MERAAJ takes place. And this journey was beyond the speed of light; it was beyond time and space. It's speed cannot be measured or quantified in any physical sense. The word MERAJ means “ an instrument of ascension,” like a “ladder” or a “stairway.  (⟪ar:عرج⟫means a ladder). So the first journey (ISRAA) was at the speed of light; and the second one (MERAJ) was beyond the speed of light, where he had a witnessing of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala)
⟪ar-quote:ثم دنی فتدلی فکان قاب قوسین او ادنی⟫

He became close to God, until he was at a distance of two bows length, which is a metaphor. Because in the Arabian tradition when you came in the presence of a king,  you could not come closer than to bows length. That was the closest you were allowed to get to the king. And so that was an honorific expression of how close the prophet got to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala); as close as you can get to a king without breaching the ADAB.  Because ⟪ar:دنی⟫is ⟪ar:مقام لا مکان⟫ , it is a closeness of station, not of place. Because there is no physicality there. You don't go into the physical presence of Allah, because he does not have physicality. 

*And there are incredible haqaiq behind all these symbolic terms: BURAAQ, ISRA, MERAAJ, 2 bows etc. So there are a lot of codes to decipher here.*

Now this experience of ascension that the Messenger of Allah(S) had; if you look at the Quranic description, it says..... 
⟪ar-quote:مَا زَاغَ ٱلْبَصَرُ وَمَا طَغَىٰ ‎⟫

His vision did not deviate, nor did it rebel against him. Now we need to understand this in the context of what was happening to him. And what was happening to him, was that he was moving through the seven heavens, which means that he was being given the unveiling of the unseen world. The unseen world was literally being unveiled for him. Now, if we had that same experience of unveiling right now; if Allah removed this veil from us; the vast majority of us would go into a state of insanity! quite literally!Because we would not be able to handle it.

We know now in our material sciences, that we are seeing less than a billionth of the material stimuli at any given moment. In other words, when you and I look out into the room we're sitting in right now, we are seeing less than a billionth of what is materially there, to stimulate our senses. Visible light is a very small spectrum on the electromagnetic spectrum; and that is all that we see. Now this is the material world! This is what we have identified, and what is called the SHAAHID (what we can witness). We do not have access to the GHAYB (to the unseen realm). We also know now, that the majority of the universe is dark matter. In other words 95% of the physical universe is not even perceived by us. When these scientists started looking outside and all they saw was stars everywhere, they asked this question, that why isn't the night sky as bright as the day sky. Because if light travels, and all of these lights are out there, if all the heavens are filled with orbs of light, then why aren't they filling up the night sky the same way? Because we only see about three thousand stars on a really clear moonless night. And what they found out is that only the light from some stars are penetrating through. It's literally a visitation, which is very interesting because the Quran says..... 

⟪ar-quote:وَٱلسَّمَآءِ وَٱلطَّارِقِ ..... وَمَآ أَدْرَىٰكَ مَا ٱلطَّارِقُ..... ٱلنَّجْمُ ٱلثَّاقِبُ⟫

The night and the night visitor. And the star is a night visitor, which indicates that the light of the star is moving! It's a journey; and when it gets here, it is quite literally like a night visitor. So the Quran describes stars as night visitors, and then it says: what will convey to you what this night visitor is? It is NAJUMUs SAAQIB (The piercing star). Now SUQUB in Arabic, is to put a whole through a pearl. And so the light of the stars that are actually reaching us is exactly like that. It is literally penetrating and making a hole in this entire celestial pearl. So what we know about this "seen" world is incredibly small, and yet the "unseen" world we have absolutely no knowledge of.

But Allah says in the Quran
⟪ar-quote:مَا زَاغَ ٱلْبَصَرُ وَمَا طَغَىٰ ‎⟫

"his vision did not deviate, nor did it rebel against him". My question is, that if you were traveling through the unseen realm, and all of this unveiling was occurring; and you were witnessing all of this extraordinary unveiling, why would you not be distracted? And this again goes back to the heart of the Prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) who had only one concern that night, which was to visit his master. He was on the journey to Allah; and he was not interested in the particulars. Because if you know Allah, you know everything!
⟪ar-quote:کلُّ ما تَھوَاہُ مَوجُودٌ فِی ذَاتِ اللہ⟫

Everything that you can ever desire exists in Allah. So if you have Allah, you have your heart's desire; and everything else that human beings are running around looking out for, is ultimately the same thing. They are looking for their hearts desire.

One of the seven deadly sins in Christianity is sloth! And most people think of it as laziness. But in Christian tradition, sloth or spiritual lassitude (lasə-tude), is that you did not take your salvation seriously. That you literally squandered your time on earth, and did not take your life seriously. And that is why the vast majority of us are in a slothful state, even if we are spending most of our time working. If we are not thinking deeply about where we're going? what we're doing? what's going to happen? then we are in a slothful state. We are spiritually lazy. And lazy people are not only uninspirED people; they are also uninspiring people; and they are held in contempt, even by other lazy people.

So this second divine experience of ISRAA and MERAAJ, was an extraordinary experience for the prophet. Because it was direct witnessing of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). So now when he returns from that divine experience, he is now ready to move on to the next phase, which is to be in this world, free of all attachments. Because the world is no longer a threat to him as a distraction. He now sees reality as it is! And this is what he always prayed to Allah for, "Show me things as they truly are!". So he was given this extraordinary gift of knowledge to see things as they truly are. And when he returns back to the world, he is now able to live in this world in a way in which the world is no longer going to be, not only a distraction to him between him and his Lord, but also that he will never miss-perceive the world. This is called "right understanding". And this is also in all of the world's religion.  There is an understanding or a first principle, that everything begins with right understanding. That we must perceive the world correctly. Because our lack of perception, or misperception of this world, is what causes us pain. This is the concept that is very dominant in the Buddhist tradition. This idea, that your suffering comes from a lack of understanding of the nature of the world. Because suffering is always related to desire, what we call, or what the Quran calls BAGHEE. And what's fascinating to me is that the word BAGHEE means desire, but it also means oppression. The word for "desire" and the word for "oppression" are both the same word in Arabic. Because desires oppress! So the freedom from desires ⟪ar:بُغیَۃ⟫..... is when you make your desire, the "right" desire.

So the first divine experience that Rasul Allah(S) has of his master, is through the veil of JIBRAEEL (AS). But the second experience is a "direct" witnessing of his master wihtout any veils. And this is where he receives this gift of immense expansion in his soul, where now nothing in the world, no trial, no tribulation, no calamity could distract him from his master. He reached the pinnacle of his Islam.

---

But Islam did not begin that way, did it? It did not begin with a "direct" experience; it began with an "intermediary" one, which was Jibraeel AS. And it began with the extreme constriction of the heart, with fear, and the physical pain of absorbing revelation. And then it was followed by 13 years of persecution, trials and hardships, and only then the unveiling of the unseen realm occured. And the reason I wanted to share this experience with you, is because his experience sets up an archetype for all Muslims! Because that is the experience of entering ISLAM for every muslim. Rasul Allah(S) took a journey which everybody has to take. Every one of us is on a journey to our master. Now you and I, can either do it willingly or we do it unwillingly; but either way we're all headed towards our master. And these experiences set the stage for our journey.

This journey begins with TAKHLIYA, an emptying out; it begins with TAHANNUS, to identify and then eradicate those elements that distract us from Allah. And the very first of that is "desire"
⟪ar-quote:أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ⟫

Do you not see the one who takes his desires as his God.

This is how ISLAM began for Rasul Allah(S) and this is how it must begin for us. With a deep reflection of the self. What am I attached to? What do I desire? I know people who literally update their whatsapp and facebook profile every single day. And it's an indication of a deep rooted sickness in the heart. Because it is practically idolizing oneself - Worship me! Worship my beauty! And then the same is true for the mentality of "Look at my house! Look at tmy car! Look at my status! Look at my power!" These are all idols of the self.

And so all of us need to reflect on our lives, look into our souls and identify the various idols that we have created, and set on the KA'ABA of our hearts? And then, one by one, to start breaking them with the sword of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLH (I have no desire except the desire for Allah). We need to make space, before Allah can enter our hearts.

And then just like Rasul Allah(S) we have to migrate. The word for migration in Arabic, is "HIJRA". There are two HIJRAS of Rasul Allah(S). The first was a physical HIJRA from Mecca to Medina; and the second was the spiritual HIJRA from this phenomenal realm to the neuomenal realm. So HIJRA has both, a physical as well as spiritual aspect. The Prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said, that the true MUHAAJIR, is the one who migrates away from what Allah has prohibited him. And what Allah has prohibited us from, is everything other than himself. LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH!

And traveling either brings out the best in people, or it brings out the worst in people, which is why the Arabs call it SAFAR, which means to expose. ⟪ar:یُسفِرُ عَنِ المرأِ⟫. Same word is used for an ambassador SAFEER; because an ambassador is someone who exposes the intentions of its government to whoever he is sent to. So SAFAR is a type of revelation for the self and others.

And then to get ready for the discomforts of the practices of Islam. Because the beginning of every spiritual experience is constriction. Entering Islam is an experience of contraction, where the world and the desires of the world have to be literally squeezed out. We are are surrounded by prohibitions no matter where we go, or what we do. We then physically suffer the obligations of the DAYAM. SALAAT, ZAKAAT, FASTING, HAJJ, these are not easy tasks. Even the Quran says these are extremely difficult tasks
⟪ar-quote:وَٱسْتَعِينُوا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ وَٱلصَّلَوٰةِ.....  وَإِنَّهَا لَكَبِيرَةٌ إِلَّا عَلَى ٱلْخَشِعِينَ ‎⟫

And seek help through patience and prayer, and indeed it is extremely difficult, except for the humbly calm

Practicing Islam is not easy. Being a muslim; being labelled as terrorists, and being constantly ridiculed is not easy. But we cannot lose our focus! We cannot be distracted in our journey just as Rasul Allah(S) constantly maintained his focus.
⟪ar-quote:مَا زَاغَ ٱلْبَصَرُ وَمَا طَغَىٰ ‎⟫

His vision did not deviate, nor did it rebel against him. We have to constantly remember that we are on a journey to Allah, and the sincerity of our SHADAH (LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH - there is not god but Allah) will be tested every step of the way. You say you don't want anything but Allah! Now show me! I am standing on the other side of this path - come to me! The world will distract you! its pleasures will entice you! your desires will consume you; friends will abandon you! people will ridicule you; make fun of you for being a Muslim! Calamities will befall you! You will suffer loss and pain! What will you do? Will you still say, I have no god but Allah and keep walking towards me? or will you forget about me, get distracted and stray off the path? Who will you choose in the end?

This is the true experience of ISLAM! But the most incredible thing about this journey is that its constriction, *always* ends with an enormous expansion of the soul; which is that final moment of the beatific witnessing of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) himself, when he will say to us:

⟪ar-quote:يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ⟫

"O content soul,
⟪ar-quote:ٱرْجِعِىٓ إِلَىٰ رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةًۭ مَّرْضِيَّةًۭ⟫

 Return to your Lord, in a state where you are well-pleased with him and he is well pleased with you
⟪ar-quote:فَٱدْخُلِى فِى عِبَدِى⟫

 And enter among My [righteous] servants
⟪ar-quote:وَٱدْخُلِى جَنَّتِى⟫

 And enter My Paradise."

This is the true experince of Islam which I wanted to share with you, before we talk about the practices of Islam. Because if ISLAM is not an experience for us, the practices become lifeless.

There is a lot to be understood here

doesn't mean you cannot enjoy life - just dont get distracted

---

One of the benefits of using the word, "night" in that verse is that for the Arabs, it took them about 40 nights to make that journey from Mecca to Jerusalem. So the verse is reemphasizing that this journey took place in one night. In some of the narrations, it is said that his bed was still warm when he returned. So it was obviously a metaphysical Journey, and it was not in the time-space continuum that we are in. In modern physics today there are things like wormholes, where you can be in one part of the universe, and then you go through this wormhole and you're instantly transported to another part of the universe. These ideas at that time were  unthinkable.

We know now in our material sciences, that we are seeing less than a billionth of the material stimuli at any given moment. In other words, when you and I look out into the room we're sitting in right now, we are seeing less than a billionth of what is materially there, to stimulate our senses. Visible light is a very small spectrum on the electromagnetic spectrum; and that is all that we see. Now this is the material world! This is what we have identified, and what is called the SHAAHID (what we can witness). We still do not have any access to the GHAYB (to the unseen realm). And we also know now, that the majority of the universe is dark matter. In other words 95% of the physical universe is not even perceived by us.

When these scientists started looking outside and all they saw was stars everywhere, they asked this question, that why isn't the night sky as bright as the day sky. Because if light travels, and all of these lights are out there; if all the heavens are filled with these orbs of light, then why aren't they filling up the night sky the same way? Because we only see about three thousand stars on a really clear moonless night. And what they found out is that only the light from some stars are penetrating through. It's literally a visitation, which is very interesting because the Quran says.....

وَٱلسَّمَآءِ وَٱلطَّارِقِ

The night and the night visitor. And the star is a night visitor, which indicates that the light of the star is moving! It's a journey; and when it gets here, it is quite literally like a night visitor. So the Quran describes stars as night visitors, and then it says:

وَمَآ أَدْرَىٰكَ مَا ٱلطَّارِقُ

and what will convey to you what this night visitor is?

ٱلنَّجْمُ ٱلثَّاقِبُ

It is NAJUMUs SAAQIB (The piercing star). Now SUQUB in Arabic, is to put a whole through a pearl. And so the light of the stars that are actually reaching us is exactly like that. It is literally penetrating and making a hole in this entire celestial pearl. So what we know about this "seen" world is incredibly small, and yet the "unseen" world we have absolutely no knowledge of.

And SAQEEFA is the experience that immediately precedes the ISRAA, which is the lowest point of the prophets life on earth. He once said to Ayesha, that the worst time I had was at the hands of your people at SAQEEF. That was the worst experience that he ever had. A total state of humiliation! Children threw rocks at him (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) as he ran away from them in the streets. And his shoes were filled with blood; and then he was offered this opportunity of revenge, which he did not take. And his reason was that they were children. So through that event, he expressed not only his ultimate humanity, but also his extraordinary magnanimity in a moment, when most people would have certainly wanted revenge. But he chose the higher ground. But then right after that low point comes the divine unveiling and the immense expansion in his soul.

<!-- section 2 (id=5769, raw_sort=2): Linguistic Meaning of ISLAM -->

## The Linguistic Meaning of Islām

In the previous session we looked at the kind of experience ISLAM was for Rasul Allah(S). Because fundamentally, ISLAM is an experience. It is an experience that is created through practice. Think about your last "great" experience! And then think about the work and the effort that went into creating that experience. Just for something as simple as taking the kids to the park. We have to make all sorts of arrangements; get everyone ready, pack lunch, drive to the place, physically play with the kids. There is a lot of physical work involved in the process, before we experience what we call "fun" or a "good time". And this is why, even though ISLAM, is essentially the "experience" of witnessing the divine, Rasul Allah(S)'s defined it as a set of physical practices. Because experience can only be created through practice and work. Experience is what you take away from the practice.

And the first practice of ISLAM, that we learn from the life of Rasul Allah(S), is a deep reflection on the self; TAHANNUS! Which is the removal of SHIRK through ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ (There is no god except Allah). One of the meanings of ILAH, is the one that is worshipped and obeyed. Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ⟫

Have you seen the one who takes his desires as his god? In other words, have you seen the one who worships and obeys his "desires and passions" instead of worshipping and obeying me? Because that changes the SHAHADAH from ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫  to ⟪ar:لا الہ الا ھوی⟫ ; I have no god but my desire. So the first act is that of TAHANNUS; to identify each and every idol that we've placed in our hearts; the idol of greed; the idol of lust; the idol of self-praise; the idol of money; the idol of the desire for power; and then to one by one, break them with the sword of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫, until the heart is empty - TAKHLIYA. "Vacate" in English means to empty out; that where vacation comes from. So TAKHLIYA is to rid the self of everything that Allah has prohibited us from; and what Allah has prohibited us from, is everything other than himself. So TAHANNUS is identification and TAKHLIYA is emptying out. And the entire purpose of this emptying out is to make room for the divine experience. When someone comes to visit us, even for a couple of day, we go through all sorts of cleaning and cleansing processes. We make all sorts of arrangements to make sure they feel welcome. So then what kind of arrangements should be made for the king of all kings? What kind of purity would you imagine will be required for the love of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) to enter our hearts?

---

Today I want to look at some of the linguistic and conceptual meanings of the word ISLAM

Islam as submission and surrender of free will

The first meaning of the word ISLAM that we'll look at, is submission. The word ⟪ar:أَسلَمَ⟫means "to submit" or "to surrender". Allah calls his religion⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫. The word DEEN in the Arabic language comes from the root letters DA-YAA-NAA.....  ⟪ar:دَیْن⟫, which has several meanings. The first meaning is a rain that falls over and over again bringing the dead earth back to life. Another meaning is to discipline something..... ⟪ar:من دان نفسہ⟫,  whoever disciplines his soul. It also means, a way of life.....⟪ar:لکم دینکم ولیدین⟫..... You have your way of life and we have ours.

But the root meaning ⟪ar:دَیْن⟫, from which all these other means are derived, actually means a "debt". And all its derivites trace their meaning from this original meaning of debt. So why does the rain keep coming back to the earth to bring it back to life, because that is what it owes the earth. The rain is fulfilling its debt to the earth. We owe it to our souls that we discipline it. The true "way of life" is to repay your debts. So all the various derivatives of this word are based on the meaning of ⟪ar:دَیْن⟫, which means debt.

So ⟪ar:دینُ الاسلام⟫ can literally be translated as the "Debt of Islam". In other words, the idea is, that we have been endowed with innumerable blessings by our creator; and for that we owe him a debt of praise and gratitude. We owe him a debt of HAMD, which can only be achieved through submission. Allah asks in the Quran:
**(http://quran.com/3/83)**
⟪ar-quote:أَفَغَيْرَ دِينِ ٱللَّهِ يَبْغُونَ⟫

Do they seek other than the DEEN of Allah?..... 
⟪ar-quote:وَلَهُۥٓ أَسْلَمَ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ طَوْعًۭا وَكَرْهًۭا⟫

While all creatures in the heaven and the earth have bowed down to him in submission, willingly or unwillingly. So what Allah is asking is, do these human beings seek other than repaying their debt? When in reality everything in existence is paying its debt of submission to its creator. Because everything else is in a state of submission, willingly or unwillingly.

Now there are certain areas of submission that we all as human being recognize; even the athiest. We have certain limitations that we cannot exceed. For instance we need to eat. When we get hungry we "must" eat or we die. We "have" to drink when we are thirsty, or we will die. We "have" to relieve ourselves once we have eaten, or taken drink. We don't have a choice! We "have" to sleep or we can literally go crazy from lack of sleep. We can only study so much before our minds cannot take anymore. So there is this idea of willing or unwilling submission to our nature itself.

And then there is also submission to our own physical being. We can only eat so much; we can only drink so much; we can only walk so much; do so much physically before we exhaust ourselves. We can only lift so much weight. We have limitations in our movements because of the way in which our bodies are structured. So we all as human beings agree that we must submit to certain limitations willingly or unwillingly, given that we are temporal creatures limited by the physical aspects of our nature.

In other words we have limits and boundaries that we must submit to; willingly or unwillingly. And the Arabic word for a boundary, or limit, is HADD. So all of creation has HUDOOD; we are all confined within our limits. Water cannot flow upwards; a rock cannot fly; a bird cannot bark; a dog cannot sing; honey will always taste sweet; citrus will always taste sour. So in the Quran there is this idea that everything is in submission to its limitations, its boundaries, it's HUDOOD; willingly or unwillingly.

---

Now when this applies to human beings, there is a slight nuance in its meaning. For us as human beings, in addition "to submit", the word ASLAMA, also means "to surrender". To surrender one's free will, to the will of the creator. The question is, surrender to what extent? Because there are degrees of surrender, right? So to what degree, must we must surrender our free will? The answer to that questions, has also been placed within our own existence; in the way the body submits to the soul. When the soul commands, the body surrenders itself instantly. If I choose to put my hand in the fire, the hand will not refuse, knowing very well that it *will* get burnt. But without a seconds delay, it will obey; it will surrender itself to my command.

Now surrender can be a very negative thing; because people can be forced into submission; and that kind of submission is degrading, it is hateful. But the surrender of ISLAM, is different in that it is a "willing" surrender; it is a "voluntary" submission, which is a very noble and dignified form of submission. Because there is absolutely no compulsion in DEEN..... ⟪ar:لا اکراہ فی الدین⟫..... Again the same word DEEN is used. In other words there is no compulsion in the payment of this debt. Allah is not going to force you to do it. You must do it out of your own free will; out of love; like a lover who submits his will to desires of his beloved. Like that poet, who came to this woman، and told her that his friend was madly in love with her. She asked the man, "Tell me about the love of your friend, and don't detract and don't embellish; just give me the straight truth". So the poet said.....

⟪ar-quote:اِن کَانَ یَظُنُّ الموتُ بِالظَّمَاءِ..... وَ قَالِ لَك لا تَشرِبُ المآءَ ..... وَلَم یَرِدِ⟫

If he was dying from thirst, and you said to him to not drink water, he wouldn't. This is true love according to the Islamic tradition; the complete surrender of ones will to the will of the beloved. It's not what Bollywood teaches us; to chase a girl around a tree singing a song.

So another nuance of the word ISLAM, is that it is not about forcing someone to submit. Allah says:

**(http://quran.com/10/99)**

⟪ar-quote:وَلَوْ شَآءَ رَبُّكَ!.....  لَآمَنَ مَن فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ كُلُّهُمْ جَمِيعًا⟫

And had your master willed, the entire creation on earth would have believed

⟪ar-quote:أَفَأَنتَ تُكْرِهُ ٱلنَّاسَ حَتَّىٰ يَكُونُوا۟ مُؤْمِنِينَ⟫⟪ar-quote:؟⟫

Then, [O Muhammad], would you compel the people in order that they become believers?

So what Allah is saying, is that I am their master; I am their creator; I am the one with ABSOLUTE power! And if *I* am not compelling them into submission; if *I* am not forcing them to believe, then neither should you. So what we're learning is that ISLAM, is a religion of wilful submission; it is a religion of honor and dignity; it is a religion motivated by love and freedom; and not by force and compulsion.

Now the next question is why? Why should we surrender, or submit our free will? The idea behind this willing surrender, is in the realization and the recognition of the fact, that we desire to place our lives into the capable hands of the Rehman and the Raheem; the intensely merciful and the constantly merciful. And this is where the knowledge of TAWHEED of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) comes into play. The more we "know" him, the more we will "love" him; and the more we will "want" to praise him; and the more we will "want" to be grateful to him; and as a result of all of that, we will "want" to surrender to him out of our own free will

⟪ar-quote:يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ أَنْتُمُ الْفُقَرَاءُ إِلَى اللَّهِ وَاللَّهُ هُوَ الْغَنِيُّ الْحَمِيدُ⟫

Oh mankind! you are the ones who need Allah; and Allah is free of all need and is forever praised.

So what we've learnt so far about the word ISLAM, is that within our existence, Allah is showing us a number of things:

First: We are created for submission, and we are in a state of submission willingly or unwillingly

Second: The expected quality of our surrender must be, like the body surrenders itself to the soul; instantly and completely.

Third: This surrender cannot be forced. It must be out of one's own free will. It must be out of love

So now if we look at this ayah again:

⟪ar-quote:أَفَغَيْرَ دِينِ ٱللَّهِ يَبْغُونَ⟫

Do they seek other than the "willing" repayment of this debt of HAMD (of praise and gratitude) that they owe Allah?

⟪ar-quote:وَلَهُۥٓ أَسْلَمَ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ طَوْعًۭا وَكَرْهًۭا⟫

When they see that everything in the heavens and the earth submit and surrender to him, and repaying their debt, willingly or unwillingly. And then the ayah ends with a reminder, that we will return to him

⟪ar-quote:وَإِلَيْهِ يُرْجَعُونَ⟫

and to him is their return

So if you look into creation, you will see things are emerging, and then they are returning back into nonexistence. Everything that has life comes into existence, and then returns back to non-existence. The plants, the vegetables, the animal kingdom, and ultimately the mineral kingdom. Everything is going into nonexistence, after it came into existence. And that's why, another word for "death" in the Arabic language is also ASLAMA.

⟪ar-quote:أسْلَمَ نَفسُہُ⟫

He gave up the ghost; he surrendered and submitted his soul. And this again goes back to the idea of a willing or unwilling submission.

**http://quran.com/21/34-35**

⟪ar-quote:وَمَا جَعَلْنَا لِبَشَرٍۢ مِّن قَبْلِكَ ٱلْخُلْدَ.....  أَفَإِي۟ن مِّتَّ فَهُمُ ٱلْخَلِدُونَ؟⟫

And We did not grant eternity to any man before you. And if someone like you is going to die, they think they would remain forever?
⟪ar-quote:كُلُّ نَفْسٍۢ ذَآئِقَةُ ٱلْمَوْتِ.....  وَنَبْلُوكُم بِٱلشَّرِّ وَٱلْخَيْرِ فِتْنَةًۭ.....  وَإِلَيْنَا تُرْجَعُونَ⟫

Every soul will taste death. And We test you with evil and with good as trial, and to us you will be returned.

So every soul will die, and when the time comes, either the NAFS is ready and willing to submit itself to its master; or it's not ready and unwilling to submit itself; but it has to, and will submit either way. Allah says in Surah AL-WAQIAH Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:فَلَوْلَآ إِذَا بَلَغَتِ ٱلْحُلْقُومَ⟫

when the soul reaches your throat.....
⟪ar-quote:وَأَنتُمْ حِينَئِذٍۢ تَنظُرُونَ⟫

and you are watching this process happen! Make it go back! The Quran challenges, "If you are the one in control, then make it go back! Make this process stop!". And then he says
⟪ar-quote:وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنكُمْ وَلَكِن لَّا تُبْصِرُونَ ‎.....⟫

We are closer to your soul than you are, but you don't see. So the idea is, when the soul or the spirit gets to that point, there is nothing we can do. That is the moment of absolute submission. Doctors can try all they want; because we have now become very good at CPR and defibri-llation. They perform CPR, and the patient come back to life. The problem is that it works 97% of the time on television, and only 3% of the time in real life! But even then, how long can you keep doing that? Death eventually always wins! So death is the ultimate submission! Death is the ultimate ISLAM, and it is inescapable. Ready or not, here I come. So the questions then is not whether death will come or not! The questions is, when it comes, will I be ready for it or not.

So now returning back to our ayah, it is reminding, and warning all mankind, that everything else in the heavens and the earth *is* paying its debt of submission to its creator. It is doing what its supposed to do, and refraining from what it is not supposed to do, whether it wants to or not; willingly or unwillingly. Their payment is of the highest quality possible; and they're paying it right now, realizing that they will one day return to their master. All of creation understands this, *except* the human being. Because we are not being taken to account for the praise and gratitude we owe Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) right this instant. So when will we be taken to account? It is on the day when we will be confronted with the ⟪ar:مالک یوم الدین⟫ . The owner, and the king of the day, when the debt of submission falls due!

So the first meaning of the word ISLAM, is submission.

Islam as peace and safety

The next definition of the word ISLAM is that which comes from ⟪ar:سَلَمِ⟫, which means "peace" and "safety". Allah says:

(**http://quran.com/5/16**)
⟪ar-quote:يَهْدِى بِهِ ٱللَّهُ مَنِ ٱتَّبَعَ رِضْوَنَهُۥ سُبُلَ ٱلسَّلَمِ وَيُخْرِجُهُم مِّنَ ٱلظُّلُمَتِ إِلَى ٱلنُّورِ بِإِذْنِهِۦ وَيَهْدِيهِمْ إِلَىٰ صِرَطٍۢ مُّسْتَقِيمٍۢ⟫

It is by the Quran that Allah guides those who pursue His pleasure to the ways of *peace* and brings them out from darknesses into the light, by His permission, and guides them to a straight path.

So in this ayah the root word ⟪ar:سَلَمِ⟫ is used which means "peace".  Rasul Allah(S) used to recite a dua every single day 5 times a day in prayer
⟪ar-quote:اللَّهُمَّ أَنْتَ السَّلاَمُ ..... وَ مِنْكَ السَّلاَمُ ..... وَ لَكَ السَّلاَمُ ..... وَ إِلَيْكَ يَعُودُ السَّلاَمُ‏ ..... حَیِّنْ رَبِّنا بِالسَّلام⟫

Oh Allah, you are peace, and from you comes peace, and to you returns peace, enable me to live in peace.

Another derivative of the same word, is  ⟪ar:سَلَامًا⟫, which means "safety". When Ibraheem AS was being thrown into the fire, Allah said:

(**http://quran.com/21/69**)
⟪ar-quote:قُلْنَا يَا نَارُ ! كُونِي بَرْدًا وَسَلَامًا عَلَىٰ إِبْرَاهِيمَ⟫
Allah said, "O fire! become cool and safe upon Ibraheem. So here the word SALAAM is used for "safety" as well.

As Mulsims, when we greet each other we say ⟪ar:السلامُ علیک⟫ , peace and safety is with you. And that greeting is then returned by saying  ⟪ar:وعلیکَ السلام⟫ , and may peace and safety be with you as well. And when the arabs leave, they would also use the exact same words. ⟪ar:السلامُ علیک یا أخی⟫, peace and safety is with you my brother, and that was then again returned with the same words:
⟪ar:وعلیکَ السلام⟫. peace and safety be with you as well.

Now we just think of this greeting, as the Arabic version of, "YO! PEACE", or "Whad up". But to the Arabs, especially from the Islamic tradition, this SALAAM meant something very special to them. When they said ⟪ar:السلامُ علیک⟫ (peace and safety be with you), it was not a greeting; it was actually a commitment. It was a commitment that while you are with me, while you're in my presence, I guaratee, that you will not receive any harm from me; I will not harm you with my words or my actions! You will find peace in my company. But not just that, to the best of my abilities, I will not let anyone harm you! If you are attacked, I will defend you. In other words, I guarantee your safety, from myself and from others!

And then when they would separate from each other, they would also use the same words, ⟪ar:السلامُ علیک⟫ (peace and safety be with you), meaning now that I am separating from you, I will not backbite against you in anway. I will not gossip about you. I will not talk about you in anway that could cause you harm. And whatever you've said to me during our conversations, is going to be safe with me. I will not divulge your secrets to anyone. So as we depart, you can have this peace of mind from the fact that you are safe from me. And this is why when the Arabs would fight each other, they would not say ⟪ar:السلامُ علیک⟫to each other; because obviously they're here to fight.

But this is what ⟪ar:السلامُ علیک⟫ means in the Islamic tradition. Now if we measure ourselves against this criteria, we're in a lot of trouble. For us "gossip" is fiber, it is gas-relief; it cures heart burns, right?

So now if we look at ISLAM in the light of these meanings, what ISLAM means, is the willing surrdner of one's will, in the capable and trustworthy hands of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) in order to achieve peace and safety from all seen and unseen evils of this world. So by becoming MUSLIM (the one who willingly surrenders his will to the will of his creator), we can live a life of peace and safety in this world. So you can think of ISLAM like a covenant between Allah and his believer, where a Muslim surrenders his or her will to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), in return for peace or safety.

Islam as the religion of all prophets

Another way in which the word ISLAM is used in the Quran, is as a "universal" religion. Allah says in the Quran:
**(http://quran.com/2/133)**
⟪ar-quote:أَمْ كُنتُمْ شُهَدَآءَ إِذْ حَضَرَ يَعْقُوبَ ٱلْمَوْتُ إِذْ قَالَ لِبَنِيهِ مَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِنۢ بَعْدِى⟪ar-quote:؟⟫⟫

Were you witnesses when death came to Yaqoob? Behold! He said to his sons, what will you worship after me?
⟪ar-quote:قَالُوا۟ نَعْبُدُ إِلَهَكَ وَإِلَهَ آبَآئِكَ إِبْرَهِۦمَ وَإِسْمَعِيلَ وَإِسْحَقَ إِلَهًۭا وَحِدًۭا⟫

They said we shall worship your god and the god of your fathers of Ibrahim, Ismaeel and Ishaq. And then they say:
⟪ar-quote:وَنَحْنُ لَهُۥ مُسْلِمُونَ⟫

We are all on Muslims!

Now generally people believe that ISLAM is specifically the religion of Prophet Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). But what's being emphasized in this verse, is that Islam is also the religion of IBRAHEEM, ISMAEEL and ISHAQ (AS). Because what they're saying in this verse is that we will submit and surrender our will to your god, and the god of those who went before you, and we are Muslims!

So another meaning of ISLAM, is this message of universal guidance from all of the prophets. It is this concept, that ISLAM is not just the religion of prophet Muhammad (PBUH);  it is the consolidation of the teaching of all the prophets that have been sent before him.

Similarly, there is another verse
**http://quran.com/5/111**
⟪ar-quote:وَإِذْ أَوْحَيْتُ إِلَى ٱلْحَوَارِيِّۦنَ أَنْ آمِنُوا۟ بِى وَبِرَسُولِى..... قَالُوٓا۟ آمَنَّا وَٱشْهَدْ بِأَنَّنَا مُسْلِمُونَ⟫

And behold! I inspired the disciples to have faith in me and my messenger, and they said we have faith; and we bear witness that we bow to Allah as Muslims. 

Now the disciples (the HAWARIYYEEN) mentioned in this verse, are the disciples of Jesus. So here again what is being emphasized, is the idea that Jesus and his disciples were all on the path of ISLAM; and this idea, that ISLAM is an unbroken chain of guidance. ISLAM is not something new. Our prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) did not see himself as bringing a "new" religion. He really saw himself as the renewer of ancient traditions. 

Syedna Jaffar bin Mansoor AlYaman states in his book "⟪ar:کتاب العالم و الغلام⟫", that every previous religion has directed its followers to the religion that followed it. So if people acted in accordance with what was revealved in the first book, it would have lead them to the second one. And if they acted in accordance with the second, it would lead them to the third; until in the end, they would have arrived at the Quran which is the final book. All previous books were from Allah, but the latest book is more deserving of being followed than the one's that came before it; because it is more recent in time; and its message is more clear than the previous ones. And also because the Quran was sent to replace all the books that came before it, and nothing has come to replace it.

So what we're learning through these verses is that ISLAM is an unbroken chain of guidance that began with ADAM (AS), all the way up to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam); and all previous religions, including Jewdism and Christianity, are in fact subsumed within ISLAM. Now Allah confirms this fact in the Quran. He says:
⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ ٱلدِّينَ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلْإِسْلَامُ⟫

No doubt, the DEEN in the eyes of Allah; the debt of submission in the eyes of Allah has always been AL-ISLAM. He did not say
⟪ar:إِنَّ ٱلدِّينَ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ اسلامٌ،⟫that would have been grammatically correct. Instead he said  ⟪ar:إِنَّ ٱلدِّينَ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ الاسلام⟫.

In TAVEEL, it has been explained, that if you look at the word AL-ISLAM, it has 7 letters, which in fact point to the 7 major religions in ISLAM, that were brought forth by 7 high ranking messengers that are called NUTAQA. In other words, just as the word AL-ISLAM is formed through these 7 letters, the universal DEEN of Allah is composed of the teachings of these 7 messengers. The content and delivery mechanisms have changed over time, to adapt to the evolving intellect of mankind. The presentation of the message has changed with the coming of each messenger, but the fundamental principles and the essence has always remaind the same.

> — *Image text (from image 001; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/001.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

So the letter ALIF sybolizes ADAM (AS), LAAM sybolizes NOOH (AS), the next ALIF symbolizes IBRAHEEM (AS), SEEN symbolizes MOOSA (AS), LAAM sybolizes EISA (AS), ALIF symbolizes our beloved prophet MUHAMMAD (PBUH), and the last MEEM represents the one who is going to come in the future, and that is QAIM (AS).

Another way of interpreting this ayah is: ⟪ar:إِنَّ ٱلدِّينَ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ الاسلام⟫. The DEEN, the debt of submission, in the sight of Allah, is achieved through submission to these 7 religions. The debt of submission has been paid by MUSLIMS (in the universal sense) in these 7 installments.

Islam as the religion of prophet Muhammad

The final meaning of ISLAM, as it applies to us today, is that this is specifically the religion of Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ). Allah says in the Quran

Just as the word AL-ISLAM is completed and perfected by the last letter MEEM, similarly the religion of all previous prophets was perfected by the final Messenger of Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). Allah says in the Quran in Surah ⟪ar:مائدۃ⟫

> — *Image text (from image 002; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/002.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Today I have *perfected* your DEEN for you, and *completed* my blessings on you; and I have approved Islam as the religion for you.

Again the word AL-ISLAM has been used in this ayah. And in TAVEEL it has been explained, what this means is that, just as the word AL-ISLAM begins with the letter ALIF and is completed and perfected by the letter MEEM, the DEEN of Allah that began with the ALIF of ADAM AS, has now been perfected and completed with the MEEM of Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam).

Now connected to this, what's so incredible, is that Quran talks about the 7 stages of the Human Embryonic Development. In Taveel, it is explained that each stage represents one of the 7 messengers.

**http://quran.com/23/12-14**)

So ⟪ar:سلالۃ⟫is Adam (AS); ⟪ar:نطفۃ⟫ is Nooh (AS); ⟪ar:علقۃ⟫is Ibraheem (AS); ⟪ar:مضغۃ⟫is Moosa (AS); ⟪ar:عظام⟫is Eisa (AS); ⟪ar:لحم⟫is Muhammad (AS) and ⟪ar:خلقاً آخر⟫ is Qaim (AS)

Now what's fascinating is that the religion of EISA (AS), is symbolized by bones, and Rasul Allah(SAWAS) is symbolized by "covering the bones with flesh". Now if you think about it, the human structure is fully formed with the development of the bones. But the perfection and completion of that form is through muscle, tissue and flesh. So what the ayah is saying is that the DEEN of Allah, that was structured through the SHAREEAH of EISA (AS), is perfected and completed by the SHAREEAH of Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). And just as the flesh covers and subsumes all the previous stages of the human embryonic development, the religion of ISLAM consumed all the previous religions. So in that sense it is now "the" religion. Therefore in this sense, a true Muslim today, is actually also a true Christian; he is also a true JEW; he is true to every single religion that came before ISLAM; because ISLAM is an embodiment of all previous religions in its most complete and perfect form.

> — *Image text (from image 003; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/003.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Now here's another fascinating fact about this ayah. This embryonic development could have been explained in a single ayah because its the same subject matter. But it has been broken down into 3 ayaats. Because AL-ISLAM has 7 letters; and these stages are broken down to match them perfectly. The first two SULALAH and NUTFA represent the two letters of "AL" and the 5 stages mentioned in the third ayah represent the 5 letters of ISLAM.

Another thing is that SULALAH comes from TEEN, just as ADAM (AS) came from TEEN.
⟪ar-quote:إِذْ قَالَ رَبُّكَ لِلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ إِنِّى خَلِقٌۢ بَشَرًۭا مِّن طِينٍۢ ‎⟫

When Allah said to angels, I am going to create a man from clay. Clay is pure soil and its boundaries are the expanse of this world, just as ADAM (AS) was created in JANNAH that has no boundaries; no restrictions; no limitations. But when it came to NOOH (AS), he is symbolized with sperm that exists firmly in a very limited space; without boundaris; within constraints. And so Allah used a separate ayah to describe that. And he says ⟪ar:ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَهُ نُطْفَةًۭ فِى قَرَارٍۢ مَّكِينٍۢ⟫, We placed him as a drop of sperm in a firm lodging, which is this earth; and then the third ayah talks about the remaining stages all of which are within the confines of this earth.

So these are the 4 meanings of ISLAM that we learn from the Quran. It is telling us that every creature is in a state of submission to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). It is telling us that the way to find peace and safety in this world and the hereafter is through submission to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). It is also telling us, that all previous prophets were teaching ISLAM as their religion. And then this idea, that this is the religion of the final messenger, Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), who was sent to complete and perfect the teachings of all previous prophets. Allah says in the Quran

<!-- section 3 (id=5770, raw_sort=3): Pillars Of ISLAM -->

## The Pillars (Arkān) of Islām

We have 7 pillars of Islam, that Syedna Qazi Noman explains in his book DAYAM AL-ISLAM. The Imam of that time, Maulana ⟪ar:امام المعز لدین اللہ⟫ commanded him to write this book, specifically to separate truth from falsehood. Because by that time a lot innovation had crept into Islam. There were a ridiculous number of false AHADEES that were being quoted and attributed to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). So one day when Syedna Qazi Noman (QR) came to visit the Imam, he recited this Hadees of Rasul Allah(SAWAS) that:
⟪ar-quote:اذا اَظھَرتَ البِدعَ فی اُمَّتِی، فَلیُظھَر العالمُ عِلمُہ⟫

When you see innovations appearing within my community, then it is obligatory on the scholar to reveal his knowledge.

Then he said to Syedna Qazi Noman, that by "scholar" Rasul Allah(SAWAS) meant people like you! And then he commanded him to write this book. So in this book Syedna Qazi Noman took all the valid AHADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and left out all the invalid ones; thus separating truth from falsehood. When he completed the book, he presented it to Imam MOIZ, who then read every single word, before sactioned it. And he said, that whoever follows even the 40th portion of this book, I guarantee JANNAH for that person.

And from that point on, this book became a constitutional book for MOMINEEN. You can realize its importance by the fact that later IMAMs such as Imam ALI-ZAAHIR commanded the people of his time to memorize this book by heart; and then he would give out huge rewards to those who did memorize this book.

In this book "DAYAM AL-ISLAM", Syedna Qazi Noman talks about these 7 pillars: Wilayah, Taharah, Salaat, Zakaat, Saum, Hajj, Jehad; which InshaAllah we will discuss over the course of these ssions. But before we begin talking about them, let's first understand why these are called "pillars". The Arabic word for a single pillar is ⟪ar:دعامۃ⟫; and its plural is ⟪ar:دعائم⟫. Generally people just think, that he called these 7 practices "pillars" because they are "essential" to Islam. Even though that is certainly true, there's a lot more to it than just that. A general principle to remember when studying our DEEN, is that if something is said by a DAI, you can be certain that the statement has immense depth to it. Because a DAI never speaks at a superficial level.

### Foundation

What kind of a structure comes to mind when you hear the word pillar?
Are pillars vertical or horizontal structures?
So, right off the bat there is this idea that pillars are something that have an upward motion to them. They're reaching towards God.
Are pillars placed randomly or strategically?

When constructing a building where are the pillars placed?

How is a foundation created?

Pillars are the **vertical**structures of a building, that are **strategically**placed, within a foundation, to support the weight of the structure. The more solid the foundation is, the stronger the pillars will stand; and the stronger the pillars are, the more stable the building will be. So there is a direct relationship of "integrity" between these components.

When we observe a building, what is visible to us, the foundation or the pillars?

There are certain places where when you construct a building, about 10-15 years later, a big crack appears on the walls. And the reason for that is that soil under the foundation shifts, and that shows up as a crack on the wall.

The foundation of our DEEN is the SHAHADAH. The concept of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ ..... There is no god but Allah. The first part is LA ILAHA, which represents creating an empty space to put in the foundation (TAHANNUS); and once that space in the heart is emptied of all false gods, ILLA ALLAH represents the foundation itself.

These 7 practices of Islam are the pillars which are very "strategically" placed within the foundation of TAWHEED. These 7 practices are not random. Every دعامۃ has a time and place; when to do it; how often do it. For instance if you look at SALAAT, it is very strategically placed during the day. It has to do with the motion of the sun. Fasting has a very specific count and is placed in a particular month of each year. HAJJ is strategically placed at a particular time to be done "once" in a lifetime. ZAKAAT has a fixed ZAKAAT. So the idea is that each DA'AMA draws its strength from the foundation of ones TAWHEED. Each practice is a physical manifestation of ones TAWHEED. If there is a crack in the foundation of TAWHEED, where will the signs of crack show up? In these practices of the Muslim.

Another very prominent fact about a pillar is that it cannot be moved from its place. Tearing down walls and other auxiliary components is easy. It will have little, to no effect on the main structure; but taking down a pillar will certainly weaken the stability of the building. So if I'm walking in a house and I come against a pillar, I will have to walk around it; it will not move for me (pillars can be quite uncompromising that way). So the idea is that when its time for SALAAT, I will have to adjust my schedule to accommodate it; SALAAT will not adjust itself for me. When the month of Ramadan arrives, I have to structure my day around it. It won't be the other way round.

### Roof

What do pillars support?
Do the pillars have to setup first, or does the roof come first?

There is a common expression, "to put a roof on one's head", which indicates that the key component of a structure is the roof or the ceiling. Once the foundation and the pillars have been built, the "final" part is the placement of the roof. The roof is always placed from the top; just as the pillars are built up. So the idea is that once these practices of Islam are firmly established, the security, safety and protection come from Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), and it sits on top of these pillars, thus completing the house of ISLAM. **This is why, one of the meanings of the word ISLAM is safety**. And once the house of Islam is built on top of these strong pillars of practices, grounded in a strong foundation of TAWHEED, the MUSLIM (the one who submits), finds peace in that house. **This is why, one of the meanings of the word ISLAM is peace.**

> — *Image text (from image 004; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/004.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

When any house is built on these solid structures, the external climatic environment becomes irrelevant to the person living in that house. No matter what kinds of winds are blowing outside, the person inside the house remain safe; and his heart and mind always remain at peace. But if the pillars are weak, and the foundation is cracked, then the person has very good reason to fear what's happening outside.

So the idea is that if the foundation of TAWHEED is strong, and one has established firm pillars through these 7 practices, then no matter what the social, political, religious climate is outside of one's ISLAM, the MUSLIM will always remain in a constant state of peace and security. And this peace and security comes from submission. Submission is defined as the act of accepting or yielding to a superior force; or to the will or authority of another entity. So a MUSLIM is the one who literally submits to the protection and the safety of his master, that comes as a result of these solid practices that he has established. And this is how a muslim finds peace and safety in this world, and in the hereafter.

<!-- section 4 (id=5772, raw_sort=4): Linguistic menaing of IMAAN -->

## The Linguistic Meaning of Īmān

Recap

We talked about ISLAM being an experience that begins with TAHANNUS (the avoidance of SHIRK) and TAKHLIYA (an emptying of the heart from everything that is not god) - It is creating that empty space of LA ILAHA, in which one can then lay the foundation of ILLA ALLAH. And then on this foundation of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ we construct the 7 pillars of ISLAM. Once the pillars are built, the roof of safety and security is provided by Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), thus completing the structure of ISLAM. And so the one who submits and surrenders to the safety of this house built on a solid foundation and strong pillars, finds peace. But if the foundation of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ is cracked, and the pillars are weak, no matter how much one tries, the heart simply cannot find peace.

We studied 4 Quranic definitions of the word ISLAM. The first meaning is to "submit" or "surrender" one's free will, one's desires, to the will and desire of the creator. The second meaning is that of peace and safety. The third meaning is ISLAM as a universal religion; and an unbroken chain of guidance that began with Adam AS, and continued all the way to the final messenger Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). And the fourth and final meaning, is ISLAM as the religion that was perfected and completed by Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam).

---

⟪ar:ایمان⟫

Today we will begin looking at the meaning of EMAN or faith. Our conversation began with a HADEES in which JIBRAEEL (AS) came to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in the form of a man and asked him about ISLAM, IMAN and IHSAN. Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) defined ISLAM as:
⟪ar-quote:الْإِسْلَامُ أَنْ تَشْهَدَ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَیْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَتُقِیمَ الصَّلَاةَ وَتُؤْتِیَ الزَّکَاةَ وَتَصُومَ رَمَضَانَ وَتَحُجَّ الْبَیْتَ إِنْ اسْتَطَعْتَ إِلَیْهِ سَبِیلًا⟫

Islam is to witness that there is no God but Allah and Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is the Messenger of Allah; to give zakaat; to fast the month of Ramadan; and to perform a pilgrimage to the house of Allah if one is capable of travel. The HADEES continues and JIBRAEEL (AS) asks the prophet about IMAAN; which he then defines as belief in 6 things:
⟪ar-quote:أَنْ تُؤْمِنَ بِاللَّهِ وَمَلَائِکَتِهِ وَکُتُبِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَالْیَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَتُؤْمِنَ بِالْقَدَرِ خَیْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ⟫

IMAN is to believe in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the final Day, and to believe in the divine providence in case of both, good and evil.

> — *Image text (from image 005; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/005.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Let's first understand the meaning of the word EMAAN. The word IMAAN comes from the root word ⟪ar:أَمَنْ⟫, which means "safety"; and safety is inherently associated with "peace". Because one cannot be at peace until one is safe. Peace is a natural consequence of safety. Its verbal form (⟪ar:أَمَنَ ، یؤمِنُ⟫) means "to have faith or to believe"; and the idea there is that, only through "faith" in these 6 articles (Allah, angels, books, messengers, day of judgment, and divine providence), a person can ensure his or her **safety**and everlasting **peace**in this life and the afterlife.

In DAYAM AL-ISLAM, Syedna Qazi Noman (QR) narrates that ⟪ar:امام جعفر الصادق علیہ السلام⟫defines EMAN as a combination of 3 things:

⟪ar-quote:تَصدِیقُ بِالِجنَان ؛ وَ قَولُ بِالِّسَان ؛ وَعَمَلُ بِالأَرکَان⟫

EMAN is to testify with the heart; and to articulate with the tongue; and act with the limbs. In other words, much like anything else in the world, faith goes through its stages of development. The first step [where it all begins] is the heart (⟪ar:تَصدِیقُ بِالِجنَان⟫); the second step is making a commitment to that believe, through "articulation" (⟪ar:قَولُ بِالِّسَان⟫); and the final step is ⟪ar:عَمَلُ بِالأَرکَان⟫, to physically act upon [what one believes in and commitment to] with the limbs. So EMAN is what begins in the heart; develops into speech; and physically materializes into action. This is how we literally *create* our EMAN. And even though these are 3 distinct components, all three are subsumed within this one entity of EMAN.

Now this pattern is very interesting, because we know that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) created us in a spiritual realm (⟪ar:عالم الروحانی⟫)  long before he created us in this physical realm. He describes that creation in Surah Yaseen. He says:
**http://quran.com/36/82**

> — *Image text (from image 006; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/006.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

His command is only when He intends a thing that He says to it, "Be," and it is.

Now if you look at this AYAH, it also has 3 parts to the process of spiritual creation. The first is ⟪ar:ارادۃ⟫, which is the "divine will"; the second is his method of executing that divine will, which is through ⟪ar:قول⟫, through "speech".  (⟪ar:يَقُولَ لَهُ: كُن⟫ : he said to it, "be"); and the third is the "action" of creation itself (⟪ar:فَيَكُونُ⟫ : it is). But you can see, that although these seem to be 3 different components, they're all subsumed within his AMR [his command]. In other words, Allah's AMR, [his command] is what is at the essence of all creation. And so this AYAH quite litereally sets the pattern or the template for all spiritual creations. This is exactly now how we must also "create" our EMAAN in this world; through

⟪ar-quote:تَصدِیقُ بِالِجنَان ؛ وَ قَولُ بِالِّسَان ؛ وَعَمَلُ بِالأَرکَان⟫

Witnessing of the heart; articulation of the tongue; and action of the limbs, all of which are subsumed with one single entity of EMAN. They appear to be 3 things, but in reality they are one.

Now let's take a look at these three components individually.

<!-- section 5 (id=5774, raw_sort=5): Witnessing of the heart -->

## Witnessing of the Heart (Tasdīq bi-l-Qalb)

The first component is (⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫), "to testify with the heart" or "to have conviction about something". ⟪ar:تصدیق⟫comes from the root word ⟪ar:صدق⟫ which means "truth". ⟪ar:تصدیق⟫is the verbal form which means "to verify a truth". The word ⟪ar:جنان⟫is generally translated as "heart", but it actually comes from the root word JIN, which means "hidden" or "concealed". For example ⟪ar:الَّیلُ جَنَّ عَلَیہِ⟫, the night concealed or covered it. So what ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫ essentially means, is to verify the truth about that which is hidden.

Now according to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), the definition of EMAN is to believe in Allah, his angels, his revelation, his messengers, the final Day, and his providence; all of which are hidden from us. Only Allah has complete knowledge of all these things. But when it comes to us, where does our knowledge reside? It resides in the heart (⟪ar:العِلمُ فی الصُّدُور⟫). And is knowledge visible or is it hidden? It's hidden in the heart, and this is how you get the meaning, "to testify with the heart". What it really means is "to testify with complete knowledge of the heart".

**What is creed?**

So the very first thing to understand about EMAN in the Islamic tradition, is that it is not simply "blind faith". It is actually a clear "witnessing" of these "unseen realities" through intellectual reasoning. It is belief based on knowledge. And what we believe in is called a "creed". Creed or (⟪ar:عَقِیدۃ⟫) is defined as a set of beliefs that guide someone's actions. ⟪ar:عَقِیدۃ⟫comes from the word ⟪ar:عقد⟫, which means a knot. So ⟪ar:عَقِیدۃ⟫is what you are bound to; it is what you have conviction about. This is why marriage is also called an ⟪ar:عقد⟫because two people are bound together in their journey through life.

> — *Image text (from image 007; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/007.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Creed essentially are narrations that are transmitted down the chain of history, through a series of verbal or written narrations of people who are called the ⟪ar:مُحَدِّثُون⟫(the narrators). Creed is basically ⟪ar:نَقَل⟫. The word ⟪ar:نَقَل⟫in Arabic means to "transfer, transmit or transport", which is exactly what narrations are.
