These transmissions are then received by the intellect, which is the ⟪ar:عقل⟫. So ⟪ar:عقل⟫is a necessary condition for ⟪ar:نَقَل⟫. It is not a "sufficient" condition; it is an "absolute" necessity. And for this very reason, the Islamic SHAREEH is not enforced on somone who does not have control over his intellect. According to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) SHAREEAH does not apply to people in 3 states:
1. A child until he reaches intellectual maturity
2. An insane person until he regains his sanity
3. An unconscious person or a person sleeping until he wakes up.

What you will find common between all three, is that they do not have control over their intellect. So the intellect is an absolute necessity for creed or religion. We've studied the word ⟪ar:عقل⟫in detail in the previous session. It has several meanings. The first meaning is container; because it has the ability to store. Another meaning comes from the word ⟪ar:عِقَال⟫, which is the rope that is used to tie a camel. So ⟪ar:عَقَلَ⟫means to restrain. ⟪ar:عقل⟫is the faculty that enables a person to "restrain" himself from that which is harmful to him. And that is also what a container does. It prevents what is put into it from flowing out. Another meaning of AQL is a "scale or a balance". The ability to discern and choose between two goods and two evils; to choose the greater of two goods or to choose the lesser of two evils.

In the light of all these meanings, a child does not have these capabilities. Children cannot remember what is said to them; they cannot restrain themselves and they do not have the ability to choose between two goods or two evils. Neither does an insane person; nor does an unconscious person or a person who is asleep. Because creed is a responsibility. And,
⟪ar-quote:اولُ واجباً علی من کُلِّفَۃٍ ..... العقل⟫

The first prerequisite for "responsibility" is the intellect. TAKLEEF comes with the intellect. The Arabic word TAKLEEF is different from the Urdu TAKLEEF. In Urdu TAKLEEF means pain, burden or discomfort. In Arabic, TAKLEEF actually means "to entrust" or "to commission". So AQL has to preceed NAQL. The intellect has to preceed the "trust" of transmission. Because that creed has to be properly understood in its proper context. If I'm speaking to you, you have to also understand what I'm telling you. If I tell you that Allah has neither ⟪ar:تَرکِیب⟫nor ⟪ar:عدد⟫, and then I explain to you, that ⟪ar:عدد⟫is number, and ⟪ar:تَرکِیب⟫is composition; you have to be able to understand the difference between discrete numbers, such as 3 pens, and a pen that is made up of 3 parts. Because even though they're both 3, one is a number, and the other is composition; and both these things are understood by the intellect. So if one does not have the ability to understand that, then that person is not teachable according to Islamic tradition.

When one of the scholars, Al-Khaleel (Ibn Ahmed) was asked a question about knowledgable people, he said there are 4 types and there is no fifth.
1. There are people who really know the truth; and they know that they know. Those are scholars, learn from them.
2. There are people who know, but they don't know that they know. Those are the heedless people. The GHAAFIL! They are heedless of their own knowledge. So remind them so that they can benefit from their knowledge.
3. The third are those who don't know, and they know that they don't know. Those are the students, so teach them.
4. And finaly there are those who don't know, but think that they know. Those are the fools, so avoid them.

So CREED are ⟪ar:نَقَل⟫or transmissions that come down through time, via narrators (the ⟪ar:مُحَدِّثُون⟫). A MUHADDIS (the narrator) is like a pharmacist. He is not a doctor. So never get a prescription from a pharmacist. All the pharmacist knows is NAQL. But what the doctor has is AQAL. A pharmacist simply knows how to read the prescription and put it together. But a doctor understands the WHY; he understands the "context" of that prescription (at least we hope :) Because a physician is trained to discern between signs and symptoms. If you have Jhondis, he knows what that means; he understands the prognosis? He knows where is it going, what its leading to? He knows all these different things.

Now the same is true about these credal formulations of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). You have the creed (which is NAQL) being transmitted down through centuries; and we know that numerous things change over time. Languages deterioriate, expressions change, ideologogies shift. So what these narrations meant to the original sources, could be very different from how we understand them in todays day and age. And this is what necessitates the presence of an IMAM. The "true" doctor, who is divinely trained in these discernments; who can separate the right from wrong. Who can tell us what is valid, and more importantly why it's valid. This is why we need the DAI, who takes his knowledge from the IMAM. This is why we need the MANASEEB, who take their knowledge from the DAI, and reveal to us the timeless and immutable "essence" hidden within these narrations; and then present them to us in a way that our intellects can grasp; in a language that we can understand. In other words, each of these HUDOOD [these ranks], they serve as an external Intellect for us.

Because the most dangerous thing that you can have, is intellect without religion; or religion without intellect. Both are disasterour states. Intellect without religion, leads to concentration camps and gas chambers. It perceives the world as "The Jewish Problem!" And what's the most efficient way to deal with this problem? To get rid of it! This is pure "blind" reasoning! This is how Nazi Germany pereceived the world! EFFICIENCY! We are the superior race, and so we are beyond good and evil. Everyone else is an inferior form, therefore genecide is perfectly acceptable. So without religion, the intellect can be used for evil. But then religion without intellect, also leads to concentration camps and gas chambers. They might be metaphorical ones, but again we have a problem. The disbelievers (the non-muslims) are a problem, so let's kill them all!! This is the solution that religion reaches without intellect. Because god said in the Quran, to kill them wherever you find them. Let's just select one single ayah, take it out of context, and just do what it says. And so now you have these lunatics, killing innocent people in the name of religion.

But this is what happens when you divorce one from the other. You end up with the same disastrous results, which is brutality and a loss of humanity. And we all know people (even in our own families at times) who subscribe to such blind faith. They don't question anything they're told to do. These are people who scoff at evolution, even though they've never studied biology. And I'm sorry, but that is just not an argument. That's called TAQLEED (blind imitation). And our religion is way exalted; it is too complete and too perfect to be followed blindly. But there are people who have this blind mentality:

*Just because it doesn't agree with my understanding of the Quran, therefore it's wrong! Why? Because the Quran is from Allah! Well, why is the Quran from Allah? Because Allah said so! Where did he say that? In the Quran!*

And it is this type of circular reasoning that drives scientific and rational people insane about religious people. Because what they say then, is that this religion is not based on a foundation. It's based on "basic beliefs" that do not have a foundation! Because that’s what a basic belief is! If I say, why do you believe that? and you tell me, Well, I don't need to tell you why I believe it! I just do because it says in the Quran! Or because my father did it this way, or my husband did it this way, or that MULLA SAHAB did it this way! If that's all you can say without providing a context for it, then that's a "basic belief" without a foundation.

Today whether we like it or not, we have to deal with the fact that we are living in a world, that has introduced ideas which have seemed to overturn previous notions and beliefs on their head. Evolution is a real theological problem. Because it's a problem that deals with cause and effect; and it deals with the origin of our species. How we were created, and who created us. And these questions need to be studied at a very deep level. They have to be looked at honestly. And if it has merits they need to be identified, and reconciled with our theology. And if there are things which are incompatible with our theology, then they need to be pointed out as well, in a way that can be logically understood.

One of the downfalls of this religion has been brought about by two people. First, the close minded teachers, who are not willing to look at any problem that defies their belief system; and second, by irresponsible students who are not willing to put in the time and effort to understand the Quran within its proper context. Students who demand one-line simple "yes/no" answers to extremely complex questions. And these are both very serious problems! And they both stem from an arrogance which prevents both from accepting the fact, that either they don't have an answer; or the fear that what they believe in might be wrong; or that they're not ready to shoulder the burden of this faith. So the easiest solution to that is bash the faith and reject it.

And the root cause of this problem is this divorce between NAQL and AQL. Its caused by these people that bash ISLAM based on their limited intellects, by quoting narrations out of context. They take a couple of AYATS without understanding their proper context, and start bashing ISLAM. These are, what I call, the NAQL-heads!! So its very important that we bring both these things together. And our SULEMANI creed is so brilliant at doing this. But it takes time and effort to study it. It takes years of discipline and hard work to see them both come together which people today are simply not ready to do. They want to choose this highly sophisticated religion of Allah, like they select products from a TV commercial. It's beyond ridiculous!!

---

So the first component of EMAN is ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫ , to verify and testify for that which is hidden, through the employment of the Intellect (AQL).

> — *Image text (from image 008; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/008.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

According to scholars, the difference between a rational person and an irrational person, is that the irrational person cannot distinguish between 3 types of propositions:

The first are the "empirical propositions", which utilizes the 5 senses. Things that we come to understand through observation or experimentation. These deal with things that we can see, hear, smell, touch and taste. In other words, empirical propositions deal with the realm that can be witnessed [which the Quran calls ⟪ar:عالم الشھادۃ⟫]. So fire is hot; it is bright; when it combines with oxygen, combustion takes place; wood emits smoke when burnt. These are all empirical observations.

The second are "rational propositions", which are logical propositions, like 3 + 2 = 5 and 5 - 3 = 2. Or propositions that work through inference. If I see smoke rising in the distance, I can infer that there is a fire there, even though I am unable to see the fire itself; because I know that when something burns, it emits smoke. But then my inference could be incorrect, if smoke is the only thing I'm factoring in. It could simply be from a large group of people having a cigar party. So then what is needed to maintain that rational proposition of "fire", is *more* empirical data. If I start walking towards the smoke, and I see things getting brighter and I feel the air is getting warmer, then the probability of my rational proposition, of there being a fire in the distance increases. Because now I have more empirical data in the form of light and heat to support my rational proposition. In other words, rational propositions help us deal with the unseen realm "through" the seen realm. And the more empirical data we have, the more we can confirm the rational proposition. The character of Sherlock Holmes is entirely based on rational propositions through empirical data.

The third type are "revelatory propositions". These are the Quranic propositions that talk about the existence of a creator, angels, divine books, messengers, day of judgment, heaven and hell. And it is these revelatory propositions, that belief or EMAN is grounded in; because they talk about the unseen realities, the greatest of which is the belief in the existence of Allah. Because once you believe in Allah, believing in the rest becomes very easy. Now the challenge here, is that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) is not an entity that can be witnessed by the 5 senses; nor can he be confined by reason or the intellect. So the *only* way we can come to know of him is not by studying him; but through the empirical and rational study of his *creation*. The only way we can come to know of him is through his "signs" or "AYAAT" which are empirical propositions, pointing back to the rational propositions. And this is precisely what the Quran does. It uses empirical data in support of rational data to prove revelatory propositions.

So for example, revelation tells us that Allah is the creator of this universe. The universe being a "created" entity, is supported by our rational and empirical observations. Because we know there was a time in the past when this universe did not exist; and there will come a time in the future when it will return back to non-existence. And existence and non-existence are attributes of creation, therefore this universe is a creation. And then empirical and rational data also confirm that every creation necessitates the existence of a creator. So if this universe is a creation, it must necessarily have a creator. So then the AYAH that
⟪ar-quote:اللہ الذی خلق السماوت و الارض⟫

Allah is the one who created the heavens and the earth, is a "revelatory proposition", that is backed up and supported by rational and empirical evidence. And so when we can believe this proposition, it makes it much easier to believe when he says, that he also created a spiritual universe. Because the one who has the power to create this physical universe from nothingness, must also have the power to create the spiritual universe from nothingness.

If you can understand this phenomenon, you can underatand the motive of the Quran. Everywhere in the Quran, Allah asks us to reflect on the "creations" of the heavens and the earth. He never asks us to reflect on Allah himself.

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱخْتِلَفِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَٱلنَّهَارِ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَلْبَبِ⟫

No doubt about it.... in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the conflict between night and day, there are signs for the people of intellect. ALBAAB comes from the word ⟪ar:لُب⟫which means seed. It means a pith, or the seed ,or the essence, or the jist of something that is always hidden in the earth. That's why ⟪ar:لُب⟫is a word that is used for the intellect, or the mind, or the vehicle of understanding, because it can recognize the unseen through the seen.

So Allah demands reflection on his creations, why? Because the heavens and the earth and everything they contain provide empirical and rational evidence for every revelatory proposition. And this why Maulana Ali taught us:
⟪ar-quote:لا تفکر فی اللہ ..... ولاکن تفکر فی خلق اللہ⟫

Don't reflect upon Allah..... Instead reflect upon the "creations" of Allah. Because through the witnessing of this universe and how it operates, lies the evidence for what lies beyond it.  ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫ (witnessing and testifying that which is hidden) is only possible through the study of *creation* and not the creator. And so Intellect is the first requirement for understanding this tradition. If one cannot distinguish between these 3 types of propositions, then he is not an AQIL.

<!-- section 6 (id=5775, raw_sort=6): Articulation of the tongue -->

## Articulation of the Tongue (Iqrār bi-l-Lisān)

Recap
- EMAN according to Imam Jaffar AlSaadiq (AS) is 3 things. The first is ⟪ar:تَصدِیقُ بِالِجنَان⟫ , witnessing and testifying with the heart for all the hidden realities described by revelatory propositions. Second is ⟪ar:قَولُ بِالِّسَان⟫, to articulate that belief with the tongue; and finally ⟪ar:عَمَلُ بِالأَرکَان⟫, to "act" upon what the heart believes and the tongue articulates.
- We talked about AQL vs NQL [Intellect vs narrations]. I explained how AQL is an absolute pre-condition for NAQL
- We also talked about the 3 types of propositions that the intellect must be able to grasp and differentiate between, in order to understand religion.

The empirical propositions that deal with the seen world utilizing the 5 senses.

The rational propositions that deal with the unseen world; and are supported by empirical data.

Finally the reveleatory propositions that deal with the spiritual universe, employing the use of rational as well as empirical data. All articles of IMAN is grounded in these revelatory propositions.
- And we ended the previous conversation with the motive of the Quran which is to reflect on the "creations" and not the "creator" of the heavens and the earth. Allah is neither empirical nor rational, and therefore it is impossible to come to know of him, except through a sincere reflection on his creation. And so the idea of ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫ is to witness and testify for authenticity of the revelatory propositions. How did the heart achieve that certainty? Through the knowledge gained by employing the "rational" intellect, and supporting it by the "empirical" evidence of the 5 senses.

⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫

Today we're going to look at the next component, which is ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫, (to articulate with the tongue). Once the heart has witnessed and believed, the tongue must now unveil that hidden belief through speech. The word ⟪ar:قول⟫ comes from ⟪ar:قُل⟫which means "to say"or "to speak". ⟪ar:لسان⟫in Arabic means two things. It generally means "tongue", but it also means "language". So ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫ means to "speak with the tongue" or "to articulate through language". So what'll we'll learn today is that this second component (of speech), is essentially a medium; an intermediary, that connects the rational world to the empirical world.
⟪ar:
> — *Image text (from image 009; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/009.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.
⟫

We know that the created world is divided into two parts. There is the ⟪ar:عالم الشھادۃ⟫, which is the empirical world that can be witnessed and experienced through the 5 senses; and there is the ⟪ar:عالم الغیب⟫, the "rational world" that cannot be experienced through the 5 senses; and yet, the intellect can experience its effects "through" the manifestations of the seen world. So if I have seen a tree, but I have never seen the roots of a tree, I could deny the existence of those roots. And yet when I water the soil, I see the plant growing out of it and coming into the world; even though I water the soil and not the plant. And so from this observation I gain some understanding about the nature of the plant and the nature of the soil. That there's a relation between what I see in the world, and what I don't see in the world. There must be something under the soil, that is taking in this water and making the plant grow. So even though the roots of the plant are hidden and concealed under the blanket of the soil, I can still observe and experience its effects through the plant that is coming out of that soil. And this is why the seed is such an extraordinary metaphor; because we also come from a seed. But we come from a seed that is nurtured in the hidden soil of a womb; and yet the effects of our growth becomes evident through the belly of the mother. So rational propositions are constantly being validated in this world, through empirical observations.

There is an AYAH in the Quran which I'd like to study in detail today: Allah says:

|

⟪ar-quote:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ⟫

We will reveal our AYAATS in the horizons and within themselves. This AYAH begins with the word ⟪ar:**سَنُرِيهِمْ**,⟫which comes from the root word ⟪ar:رأی⟫, which is generally translated as "to see"; but what it really means is to "reveal through a different form". So for example Allah says to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in Surah AlFeel:

⟪ar-quote:أَلَمْ تَرَ كَيْفَ فَعَلَ رَبُّكَ بِأَصْحَبِ ٱلْفِيلِ⟫

Did you not see what your master did with the people of elephants? Now the event Allah is referring to the time when ABRAHA came with his armies of elephants to destroy the KA'ABA. This incident during the time of his grand father (Maulana Abdul Muttaib AS) long before the prophet was born. So there is no way he could have physically seen the event with his eyes. And that's why the word ⟪ar:تَرَی⟫is used! Have we not revealed to you in the form of stories and narrations, about what your master did with the people of the elephants? So Allah says ⟪ar:**سَنُرِيهِمْ**⟫we will soon reveal through a different form. Reveal what?

⟪ar:آيَتِنَا⟫, which comes from the word ⟪ar:آیۃ⟫and it means a number of things. The first meaning is something valuable, or something that has a purpose. For example, ⟪ar:خرج القوم بآیاتھم⟫(People came out with their valuables). ⟪ar:آیۃ⟫also means to clearly distinguish one thing from another. But the most prominant meaning is that of a "sign" or a "symbol" that points to something else. When you are driving to work following the road signs, one road-sign leads you to another road-sign; which then leads you to another road-sign; until you reach your final destination. The purpose of a sign or a symbol is never the symbol itself; rather the thing that it points to.

Allah says, ⟪ar:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا⟫ we will reveal "our" signs in differnt forms. What are Allah's AYAATS? They're the AYATS of the Quran! His "revelatory propositions", that are valuable; that are meaningful; that have purpose, that distinguish truth from falsehood; and that points to something else. Where will these signs be revealed? ⟪ar:فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ⟫ , in the horizons (in things that can be observed and experienced through the 5 senses); ⟪ar:وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ⟫, and in their own souls (which are hidden and can only be witnessed through rational propositions). In other words we will reveal our revelatory propositions to them, in the form of empirical and rational data.

Now from a linguistic perfection of the Quran, what does Allah mention first? empirical observations or rational observations? He mentions empirical first (⟪ar:ٱلأٓفَاقِ⟫), because we as children begin our lives in the empirical realm. We do not begin our life in the rational realm. As children all we do is observe and experience through the 5 senses. Rationality comes with maturity. As we grow older and have acquired enough empirical data, we gain the ability to reason. And so the AYAH mentions horizons first, and souls second. SubhanAllah!

Now what's interesting is that by the nature of this world, we are constantly decreasing in the sensory, but we are increasing in meaning. As we grow older, our senses weaken, but our intellects strengthen. And this in itself is a sign, that we are not created for the sensory world; rather we are created for the rational world. But then it is also true, that reason can only increase through the 5 senses. The more empiricial data we have to support rational propositions, the more we are able to believe that rational proposition to be true. So Allah says:

⟪ar-quote:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ⟫

We will reveal to them our revelatory propositions in the form of empirical and rational evidence. And how much data will will provide for both propositions?

 ⟪ar-quote:حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ⟫

Until it becomes absolutely clear to them that these revelatory propositions are absolutely real. The AYAH does not define a limit; it states a condition. "Until" it becomes clear to them that these revelatory propositions are absolutely real. In other words, evey single human being regardless of their intellectual capacity, will have as much evidence as they need, to make the hidden, absolutely manifest before them. We will keep showing them our signs, until they are able to "see" these revelatory propositions with the eyes of their intellect; until they will be able to hear the sounds of the heavens with the ears. Until they can smell its fragrance; taste its sweetness; feel its pleasures; and then testify with absolute conviction..... s

⟪ar-quote:أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ⟫

that all of this is AL-HAQQ (Absolutely Real).

Reality and things

Now there is a theory in linguistics, that language is not just for the purpose of communication, but embedded within the language is a worldview. In other words, individuals articulate their worldview through their language. Just to give you a good example of this, the word in English for "reality" comes from a Latin word "RES" which means "thing". That's a very interesting concept right there! In other words embedded in the English language itself, they're telling you how they perceive reality. Reality is "things".  There is an inherent materialism in that word. But now if you look at the Arabic language, the word for reality is ⟪ar:حَقِیقَۃ⟫, and it comes from the root word HAQ, which means "real". ⟪ar:الحَقُّ⟫means "the real". So embedded in the Arabic language itself, we find, that the perception of reality is already related to something that is beyond materialism. It is related to the divine! The idea is that "reality" is not what we are experiencing in the realm of "things";  but it actually transcends the realm of things. Because in the Islamic tradition God is not a thing! The word in Arabic for thing is ⟪ar:شئی⟫. And ⟪ar:شئی⟫comes from the word ⟪ar:مشیئۃ⟫ (a will). So SHAI means "that which is willed into existence". We studied in the previous session:

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّمَآ أَمْرُهُۥٓ إِذَآ أَرَادَ شَيْـًٔا⟫

It is from his command, that when he wills a SHAI (a thing),

⟪ar-quote:أَن يَقُولَ لَهُۥ كُن فَيَكُونُ⟫

he says to it BE and it is. So this universe that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) created for us is a SHAI, It is a valuable, it has meaning and a purpose. What is that purpose? To point back to his IRADAH (his divine will) and his AMR (his command). To understand why he created us! For that reason alone he created this universe! That's the reason this universe is called ⟪ar:العالم⟫.

> — *Image text (from image 012; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/012.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

There are three words to understand here. ALAM, ALIM, and ALEEM. All 3 words share a common root, which is ILM (knowledge). The first word ALAM means "that which can be known". The second word ALIM means "the one who comes to know". The third is ALEEM, which means "the all-knowing" and is one of the attributes of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). So Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) created the ALAM (that which can be known); so that we could study it (become ALIM) and come to know of the ALEEM (the all-knowing).  And so Allah says,

⟪ar-quote:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ⟫

We will reveal to them our IRADAH, our MASHEEAA [our divine will], in the horizons (which is the ALAM); and in their own souls (which is the ALIM); because we are souls who are given intellectual capacity to study the horizons!

 ⟪ar-quote:حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ..... أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ⟫

Until it becomes absolutely clear to them, that all of this is from the ALEEM! That none of this could have existsed without the⟪ar:أَمرُ الحَق⟫; without the command of the one who is the "absolute real". In other words, this universe is not real in the true sense of the word! Because by definition "reality" is something that does not change. And the *only" thing constant in this universe *is* change! Empirical propositions change; rational propositions change; but what never changes are the revelatory propositions. They are always constant! Because Allah is absolute! He is the ultimate reality! He is a reality that has no "otherness"; that when his reality is articulated, every other reality disappears into the falsehood of non-existence. This is the concept of utter "transcendence and immanence". He is beyond all "things" and yet he is manifesting through every "thing" in existence. He cannot be accessed because of his remoteness, but neither can he be alienated because of his closeness. And this is why the ONLY way to come to know of him, is through the empirical and rational study of what he created [His AYAAT]. But Allah himself is above and *beyond* all the empirical and rational confines of his creation.

---

### Language

So what this AYAH is telling us, is that the ⟪ar:آفاق⟫and the ⟪ar:أنفس⟫are the empirical and rational propositions through which the revelatory propositions are revealed! Now if you think about it, this is exactly what language does. Our [thoughts, intent, desires, meanings, knowledge] are all unseen revelatory propositions, that we "reveal" through language. Through our speech we give our imperceptible thoughts a "form", which are made up of words and meanings!  Words are empirical in nature (like the ⟪ar:آفاق⟫, the horizons) because they can be heard; but what we extract from words are meanings, which are formless and rational in nature (like the ⟪ar:أنفس⟫or souls); And our words and meanings, point back to what? Our intentions and thoughts, which are our revelatory propositions. Now what comes first? Words or Meanings? We hear the words first and then extract the meaning. In other words, even with language, it is empirical first and rational second. And where do the meanings guide us to? To the intentions, thoughts, desires, knowledge of the speaker! SubhanAllah!

Now we know that this earth is nothing in comparison to the size of the universe, let alone the size of the spiritual universe; and yet from the horizons of our finite world, we draw an infinite amount of rational knowledge. And this is again, exactly what speech does! Speech is a structure of words, that reveal an "infinite" amount of hidden meanings, through a "finite" set of letters and sounds. Just think about that for a second! We as human beings, have the capacity to produce an infinite number of meanings using just a few letters and sounds. Quran, that is this vast ocean of meanings, is essentially built upon just 28 letters! Allahu Akbar!!  You want to experience a miracle? There you have it right there in speech! It's really incredible!

So what we're learning now is that through speech, we are literally creating a universe, on the "exact same pattern as Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) created his universe! Let's look at this AYAH in our own human context:
⟪ar-quote:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا⟫

You and I reveal "our" intentions [knowledge, beliefs]
⟪ar-quote:فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ⟫

through words and meanings
⟪ar-quote:حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ..... أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ⟫

until our intent becomes absolutely clear to the person we are communicating with!  Allah has literally given us the power to create, on the "exact" same pattern as he created this universe! How did Allah create the universe? Through a command! KUN (Be),  which then executed -  FAYAKOON (and it became).

> — *Image text (from image 013; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/013.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

If you look at the word KUN, it is a command that is made up of 2 letters; and FAYAKOON is the excution of that command which has is made up of 5 letters. What does our command center [the AQL] comprise of? Two entities: the heart and the intellect. What do we use to execute the commands of our intellect? The 5 senses! SubhanAllah! Can evolution explain this perfection?

And this is why the Arabs, in their eloquence called human beings ⟪ar:الحیوان الناطق⟫. NUTQ in Arabic means "to articulate"; but it also means "to reason". NUTQ is also the root word for ⟪ar:مَنطِق⟫, which means "rationale" or "logic". Why? Because at the very root of our "reasoning powers", is speech. At the very root of *all* knowledge, is language. There would be no knowledge, and there would be no ability to reason without language; because language "unveils" knowledge! Everything I've taught you so far, I did not create anything new to show you, I simply unveiled what was hidden from you! How did I do this unveiling? Through speech! In other words, language is the "meeting point" of empirical and rational propositions in the form of words and meanings! And this is why language is such an incredible gift that has been given to us by Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala); and it comes from the heaven. Allah says:

> — *Image text (from image 014; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/014.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

⟪ar-quote:وَمِنْ آيَتِهِۦ خَلْقُ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْض⟫

From amongst his signs, is the creation of the heavens and the earth

⟪ar-quote:وَٱخْتِلَفُ أَلْسِنَتِكُمْ وَأَلْوَنِكُمْ⟫

And the differences in your languages and your complexion's

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّلْعَلِمِينَ⟫

Surely  in that, there is a sign for people who know; for  people who have this knowledge.

In Arabic rhetoric there is this concept of TIBAAQ, in which you use opposites like ⟪ar:لیل و النھار⟫ (night and day). This is a very common motive in the Quran to use these opposites. ⟪ar:الدنیا و الآخرۃ⟫ (this life and the afterlife); ⟪ar:الذکر و الانثا⟫ (male and female). Allah uses these opposites, but when multiple comparisons are made in the Quran, there is always a corelation between them. In this verse, Allah first mentions the creations of the heavens and then the earth; and then he corresponds that with the diversity in languages and complexions. Which means there is a relationship between the heavens and language; and there is a relationship between earth and complexions. So what is that relation?

In the story of Adam (AS), Allah says

⟪ar-quote:وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا⟫

Allah taught Adam (AS) the ⟪ar:أَسْمَآءَ⟫. ASMAA comes from the root word ⟪ar:سَمُو⟫, which means, "to come from above". It is also the root word for ⟪ar:سمآء⟫, or ⟪ar:ٱلسَّمَوَتِ ,⟫ referring to the heaven. The reason for that is, that Allah gave Adam (AS) the knowledge of the divine names (⟪ar:الاسمآء⟫), and the nature of knowledge is that it always flows from a higher rank to a lower rank. just as water falls from the heavens to the earth. Language corelates to the heavens, because language is "celestial" in nature; but complexions are "terrestrial", because they come from ⟪ar:الارض⟫, they come from the mud. So once again, what we are being told here is that the human being is a meeting place between the heavens and the earth. What represents our celestial nature is our language and our ability to acquire knowledge through it; and what represents our terrestrial nature is our complexions, and our diversities, and our appearances.

And so the Arabs recognized this reality, and called human beings ⟪ar:الحیوان الناطق⟫ (the articulating and reasoning animal)! Because we not only have the ability to reveal what lies hidden within us; we also possess the ability to interpret what lies hidden outside of us. We are able to discern through language which is another sign from Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). Because if you look at the essence of speech, it is basically encoding and decoding. I am encoding the knowledge that lies hidden within me, and I am revealing it to you. I am taking a MEANING, which is spiritual or meta-physical in nature, and then I am encoding that meaning into a structure of physical words which you can hear. You then listen to those physical words, decode it, and extract my intended meaning from it. And this ability to encode and decode, is something we all possess at the MOST basic level. Why? Because THAT is the very nature of this physical universe (the ALAM). Allah (the ALEEM) encoded all the realities of his spiritual realm, in the form of this physical universe (the ALAM)! Who did he do this for? For us! So that we would study it, decode it, and come to know (become AALIM) of the one who is the ultimate reality!

That is the purpose of articulation! When I tell you "Please bring me a glass of water", hidden in those words and meanings, lies my "will", my "desire", my "intent"; and in it is a call to "action". The purpose of my words, was for you to hear it, understand it and then bring me a glass a water. But what the NAQL-head evolutionist does, is he gets lost in analysing the words and the letters of the statement. Look how the word "please" comes before the statement making it a request and not a command. And the word "please" comes from the old French word "ple-ze-yar" which means joy or pleasure. Look how this word "evolved" from Latin into French and then into Middle English. Because evolution demands survival of the fittest. Look how grammatically each word is connected to the rest of the word. This is a noun, this is a verb..... ..... Aaaah..... Hello! I'm still thirsty here!

It sounds silly, but this is *exactly* what people are doing! The purpose of encoding this physical universe as SHAI; was for us to decode it and see the ⟪ar:مشیئا⟫of the creator. To understand his "divine will" ; to learn the "meaning"; the meta-physical aspects that they point to; and to ultimately recognize his AMR (his command) from which it all began. And this is why language is such a fundamental component in our human existence because it is the key to this cipher. Because through language you are witnessing me and I am witnessing you! Through language you get to know who I am; and I get to know who you are. You cannot see me right now, but by witnessing my creation (the sound of my words), you know that I exist! And as long as you can hear my voice, I exist for you! This is the out-of-sight out-of-mind phenomena; that as subjective human beings, things have reality for us only as long as we perceive them. When they are no longer within our perception of witnessing or hearing, or our intellectual perception through thinking about things, they disappear. And so Allah says:

⟪ar-quote:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ⟫

We will constantly reveal to them our signs, in the horizons and in their souls, until they witness the one who is "ultimately real". And then he asks us a question:
⟪ar-quote:أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ⟫

Isn't it [proof] enough that your master is witnessing everything? The AYAH begins with Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) making us witness his signs; and ends with him witnessing us. Just as you are witnessing the world of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), your world is being witnessed by him. In other words, isn'the fact that this universe exists, and continues to exist, proof of my existence? Because without *his* witnessing, this world would disappear. Just as things disappear for us when we are not actively witnessing them. SubhanAllah!

---

Do you see how magnificent this design is? Within the very definition of EMAN; within these 3 components, Allah has revealed to us the entire formula and purpose of his creation?

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّمَآ أَمْرُهُۥٓ إِذَآ أَرَادَ شَيْـًٔا⟫⟪ar-quote:أَن يَقُولَ لَهُۥ كُن فَيَكُونُ⟫

There is the IRADAH, the divine will (⟪ar:تصدیق بالاجنان⟫). There is the execution of that IRADAH (⟪ar:فَيَكُونُ⟫) which is the creation of the universe; and in between the two you have speech; the command KUN, connecting the two, by bringing the divine will into existence.

⟪ar:تصدیق ⟪ar:بالاجنان⟫⟫; the spiritual universe; ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫ the physical universe; and in between the two ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫; which is the Quran itself connecting the two together. Quran being the speech of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) is completely "spiritual", and yet it is in the form of  a "book" made up of words, which is completely physical. One one hand it describes the pleasures and pains of the afterlife, and on the other explains how to live life in this physical world.

⟪ar:تصدیق ⟪ar:بالاجنان⟫⟫; unseen revelatory propositions;  ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫ entirely perceivable empirical observations; and in between the two, there is ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫; the rational propositions, which even though are unseen, are supported by the 5 senses.

⟪ar:تصدیق ⟪ar:⟪ar:بالاجنان⟫⟫⟫; our beliefs, which are completely spiritual; ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫ the action of the limbs which are completely physical; and in between the two, ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫, language which is both empirical as well as rational. It is articulated in the form of sounds which are physical in nature, and they contain meanings and intentions which are meta-physical in nature.

⟪ar:تصدیق ⟪ar:⟪ar:⟪ar:بالاجنان⟫⟫⟫⟫, witnessing with the heart. Where is the heart situated? Hidden inside the body; ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫; action of the limbs. Where are the limbs situated? Outside the body where it can be seen? Connecting the two is ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫; speech of the tongue. Where is the tongue placed? Within the mouth, where it can be seen, but also hidden with the jaw. The tongue exists in both states.

⟪ar:تصدیق ⟪ar:⟪ar:⟪ar:⟪ar:بالاجنان⟫⟫⟫⟫⟫; belief in the spiritual universe, which is entirely meta-physical, and yet absolutely real and immutable. It never changes form and will never ceases to exist. ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫;  actions which even though are entirely physical, they are temporal in nature. All actions come to an end, just as this physical universe will come to an end. So one is unseen but permanent; the other is seen but temporal, and connecting the two is ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫; articulation through speech; which is physical because it travels through sound waves, and yet temporal, because those sound waves dissipates into nonexistence. But the meanings those sounds carry, even though unseen are preserved forever in the hearts of the one who hear it. Speech reflects both attributes.

So within these 3 components, Allah has revealed his formula of creation for us. Now why is the essence of everything 3? Because the essence of our creedal formula (⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫), is made up of 3 letters: ALIF, LAAM and HA.

> — *Image text (from image 015; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/015.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Alif represents the spiritual universe, hence it is vertical! HA represents the physical universe, hence it is circular! Because every phenomenon in this world repeats itself. LAAM is the letter in between. Look at its shape! It has both shapes [of ALIF and HAA] within it. A part of it is straight like the ALIF, and a part of it is circular like the HA.....

⟪ar-quote:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ⟫

We will reveal to them our signs in the horizons and their souls until it becomes unmistakably clear to them, then all of this is from AL-HAQ. He made us interpreters of the world; so we could study this universe which is echoing one single truth! That behind all of this, at the root of all existence is Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), who is its creator and its sustainer. And this is why those who look at the tree and cannot even comprehend the existence of the root structure, only know half of the story. Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) says.....
⟪ar-quote:يَعْلَمُونَ ظَهِرًۭا مِّنَ ٱلْحَيَوٰةِ ٱلدُّنْيَا⟫

They know the outward half the world
⟪ar-quote:وَهُمْ عَنِ ٱلْآخِرَةِ هُمْ غَفِلُونَ⟫

but they are heedless about the other half. In other words, "knowledge",  is not sufficient knowledge if you only know half of this created reality. Until you see the hidden one manifesting through the outward, you are in a state of heedlesness.  And what's interesting is that he does not say:
⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:وَهُمْ⟫عَنِ الباطنۃ هُمْ غَفِلُونَ⟫

They are heedless about the hidden. He didn't say that. He said ⟪ar:وَهُمْ عَنِ ٱلْآخِرَةِ هُمْ غَفِلُونَ⟫ , They are heedless about the ⟪ar:آخرۃ⟫, which comes from ⟪ar:خیر⟫(that which is better). So these are people who are looking at this external form of the universe, but they are heedless about what's actually better. And through the AYAH of language and speech, we come to know that if this physical universe exists, there must exist a corresponding spiritual universe, which is much better and loftier than this physical universe. Because meanings are superior to words, in that they create the words. Soul is superior to the body, because it animates the body. Energy is superior to mass, because it controls it. Heaven is superior to the earth, because it sustains it. And therefore against this physical universe, there must be a spiritual universe that is superior to it and in control of it; animating it; sustaining it. And just as neither meanings, nor words can exist, unitl "I" exist; neither of these worlds could exist with the ⟪ar:أمر⟫and ⟪ar:أرادۃ⟫of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). 

And so ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫ , then becomes the intermediary and the medium that connects the belief of the heart with action of the limbs.

<!-- section 7 (id=5777, raw_sort=7): Action with the limbs -->

## Action with the Limbs (ʿAmal bi-l-Jawāriḥ)

The first component of IMAN was to witness and testify for all the revelatory propositions that are unseen ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫. How do you do that? Through the knowledge of creation. By deeply reflecting on the creations of the heavens and the earth, and recognizing the one manifesting behind all of creation. Recognizing the one who is "ultimately real" ⟪ar:الحق⟫. Once that belief is established in the heart, the next step is to testify to those realities with the tongue - ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫ - To testify:

⟪ar-quote:اشھد ان لا الہ الا اللہ ; و اشھد ان محمد رسول اللہ؛ و اشھد ان مولانا علی ولی اللہ⟫

I testify there is no God but Allah; I testify that Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is the messenger of Allah; and I testify that Maulana Ali is the WALI of Allah. WALI is a very complex word, and InshaAllah we'll look at it in depth when we study WILAYAH. So ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫ are these 3 testimonies, and then of course the articles of faith:

⟪ar-quote:الجنۃ حق و النار حق⟫

Heaven is real; hellfire is real;

⟪ar-quote:و الموت حق والبعث حق⟫

death is real; rising from the dead is real

⟪ar-quote:والمیزان حق والصراط حق⟫

The scale of deeds is real; the path is real;  

⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:و ان الساعۃ آتیۃُ لا ریب فیہ⟫⟫

And without a doubt, the final moment is coming.

⟪ar-quote:وان اللہ یبعث من فی القبور⟫

And on that day, Allah will raise everyone from their graves.

And then comes the final component,  ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫. To physically "act" in life, as if you really believe in what you testified for. In other words, bring your testimony to life through action. The word ⟪ar:عمل⟫ means "action", and ⟪ar:أرکان⟫ is the plural of ⟪ar:رکن⟫which linguistically means "support". It is the thing that supports you. That's why one of the meanings of ⟪ar:رکن⟫is "pillar", becaue it "supports" the weight of the roof. So metaphorically, ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫means to "act with the limbs"; because limbs (arms and legs) are what support in carrying out our taks. We rely on them!

So now if we look at the complete definition of EMAN:

⟪ar-quote:تصدیق بالجنان؛ قول بالسان؛ عمل بالارکان⟫

To witness the unseen realities with the heart; to testify to those realities with the tongue; and to "support" that belief and testimony through "action".

### Action and its relationship with knowledge

The word for knowledge in the Arabic language is ILM; and the word for action is AMAL; and they're both made up of the same letters [AIN, LAAM, MEEM]. Now if you look at the weight of these letters:

> — *Image text (from image 016; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/016.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

The letter AIN represents the revelatory propositions, and its weight is 70. The LAAM and the MEEM symbolize the rational and the empirical propositions which are 40 and 30. And if add 40 and 30, you get 70. In other words the knowledge of revelatory propositions of the spiritual realm balance out the empirical and rational propositions of the physical realm.

So you have 7 on both sides. Why? Because ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ has 7 syllabels, or 7 distinct parts, and so AIN represent the knowledge of the 7 hidden realities:
⟪ar-quote:الجنۃ حق؛ و النار حق؛ و الموت حق؛ والبعث حق ؛ ⟪ar-quote:والمیزان حق؛ والصراط حق؛ ⟪ar-quote:و ان الساعۃ آتیۃُ لا ریب فیہ⟫⟫⟫

Heaven, hellfire; death; the rising; the scales; the path; and the day of judgment. These 7 hidden realities of the spiritual realm are balanced out by the knowledge of the 7 pillars of ISLAM (WILAYAH, TAHARAH, SALAAT, ZAKAAT, SAUM, HAJJ and JEHAD).

  (image preserved at ../images/017.png)

Now if you look at the word ⟪ar:عمل⟫, it is switching positions of the last two letters. So the weight of both ILM and AML is 140. Which means knowledge must be perfectly balanced with action. All of these amazing realities have been symbolized by just the words ILM and AMAL

### What is the philosophy behind action?

> — *Image text (from image 018; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/018.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Allah says in Surah Al-Rehman:
⟪ar-quote:ٱلرَّحْمَنُ ؛ عَلَّمَ ٱلْقُرْآنَ ؛ خَلَقَ ٱلْإِنسَنَ ؛ عَلَّمَهُ ٱلْبَيَان⟫

The intensely merciful taught the Quran, created man; taught him eloquence. So there are two teachings mentioned here. Teaching of the Quran (⟪ar:عَلَّمَ ٱلْقُرْآنَ⟫) and teaching of articulation (⟪ar:عَلَّمَهُ ٱلْبَيَان⟫); and in between these two teachings, there is (⟪ar:خَلَقَ ٱلْإِنسَنَ⟫), the creation of man. In other words the created human being exists between two teachings: The teaching of Quran and teaching of articulation. In these AYATS, Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) is telling us something about our very nature. ⟪ar:عَلَّمَ⟫is an incredible word in the Arabic language, because it means "to imprint". It means to make an impression. Now if you look at the first tools of writing, they were clay. And the way that impressions were made on them, was by literally pushing in, and making in a ⟪ar:علامۃ⟫or an imprint; like in the Babylonian tablets. You'll see that the text is actually imprinted into them. That is what ⟪ar:عَلَّمَ⟫means، "to imprint". And an imprint is something that cannot be wiped off. It can be covered up, it can be concealed, but it can never be wiped off. Because an imprint becomes part of the essence of the one that takes the imprint.

Now Allah says that he "imprinted" us with the Quran (⟪ar:عَلَّمَ ٱلْقُرْآنَ⟫) ; then created us in this physical world; and then imprinted us again with speech (⟪ar:عَلَّمَهُ ٱلْبَيَان⟫). And what is the most profound speech in human existence? The Quran itself! And this is why Allah refers to his book as BAYAN in the Quran
⟪ar-quote:هَذَا بَيَانٌۭ لِّلنَّاسِ وَهُدًۭى وَمَوْعِظَةٌۭ لِّلْمُتَّقِينَ⟫
This Quran is a clear statement for mankind, a guidance and instruction to those who are pious. So human being exists between two imprints. First, the imprint of the revelatory propositions; then creation of man in this world; and then the imprint of language, or the words of the Quran. Isn't that interesting? Because I would have thought Allah would say

⟪ar-quote:ٱلرَّحْمَنُ .....  ⟪ar-quote:خَلَقَ ٱلْإِنسَنَ.....⟫ عَلَّمَ ٱلْقُرْآنَ ..... عَلَّمَهُ ٱلْبَيَان⟫

The most merciful created human man; taught him Quran and taught him articulation. Allah says NO NO NO! The REHMAN first imprinted the meanings of the Quran in the soul, then created man in the world and then imprinted him with the language of Quran. Now why is that?

The Quran tells us that when Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) created us in the spiritual world, the first thing he did, was make us "witness" him, and then "testify" to that witnessing:

> — *Image text (from image 019; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/019.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

⟪ar-quote:وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ⟫

And when your master created the children of Adam and their descendants
⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ⟫

and made them witess and testify. SHAHADAH in Arabic, means to first witness and *then* testify. Because if you testify without actually witnessing, that testimony is considered a lie. So Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) first made us witness his divine presence, and then he asked us:
⟪ar-quote:أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ؟⟫

"Am I not your master?"
⟪ar-quote:قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ⟫

We replied, "Yes, indeed we testify!". We did not say, "Do you really exist? Are you real? Is there a heaven? Is there a hell? Are there angels? Are there messengers?" NO! That would have been stupid. Because everything is right there! Right in front of us. So when Allah asked us  ⟪ar:أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ؟⟫  "Am I not your master?" All of creation unanimously replied: ⟪ar:بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ⟫  "Yes, indeed we testify!"

So if you look at the components of EMAN, this AYAH mentions the witnessing - ⟪ar:وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ⟫ (which is ⟪ar:تَصدِیقُ بِالِجنَان⟫); followed by a verbal testimony of ⟪ar:بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ⟫ Indeed we testify! which is (⟪ar:قَولُ بِالِّسَان⟫). What's missing? The third component of ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫ is missing. I want you to remember that.

So now the first imprint is done. ⟪ar:ٱلرَّحْمَنُ ؛ عَلَّمَ ٱلْقُرْآنَ⟫. The most merciful imprinted us with the Quran (the revelatory propositions). He made us witness everything and testify to it. Then he created us in this world. ⟪ar:خَلَقَ ٱلْإِنسَنَ⟫.  The word INSAAN comes from ⟪ar:نَسَ⟫which means "to forget". INSAAN means "the one who forgets". So Allah created us in this physical world in a state where we have forgotten everything that occurred in that spiritual realm. Why is that? What's the wisdom behind that? Wouldn't it be so much easier if we remembered everything in this world? We could all immediately say LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH, and be done with it, right? So then why did Allah complicate things so much?

I want you to imagine something. Imagine you are standing before an extremely powerful king! And he asks you, "Do you accept me as a king?". What are you going to say? Even if you don't accept him as king, would you say? Would you say NAH! I don't think so! I don't accept you as my king! Who the hell even made you king in the first place? If you say that, what do you think will happen? So obviously the only sane choice you have, is what? YES! OF COURSE I ACCEPT YOU AS MY KING! WHO ELSE WOULD I ACCEPT AS MY KING?!

Now imagine that we're all standing, not before a worldly king, but before Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). We're standing before the creator and sustainer of kings in the spiritual realm witnessing him. Now he asks, Am I not your master? What did each and everyone of us reply? NO DOUBT! ⟪ar:بلی شھدنا⟫! We totally testify that you are our master! Now is it possible that some were sincere in their testimony and some were not? Some did accept him as their master, and some did not? And amongst the ones who accepted him, could there be levels of sincerity? Some may have entirely and completely accepted him as master. Some may have accepted him as master to a certain degree? Also for those who did not accept him as master in their hearts, could there be degrees of rejection? Some might have totally rejected him in their hearts, while others might have rejected him partially? Could there have been people in that group that were completely confused? I don't know, should I accept him as master, or should I not. Maybe he is master, maybe he's not, I'm not sure. I don't know! My head hurts! Could there be people that might have been on the fence? And could there be degrees in those doubts as well? YES! All of that is possible. But what did each and everyone say in response? ⟪ar:بلی شھدنا⟫! We totally testify that you are our master!

So now Allah (AL-ALEEM: the all knowing), based on his knowledge of the unseen, he starts handing out rewards and punishments. Some go to heaven, some are thrown in hellfire. The one's going in hellfire, what would they say? Why am I being thrown in hellfire? I said YES! just like she said YES! Why does she go to heaven and I go to hell? Allah says, because you do not see me as your master! You lied. You testified but you didn't mean it. The guy says, "how can you say that? I said YES just like the rest. How do I know that the ones you're housing in heaven also didn't reject you? You are the All-Knowing, I'm not! How do I know that's what's happening. How do I know you're not favoring him over others. You want me to just take your word for it?". You see the problem here?

Another scenario: Let's say you're one of the guys who make it to heaven. But you're in the 50th rank of heaven and your friend is in the 10th rank of heaven. And you're like, "Hey! Wait a minute! Why does he get the 10th rank and I get such a low rank? He said Yes and I said yes! I even shook my head, he didn't even shake his head!". Allah says, because the degree and the sincerity of him accepting me as master was 40 times greater than yours. So he deserves that rank!". What will you think? I don't know that! How do I know that? What if it's not? Am I just to take your word for it?". Again the same problem, you see?

Think about this in the worldly sense. In school, at the end of the term, without any examination, without grading results, the teacher based on her knowledge, simply promotes some students to the next grade and fails some. How do you think that'll work out? What if a judge, without holding a trial, passes his verdict on a case and sends some people to prison and sets others free. How would that work out? Without us witnessing the trial; without us witnessing the examination results, who's justice or fairness would be in doubt? The teacher, the judge.

So Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) made us witness him, and testify, and he knew exactly what was in everyone's heart. And so then in his vast wisdom, he created this universe, and reflected the same divine principles that were "imprinted" within us in the spiritual realm. He then created us all at the same level; ⟪ar:خلق الانسان⟫ . He made us forget everything that we witnessed in that spiritual realm. He wiped the slate clean, but then he sent us his BAYAAN (⟪ar:علمہُ البیان⟫). He imprinted us again with the language of Quran, that reveals and unveils the realities of the spiritual realm. Which realities? the ones have already been imprinted with; so that we could recognize them when we see them manifesting in the ALAM, and once again testify "through" action! Testify what?
⟪ar-quote:أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ؟⟫

"Am I not your master?"
⟪ar-quote:قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ⟫

We replied, "Yes, indeed we testify!".

So the idea is that the one who was sincere in his testimony in the spiritual realm, when he hears the words of the Quran, will immediately be reminded of that primoridial testimony in the spiritual realm; with the same sincerity and conviction that he possessed then, and accept Allah as his master to the same degree as he did then! The wisdom behind our physical creation in the ALAM; the wisdom behind the reminder of the Quran; is for us to prove the sincerity of our primordial claim, that indeed Allah is our master. And this is why, the one who accepted him in his heart back then, will accept him again in this world; and the one who rejected him back then, will reject him again in this world. ⟪ar:ما کان سیکون⟫; What happened then, shall happen again. But what's incredible about this opportunity is that through this mechanism, Allah also gave us all a chance to redress our wrongs. So If we rejected Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) as our master in the spiritual realm, we now have the opportunity to correct that mistake. If we accepted him as master with a lower degree of sincerity, we now have the opportunity to strive and achieve a higher degree of sincerity.

---

Do you remember in the primoridial witnessing and testifying one component was missing. What was missing? عمل بالارکان. Why was it missing? Because the only way to measure the sincerity of someone's intentions and claims, is through action! I can believe in my heart that I love somone; I can verbally announce my love to the person; but the only thing that can prove the sincerity of my love to that person is - what I do in action. So now we branching off into two forms of sincerity. There is sincerity of speech; and sincerity of action

**What is sincerity of speech?**

Maulana Ahmad (AS), our 9th Imam, gives this beautiful example in his book ⟪ar:رسائل اخوان الصفاء⟫. He says a group of men board a ship. And as they board, they recite the traditional prayer with their tongues:
⟪ar-quote:لا حول ولا قوۃ الا باللہ العلی العظیم⟫

There is no power and no strength execept that of Allah the All-mighty. 

The Imam AS writes, that they make this claim with their tongues, that there is no power and strength except that of Allah, but in their hearts, they believe in the weather man's predictions. In reality they put their trust in the strength and sturdiness of the ship. They put their faith in the skills and capabilities of the captain of the ship.

Now the ship begins sailing and when it reaches the middle of the ocean, the weather begins to change, and they start seeing signs of an impending storm. And now they realize that the weather man's prediction was wrong. And then the storm begins, and the ship starts shaking like a leaf; things are breaking all around them; equipment starts malfunctioning; and now they see that the even the captain looks perturbed and frightened. They can now really see, that this ship is going to sink. And they also realize that now no one except Allah can save them from drowning. So what do they say? They recite
⟪ar-quote:لا حول ولا قوۃ الا باللہ العلی العظیم⟫

There is no power and no strength execept that of Allah the All-mighty. 

They recite the exact same words as they did when they were boarding the ship. But this time, it is completely different. This time they have no faith in the weather man's prediction. They have no reliance on the sturdiness of the ship. There is no trust in the skills of the captain. They only trust they now have is on Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). The Imam says, this second time when they recite this verse,  ⟪ar:لا حول ولا قوۃ الا باللہ العلی العظیم⟫, they are perfectly sincere in their speech.

This is an excellent story for us to measure the sincerity of our claims. When we say we love Allah, when we say:
⟪ar-quote:الحمد للہ رب العالمین۔ الرحمن الرحیم۔ مالک یوم الدین؛ ایاک نعبد و ایاک نستعین⟫

How sincere are we in those claims? Do we accept him as our RABB, or do we accept our house, our jobs, our posessions as our Rabb. Are we able to remember that he is the intensely merciful and the constantly merciful when calamities befalls us? The way we are living in this world, the choices we make, the priorities we make, are they aligned with the fact that we believe he is the owner and king of the day when our debt of submission will fall due? Are we sincere in our claim of ⟪ar:ایاک نعبد⟫, it is only you that we enslave ourselves to! Or are we enslaved to this DUNIYA, and our passions and our desires? When we say  ⟪ar:ایاک نستعین⟫, do we really rely on his help alone, or do we rely on the help of our friends and family? What is the purity and sincerity of our claim, every single day when we recite the Fatiha in our prayers?

Because purity of speech is confirmed by action! Without action, claims are just empty words! They mean nothing!

---

This is why Rasul Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) once asked a companion

⟪ar-quote:کیف اصبَحتُ؟⟫

How have you woken up? He replied

⟪ar-quote:اصبَحتُ مؤمِناً حقَّا⟫

I have woken up a true believer! In other words, something happened to this companion in which he went from a MUMIN to a MUMIN HAQQAN. Because in that statement he is qualifying his state of EMAAN. In other words he's saying: There is a qualitative difference between my state of IMAN this morning than other mornings. And Rasul Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said, Think about what you're saying! Because every reality has a proof! So what is the proof of your reality? And then this companion gives a description; that I am experiencing JANNAH as its right here; and I can hear the people moaning from the agony of hell as if I'm right there. In other words he was in a state of experience! And Rasul Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said…..

⟪ar-quote:عرَفتَ ..... فَالزَمْ⟫

You have MAARIFA! You have true knowledge! So hold tight to it because you can lose that if you're not careful.

---

A man travelled a long distance and came to Maulana Ali (AS) when he was standing near a burning furnace. This man says to him:

⟪ar-quote:أِنِّی اُحِبُّکَ بالصدق⟫

I sincerly and truly love you! I have heard all about your miracles and your station with Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala); and I've travelled a very long distance just to meet you out of pure love. Maulana Ali says to him, "go sit in that burning furnace". The man says, I won't do that! Maulana Ali says to him

⟪ar-quote:أَحبِب غَیرِی⟫

Go love someone else! In other words, if you're not going to obey me, then that's not true love! I don't need that kind of love. Go love someone else! Right then another man comes there and says the same thing. He says, I have travelled a long distance to meet you. I am one of your true شیعۃ. Maulana Ali says the same thing. Go and sit in that burning furnace! This man instantly drops the bag he was carrying on his shoulder and walks right into the furnace. The second he steps in, the fire turns into flowers. This incident is quoted in Dayam Al-Islam! In other words, if you say you've heard about my powers and station with Allah. If you truly know who I am then you will obey what I tell you do. You would trust me in what I tell you to do!

---

So the proof of sincerity is action! What was the question Allah asked us?

⟪ar-quote:أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ؟⟫

"Am I not your master?" What is the relationship between a master and a slave? Servitude! Obedience! Doing what the master says! And so ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫ is where we go and sit in the burning furnace (metaphorically speaking). If you truly believe, and if your testimony of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫is true! Then prove it to me in action! Balance the testimony of those 7 realities with the practices of these 7 pillars of ISLAM.

---

Just look at the wisdom in this design, SubhanAllah! In the spiritual realm, I had no idea about your sincerity, and you had no idea about my sincerity, right? But in this physical realm, the manner in which I practice ISLAM is visible to you; and the way in which you practice ISLAM is visible to you. You can tell whether I believe or not; and to what degree I believe based on how I practice my ISLAM. But let's say even if I am awesome at faking it, every act that I do [good or bad] is being recorded in a book. There are two angels, one on each shoulder recording every good and bad act that I do. Why write in a book? Because verbal claims can be denied in a court of law, but written text cannot be refuted. It becomes a binding document. And on the day of judgment, Allah says each person will be handed his own book of deeds. Not book of verbal comments, but book of actions. And then they will be asked to read it, and verify [testify] that what's written in it is accurate. Do you see the wisdom behind Allah's justice. Not a single soul will be able to claim injustice, because each and every soul will be asked to sign their own document of deeds.

⟪ar-quote:يَوْمَئِذٍۢ تُعْرَضُونَ لَا تَخْفَىٰ مِنكُمْ خَافِيَةٌۭ⟫

That day shall come when you will be judged, and on that day not a single secret will be hidden. In other words your book of deeds will show every single thing that you did in this world.

⟪ar-quote:فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِىَ كِتَبَهُۥ بِيَمِينِهِۦ فَيَقُولُ هَآؤُمُ ٱقْرَءُوا۟ كِتَبِيَهْ⟫

Then as for him who will be given his book in his right hand will say to others: "Look! Look! Read my Record! You know when you pass an exam and the teacher hands out your answer sheet with that big A+ in a circle at the top in red! That paper for some reason keeps slipping and falling in front of others to pick up and hand it to you, as they see your grade. Oh I'm sorry! How clumsy of me! You know what I'm talking about? You can't want to show your result to your friends! You're so proud of that score! Look what I've accomplished!! And they say, WOW! how did you do that? How did you get such an awesome score?

⟪ar-quote:إِنِّى ظَنَنتُ أَنِّى مُلَقٍ حِسَابِيَهْ ‎⟫

Because I believed that one day I shall meet have to account for my actions

⟪ar-quote:فَهُوَ فِى عِيشَةٍۢ رَّاضِيَةٍۢ⟫

So he shall then live a pleasurable life

⟪ar-quote:‏فِى جَنَّةٍ عَالِيَةٍۢ ‎⟫

In a lofty Paradise,

⟪ar-quote:‏قُطُوفُهَا دَانِيَةٌۭ⟫

There will be bunches of fruits hanging low before him, that he'll easily be able to access them.

⟪ar-quote:كُلُوا۟ وَٱشْرَبُوا۟ هَنِيٓـًٔۢا بِمَآ أَسْلَفْتُمْ فِى ٱلْأَيَّامِ ٱلْخَالِيَة⟫

Eat and drink at your leisure, as a reward for all the good that you did in your earthly life

⟪ar-quote:وَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِىَ كِتَبَهُۥ بِشِمَالِهِ⟫

But as for him who will be given his book in his left hand,

⟪ar-quote:فَيَقُولُ يَلَيْتَنِى لَمْ أُوتَ كِتَبِيَهْ ‎ ‎⟫

He will say: "I wish I never had to see this horrible book of deeds

⟪ar-quote:وَلَمْ أَدْرِ مَا حِسَابِيَهْ⟫

And I wish I never had to account for these deeds

⟪ar-quote:يَلَيْتَهَا كَانَتِ ٱلْقَاضِيَةَ⟫

I wish, my death in the world would have been the end of existence!! Imagine that! Words of the Quran. Today there are people that say, that there is no after life. Once you're dead its dust to dust ashes to ashes. There is no resurrection; there is no accountability. Allah says on that that day they will wish that was true, just to not face the horrors of their evil acts

⟪ar-quote:‎ ‏مَآ أَغْنَىٰ عَنِّى مَالِيَهْۜ ‎⟫

All my wealth that I collected in my life cannot help me today

⟪ar-quote:هَلَكَ عَنِّى سُلْطَنِيَهْ ‎‏⟫

My arrogance has destroyed me today. I just cannot deny or falsify this document. And then Allah says to the angels.....

⟪ar-quote:خُذُوهُ فَغُلُّوهُ⟫

Grab him! Chain him!

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ ٱلْجَحِيمَ صَلُّوهُ⟫

Then throw him in the blazing fire

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ فِى سِلْسِلَةٍۢ ذَرْعُهَا سَبْعُونَ ذِرَاعًۭا فَٱسْلُكُوهُ⟫

Shackle him with a chain made up of 70 links. Why?

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ لَا يُؤْمِنُ بِٱللَّهِ ٱلْعَظِيمِ⟫

Because he did not believe in Allah, the magnificent. Notice the word IMAN is used. And its not IMAN in heaven, hell, angels, messengers, resurrection. None of those are mentioned. Just that he did not believe in Allah. Because once you believe in Allah, believing in the rest just comes naturally.

And so on the final day, when ranks are being distributed based on sincerity, neither you, nor I will have a problem with any of it. And there will be no blame on the justice and the REHMANIYAH of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). All blame that day will fall on the person himself; to which he will testify and sign the dotted line before seeing his rewards or punishment. Because it's all going to be based on physical evidence of action and practice.

Now what's interesting about "action"; and this is something we learn from studying this ALAM, that aciton must be consistent! If you observe the phenomenon that occur in this world, one thing we can see very clearly, is that the principles of cause of effects are very consistent. Seasons recur in the same pattern; Water always flows downhill; Sun rises in the east, sets in the west; phases of the moon. Everything that we find in the ALAM, everthing that we find in Allah's ACT are consistent. So one of the proofs of sincerity is not just action, but consistent action. If you wish to measure yourself about the sincerity of your testimony; of your ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ , the easiest way to do it, is to look at the consistency of your actions. Because a slave who sincerly recognizes Allah as his master, will not do what the master says occassionally; or when it its convenient to him. He will always obey him - consistently. The one who recognizes Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) as the true messenger of Allah, will not just follow his teachings just when it suits him. So in the final analysis, consistency of ones actions serves as the proof of ones sincerity about his claim and intentions.

The companions were people that worked in such a powerful experiential ISLAM. They were living these truths. Maulana Ali (AS) said, "I never saw anything, except that I saw Allah before it, and after it and within it". In other words, he was witnessing the actions of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) in creation. The idea that not a single leaf  falls, except with the knowledge of Allah.  So being aware of Allah in that way, in a very real presence, was is permanent state. These people didn't have an ISLAM like we do. For them it was not informational; for them it was completely experiential. They didn't see these DAYAM as separate acts of worship; they saw them all as one.

Now look at how all of this comes together so beautifully. Allah created us in the spiritual realm and made us witness him and testify in speech! Where did he make us do that in the hidden realm! Where did he send us to prove the sincerity of our witnessing and our claim? In the physical world.

For us as believers, what is IMAN?

⟪ar-quote:تصدیق بالجنان؛ قول بالسان؛⟫

To witness the unseen realities with the heart; and to testify to those realities with the tongue. Where do these happen? Inside us? Within our spiritual realm? Where do prove the sincerity of our belief and our claim?

⟪ar-quote:عمل بالارکان⟫

Through action in the physical world. SubhanAllah! How incredible is that?

---

---

<!-- section 8 (id=5778, raw_sort=8): COMPLETE REVIEW -->

## Complete Review — Synthesis of Heart, Tongue, and Limbs

According to HADEES JIBRAEEL, Rasul Allah(S) described ISLAM as: in the form of a man, and asks him 4 questions. He asks him what is ISLAM; what is IMAN; what is IHSAN and he asks about

⟪ar-quote:الْإِسْلَامُ أَنْ تَشْهَدَ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَیْهِ وَسَلَّمَ⟫

Islam is to witness that there is no God but Allah, and Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is the Messenger of Allah;

⟪ar-quote:وَتُقِیمَ الصَّلَاةَ⟫

And that you establish the prayer

⟪ar-quote:وَتُؤْتِیَ الزَّکَاةَ⟫

that you give the alms;

⟪ar-quote:وَتَصُومَ رَمَضَانَ⟫

that you fast the month of Ramadan;

⟪ar-quote:وَتَحُجَّ الْبَیْتَ إِنْ اسْتَطَعْتَ إِلَیْهِ سَبِیلًا⟫

and you perform pilgrimage to the House if you are capable of travel.

**Why did Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) describe ISLAM as a set of practices intead of a set of concepts?**

---

**What was the experience  or Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)'s ISLAM?**

- IQRA vs ISRA

- Tahannus (40 years)

- Difference between divine and demonic experience

- ISLAM began with constriction of IQRA and ended with expansion of ISRA (MERAAJ)

**What is the lesson we gain from  Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)'s experience?**

**What are the 4 linguistic meanings of ISLAM?**

- Islam as submission and surrender of free will

- Islam as peace and safety

- Islam as the religion of all prophets

- Islam as the religion of prophet Muhammad

**Why are the 7 practices of ISLAM called the pillars of ISLAM?**

**What is the meaning of IMAN?**

**Witnessing of the heart**

- AQL vs NAQL

- Revelatory propositions testified through the study of rational and empirical propositions

**Articulation of the tongue**

- To unveil the hidden realities through speech - knowledge (others)

- To testify and commit (self)

- Has properties of both components.

**Act with the limbs**

- What is the philosophy behind action?

⟪ar-quote:أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ؟⟫

- To prove the primoridial testimony through action

- so that there is no blame on Allah's justice

---

Now ISLAM, in a generic sense, is seen as the overriding rubric, under which ISLAM, IMAAN and IHSAAN are subsumed. In Arabic semantics, most synonyms (called مُترَادِفات) are telescopic in nature. Just like a telescope can extend, in that all the individual discs separate out; it can also contract, in which each disc gets overlapped by the outer disc. So one of the basic principles of Arabic semantics, is that when such terms are used, they say:

اِذا اجْتَمَعَت أِفتَرَقَت..... واِذا افْتَرَقَت أِجتَمَعَت..... 

When these terms occur together in a single context, they separate out in meaning; and each word takes on its own particular meaning. But if they are used in isolation, then one term takes on the meanings of the other terms. In other words, the outer term bring all of the inner meanings together.

 

So when we talk about ISLAM in a general way, it can take on the meanings of IMAN and IHSAN as well. But when these terms are discussed together in a single context, then each term takes on very specific meanings and characteristics.

After defining IMAAN, Imam Jaffar AlSadiq (AS) says, Know! that IMAAN is not just belief; it is not just a declaration; it is not just an action. It is a combination of all three things; where the tongue declares what the heart believes; and the limbs act according to what the tongue declared. This would be considered a "perfect" IMAAN. Just as a human being would not be considered perfectly rational, unless he posessed all 3 things: the AQL (the intellect),  NAFS (the soul) and ARKAAN (the body). Anything less and that human being would be considered defective. Similarly until these three comonents of faith: witnessing, articulation and action, until they come together, one's faith is considered defective in the eyes of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala).

 

This is why Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) says in the Quran:

⟪ar-quote:وَٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ أَصْحَبُ ٱلْجَنَّةِ ۖ هُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ⟫

And those who have IMAAN, and do good deeds; they are the people of JANNAH; they will live in it for ever.
