Quran is filled with such ayats, where Allah calls out to people who believe and do good deeds. If you study the ayah carefully, it does not say, ⟪ar:وَٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَٱلَّذِينَ عَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ⟫; those who believe and those who do good deeds. If it did that, then the ayah would be talking about two groups of people. One that believes and the other that does good deeds. NO! Allah says:

⟪ar:وَٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ⟫; Those who believe *and* do good deeds. So the evidence of faith, IS good deeds. And this is why there is no knowledge without action; and there is no action without knowledge. They both go hand in hand. This is why Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said:

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ .....  دخل الجنۃ⟫

The one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH has entered JANNAH. People said that's really easy.

One of the beauties of our creedal formula..... 

اشھد ان لا الہ الا اللہ

is that it is not just a testimony. Because SHAHADAH means to testify, but it also means "to witness"; and that is why the beauty of Islam is that it has enabled the proposition to also be experienced. We can say the SHAHADAH in two ways.....  We can say.....

 اشھد ان لا الہ الا اللہ

I can say: I TESTIFY that there is no god but Allah; or I can say: I SEE with my intellect, by reflecting on the creation of the heavens and the earth, that there is no god but Allah. That Arabic word SHAHADAH holds both those meanings. So it's not just a proposition, it is also that personal level of experience

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ .....  مُخلِصاً ..... دخل الجنۃ⟫

The one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH sincerely has entered JANNAH. Why did he say it twice? He could have just said it once and be done with it right? The first is the JANNAH of ISLAM, and the second is the JANNAH of IMAN. There are no levels in ISLAM; but there are levels in IKHLAAS [sincerity] of IMAN. And these are what Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) refers to in SURAH REHMAN when he says.....

⟪ar-quote:وَلِمَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ جَنَّتَانِ⟫

For the one who fears the station of his Lord, there will be two Gardens for him. That's the garden of ISLAM and the garden of IMAN. Why gardens?

Because the soul finds peace and tranquility in a garden. And so ISLAM and IMAN are the two gardens of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) where the soul finds peace and ease.

Now what's sincerity? The Arabic word for sincerity is ⟪ar:أخلاص⟫, which comes from the word ⟪ar:خَلُصَ⟫, which means pure, clear or free from mixture. That's where you get the word ⟪ar:خالص⟫which means pure; of the best quality. ‏ Maulana Ali (AS) says

⟪ar-quote:اَلأِخْلاَصْ یَکُونُ بِہِ اَلْخَلاَصْ⟫

Sincerity is that which brings about salvation

⟪ar-quote:وَ اَلأِخْلاَصْ ثَمَرَۃُ الیَقِین⟫

Sincerity is the fruit of conviction. Fruit is the last thing that shows up on a tree. And the purpose of planting the tree in the first place was what? Its fruit! So the consistent effort of developing conviction through knowledge produces the fruit of sincerity.

⟪ar-quote:وَاَلأِخْلاَصْ ثَمَرَۃُ العِباَدَۃْ⟫

Sincerity is the fruit of all worship. Again, consistent worship, with a clear understanding of why we are worshipping, who we are worshipping, results in sincerity

⟪ar-quote:واَلأِخْلاَصْ ھِیَ خَیرُ العَمَل⟫

And sincerity is the best of all actions. Of all the "actions or practices" that fall under the category of عمل بالارکان, sincerity is the summit. It is the at the peak of the mountain.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ یَکُونُ خَیرُ العَمَل اِلاَّ بِالعِلم⟫

And the best of actions cannot be practiced without knowledge

⟪ar-quote:وَاَجَلُّ اَلْعِلْم، اَلعِلْمُ التَّوحِید⟫

And the greatest of all knowledge, is the knowledge of Tawheed. The oneness of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). The more we are able to witness the one manifesting behind all creations, the more sincerity we will be able to achive. In other words, sincerity is directly proportional to our knowledge of Tawheed.

And the fact that ⟪ar:اخلاص⟫means to make pure, it means that we are in an impure state. Our love of Allah is mixed with the love of DUNIYA. So the more knowledge of Allah's TAWHEED we gain, the more it will reflect in our convictions and practices of worship, and the more sincere we will become in our efforts.

<!-- section 9 (id=5771, raw_sort=9): Tree and Root Structure -->

## The Tree-and-Root Structure of Faith

Concepts of USOOL AL-DEEN

In todays session, I want to provide some clarity for these terms of TAWHEED, IMAN and ISLAM. We'll look at how these 3 terms are related to each other. Are they dependent on each other, or are they independent of each other? So a different way of looking at this is: Are ISLAM, IMAN and TAWHEED, three different children? Or is it one single child with 3 different features?

It's actually one child, with three different features that grow and develop together.

> — *Image text (from image 020; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/020.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

This diagram might seem a bit confusing right now, but it will become clear as we progress and work through an example InshaAllah. For now I just want to explain how these 3 terms are related to one another.

TAWHEED is the concept of the absolute uniqueness of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), that is articulated through the creedal formula: ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫. Linguistically the word TAWHEED, means "to make one"; or "to unify". TAWHEED is make our ILAH, our deity, our passions ALLAH. Because we have many different ILAH. Our desires are our ILAH, our passions, our goals, our jobs, our houses, our cards, our money, we have a *lot* of deities that we depend on. TAWHEED is to deny and reject them all and unify everything within the one and only ILAH which is Allah. TAWHEED is the very first stage.

This TAWHEED then develops or progresses into IMAN, which is a composition of 3 things. The first is ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫ (witnessing and testifying for the hidden revelatory propositions with conviction). The second is ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫ (Articulating that conviction through a commitment). The third component is ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫ , bringing to life, that belief and the commitment in the form of action. And those actions are the 7 practices of DA'IM AL-ISLAM.

Quran explains this concept, by giving us the metaphore of a tree and a good word. Allah says:

**http://quran.com/14/24**
⟪ar-quote:أَلَمْ تَرَ كَيْفَ ضَرَبَ ٱللَّهُ مَثَلًۭا كَلِمَةًۭ طَيِّبَةًۭ كَشَجَرَةٍۢ طَيِّبَةٍ⟫

Have you not seen how Allah sets forth the example of a good word like a good tree?
⟪ar-quote:أَصْلُهَا ثَابِتٌۭ وَفَرْعُهَا فِى ٱلسَّمَآءِ⟫

Its root are firmly set in the ground and its branch are in the heaven

In this ayah Allah mentions 3 things. He mentions ⟪ar:شجر⟫which is the tree. Then he says, ⟪ar:أَصْلُهَا ثَابِتٌۭ⟫ it's roots are firmly grounded; ⟪ar:وَفَرْعُهَا فِى ٱلسَّمَآءِ⟫ and its branches rise to the heavens. So we have 3 things, the tree, its roots and its branches. So in the Quranic sense, our religions framework explains the principles of IMAN and ISLAM, as what's called: ⟪ar:أُصُولَ الدِّن⟫ ; the roots of religion; and  ⟪ar:فُرُوع الدِّن⟫ ; which are the branches of religion. So we're going to study this metaphore of a tree, with its roots and branches to see how it relates to one's spiritual development.

**Seed**

Where does a tree come from? It comes from a seed. You cannot have a tree without a seed! What is a seed? It is the essence of the tree; because it contains within it the entire tree in its dormant form. The *entire" tree, with all of its roots, trunk, branches and fruits, exist within the seed in a passive state. All that is needed is for that potential to be activated. Isn't that true? What's common between a seed and a human being? We also come from a seed, which is the sperm. The sperm (just like the seed) contains within it the entire human form in a passive state.

In the spiritual sense TAWHEED (⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ - There is no god execpt Allah) is symbolized by a seed. Why? Because the testimony of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH contains the entire spiritual form of the perfect momin in its passive state. If I asked you to compare a regular MOMIN, to a perfect MOMIN; such as Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) or Maulana Ali? What scale would you use? It would be the scale of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH. The difference between us an them, is that our TAWHEED is imperfect [flawed] whereas their TAWHEED is perfect and complete; it is flawless. They have fully and completely activated their potential of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH, whereas we are in the process of gradually activating it, little by little.

So all human beings [Muslims or non-Muslims] are born with the seeds of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫within their souls. This is because of that primorideal witnessing that occurred in the spiritual realm before we were created in this world. So every human being is a potential MOMIN. All that is needed is the activation of that potential.

**Environment**

How do you activate this dormant potential of a seed? By providing it with an environment that is conducive for its growth. For a seed, that environment is the soil or the earth. For a sperm that evironment is its mothers womb. Now what is a conducive environment to activate the seeds of TAWHEED? It is a teacher. A teacher takes his student within his care, just like the earth takes the seed within itself; just as a mother's womb takes the sperm within itself. And so a good teacher becomes the earth or the soil for the nurturing of the human soul.

**Importance of permission (Digression)**

Do the seed and earth make this decision to unite by themselves, or is there someone else involved? Does the seed say to the earth, "I want to turn into a tree, so please take me within your care!"? Or does the earth say to the seed, "I want to activate your potential and so I want you come under my care"? Do they mutually decide on this union, or does someone else decide this union for them? It is always the farmer who brings the two together. Why? Because the farmer knows, which seed need what type of soil to grow in. The farmer knows which enviroment is conducive to the growth of the seed, because he posesses knowledge of both entities - the seed and the soil.

This is why, the selection of a teacher for a student has to come from an elder. Because the elder is like the farmer, who not only understands the capabilities of the student, he also knows the level of the teachers knowledge. He understands what level of knowledge will benefit the student in the best possible way. And so he selects a teacher who has the necessary knowledge, and brings them both together. And then he doesn't just leave them on their own; he oversees the entire training process, just as a farmer constantly monitors the growth and development of a tree.

This is an extremely important aspect of spiritual development that is completely ignored today. Today within our JAMAAT, there are so many people teaching groups of people without taking permission from our elders. People just decide amongst themselves to come together in this "teacher student" relationship, and this is disasterous! What do you call plants, that unite with the soil, without the explicit decision or supervision of a farmer? They are called weeds! And what do you eventually have to do with weeds? You have to uproot them. So learning spiritual knowledge from anyone, without the explicit permission of an elder is disasterous for the spiritual growth of a student. Why? Because the earth in which the seeds are being deposited, has not been tested for nutrients; it has not been tested for deficiencies; and those deficiencies have not been removed. What happens when even the most perfect seeds are planted within an earth that is deficient of healthy nutrients? They inhibit the growth of that plant. So a teacher whose knowledge has not been tested and sanctioned by an elder; he becomes the worst possible environment for that students spiritual development. Because one: that person does not possess the proper knowledge himself to give to the students; and two: his lack of knowledge or misconceptions then get transferred to the students. And so this is something to be very careful about! This is why I have Javeed bhai as part of all my groups - for accountability

What have we established so far? All human beings are born with the seeds of TAWHEED within their souls in a dormant state. In order to activate that potential, an elder places that person in the care and training of a sanctioned teacher; just as a farmer places the seeds in the proper soil, and then oversees the entire developmental process. He monitors the growth of the plant, as well as the health of the soil. Because if you think about it, the farmer waters the soil you see? He does not water the seed (he waters the soil). The effort of the farmer is focused on the soil, because he knows that if he prepares the soil properly, the seeds will naturally grow. Similarly the elder gives his knowledge to the teacher, and not the student directly. He water's the soil.

**Teacher filters knowledge**

Now what does the soil do? It takes in [or absorbs] all the water that the farmer puts into it; but it does not give it all to the seeds. It only gives the seed what it requires. The soil channels its nutrients to the seed through that water. Similarly the teacher takes in the knowledge from his elder, but does not transfer it all to his students. He gives them only what they need; and in the amount that they can handle. He filters that knowledge, brining it down to the level that is appropriate for the student. So that the student can understand and digest that information. In other words the teacher, by providing his knowledge to the student, begins to activate the dormant TAWHEED within the heart of the student.

**Process of germination**

How does the process of germination begin? What is the first thing that comes out? The first thing that breaks out of the seed is the roots, and its direction is downward. Roots continuously grow deeper into the earth. So now as the training and guidance of the teacher continues, those dormant seeds of لا الہ الا اللہ, begin to gradually activate within the student; and IMAN begins to develop, which is symbolized by the roots. Where does this development of IMAN takes place? In the students heart, which is a hidden realm. No one can see another persons IMAN developing or taking root. Just as no one can see the roots growing under the soil. The deeper the roots grow into the earth, the more nutrients it is able to provide to the seed. The more the student learns from his teacher, the more he is able to activate the potential of his TAWHEED. This is the first component of faith: ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫

**The embryo breaks the shell**

Once the roots break out and spread into the earth, they begin drawing more and more nourishement for the embryow within the seed. The embryo begins to develop until there comes a point where the shell can no longer contain it; and the embryo breaks out of that containment in the form of a shoot, and begins an upward journey towards sunlight.

As the student increases in his knowledge, his IMAN begins to grow and get stronger. Until it reaches a point where his heart can no longer contain it, and that IMAN breaks out on his tongue. His IMAN (faith), bursts out of his heart and begins to flow on his tongue in the form of the praise and glory of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). This is a point of transition in the believers life. Belief has now transcended into speech, which is the second component of faith: ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫.

**Plant begins to grow**

And now the shoot breaks through the soil and sprout out into the open world above. Now now only does it continue to draw food through the roots, it now also becomes capable of generating its own food directly from sunlight. In other words, it can now perform its own action; it gains the ability to act. And from this point on, as long as it keeps getting water, the right temprature and enough sunlight, it will continue to grow and develop.

For the believer, now his faith and knowledge has increased to the point where his speech begins to translate into action. Just as the plant comes out of hiding and manifests its existence to the physical world; the believers faith and speech begin to mainfest in the world through action. He begins practicing the 7 pillars of ISLAM. This is the 3rd and final component of IMAN: ⟪ar:العمل بالارکان⟫.

**Growth of roots is directly proportional to the growth of the plant**

Now let's think about the rate of growth for the roots in comparison to the plant. Do the roots grow out completely, before the plant begins growing? No! The roots only grow to a point before the stem of the plant shoots out. And then as the root keeps growing, the plant keeps growing as well. In other words, the rate at which the roots grow is directly proportional to the rate at which the plant grows. In other words, the more the roots grow, the more the plant grows. Also, does a stem first come out of the soil, or does the entire tree show up all of a sudden? Only a small tiny little shoot raises its head out of the soil.

Similarly with a believer, as his IMAN grows through the knowledge of his teacher, his ISLAM grows along with it. The more knowledge he acquires, the more his IMAN increases which increases his ISLAM accordingly. And just as the plant begins with a weak stem, a believer begins with a weak ISLAM, which grows and develops over a lifetime

**This does not go by age. There are many people whose TAWHEED get activated when they're in their 40s.**

> — *Image text (from image 021; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/021.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

**Recap**

So you can see how identical both these processes are. The developmental stages of a seed are perfectly corelated to the developmental stages of a person's IMAN. The plant begins with a seed containing the complete essence of a tree. A potential MOMIN begins with the seeds of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH within his essence, that contains within it the entire structure of his IMAN, ISLAM and IHSAN. Once the farmer places the seed in the proper soil; or an elder places the student under the guidance of a sanctioned teacher, the germination process begins for both. Through the nurturing of the soil, the first thing that breaks out of the seed are the roots. And the first thing that develops through the proper guidance of one's teacher, is IMAN (orfaith). Roots keep nourishing the embryo, just as IMAN keeps feeding and strengthning the conviction of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH. Eventually, the embryo develops to a point where it can no longer be contained within its shell; just as the IMAN of the believer, reaches a point where it can no longer be contained in the heart; and it begins flowing on his tonuge in the form of speech - through praise and glory of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). Next, the plant breaks through its dark hidden world and shoots out into the open world. Until now the roots were the only source of nutrition for it, but now it wants to act. It wants to create its own nutrition from sunlight. Similarly the believer reaches his final stage, where his belief is no longer simply hidden in his heart, or revealed through his speech, he brings it to life in action through the 7 practices of ISLAM. And then as the believers IMAN increases through knowledge, over a period of a lifetime, to activate the full potential of that dormant TAWHEED that he was created with. SubhanAllah!

Now if you think about the process of child birth, it is exctly same. While the fetus is in the womb of its mother, the womb does all the work of providing nutrition to it. But as it grows there comes a point where it needs to come into the world and begin to "use" or put to "work" the organs and limbs that were developed within the womb. The process is exactly identical!

Look at the developmental stages of a "good word". Good words begins with a good intention hidden in the depths of ones heart. That intention, nourished by pure knowledge, develops over time and reaches a point where it now has to be expressed. The person begins articulating his intentions. And then there comes a time when speech is no longer enough, and one begins "doing" or "acting" upon ones intention and speech. SubhanAllah!

We should all take a moment, to really appreciate the beauty of this marvellous design. Just think about the spectacular design of this amazing designer. He used the exact same template for development, for completely disparate and disconnected entities. What has a tree got to do with a word; and what does a word have to do with a believer? There's absolutely no connection between them; and yet they develop and function in exactly the same way. And so Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) says:
⟪ar-quote:أَلَمْ تَرَ كَيْفَ ضَرَبَ ٱللَّهُ مَثَلًۭا كَلِمَةًۭ طَيِّبَةًۭ كَشَجَرَةٍۢ طَيِّبَةٍ⟫

Have you not seen how Allah sets forth the example of a good word like a good tree?
⟪ar-quote:أَصْلُهَا ثَابِتٌۭ وَفَرْعُهَا فِى ٱلسَّمَآءِ⟫

Its root are firmly set in the ground and its branch are in the heaven
⟪ar-quote:تُؤْتِىٓ أُكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍۭ بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهَا⟫

Giving its fruit in all seasons by the permission of its master.

Now what is he talking about here? What has giving fruit in all seasons have to do with the IMAN and ISLAM of a believer? Consistencey! Integrity! Dependency! A good tree is consistent, people can depend all year on it for its fruits. A good word is consistent with the original intention and the subsequent actions. A believers ISLAM is consistent with his IMAN. The belief in his heart matches the speech of his tongue; and they're both consistent with his actions. There is no discrepancy between them. His intention is LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH; his speech is LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH and his action are LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH. In other words, all manifestations of his TAWHEED are in harmony. Have you ever thought about the shape of the roots and how they compare to the shape of the branches? They're both the same shape. Branches are the mirrored shape of roots. Because ISLAM is the mirror of IMAN. A believers ISLAM reflects his IMAN. Isn't that true?
⟪ar-quote:وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَالَ لِلنَّاسِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫

And Allah sets forth examples for mankind so that they may remember! Now the question is, why does Allah say that he sets forth such examples so we can remember? He used the word MISAL in the beginning of the verse:
⟪ar-quote:أَلَمْ تَرَ كَيْفَ ضَرَبَ ٱللَّهُ مَثَلًۭا كَلِمَةًۭ طَيِّبَةًۭ كَشَجَرَةٍۢ طَيِّبَةٍ⟫

Have you not seen how Allah sets forth the example of a good word like a good tree? He already said its an example, and we know that examples are used for anologies; they're used to explain a concept better. Then why does he repeat himself again at the end? He repeats it to stress a profound reality! Through the examples of a tree, a good word, the various stages of development for a believer, Allah wants us to understand a fundamental reality, that all external dimensions of creation, are always sustained through their inner dimensions. Which means that this world, and everything it contains, has a counter-part, which is its inner dimension. So every ZAAHIR, is sustained by it's BATIN; just as the tree exists because of its roots; just as the child was developed in the womb of its mother; just as a good word is sustained by its inner meaning; just as ISLAM is sustained by IMAN.  Every outer aspect of creation (ZAAHRI) is sustained by its inner aspect (BAATIN). There would not be an outer aspect, if there was an inner aspect that preceeded it. This is the reality that Allah wants to direct our attention towards. That if there is this physical universe, there has to be a spiritual universe behind the scenes that is sustaining it.

---

<!-- section 10 (id=5783, raw_sort=10): 3 Levels Of Existence -->

## The Three Levels of Existence (Mubdaʿ, Lāhūt, Nāsūt)

In the previous session we looked at the relationship between Tawheed, IMAN and ISLAM. I explained that TAWHEED is symbolized by the seed; because a seed is the essence of the tree. It contains within it the entire tree in its passive form. Similarly, the Islamic creedal formula LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH contains within it the entire ISLAM and IMAN of a MOMIN in a dormant form. What is needed, is an environment to activate that dormant potential. For a seed that environment is the soil; whereas for a believer that environment is his teacher, that has been sanctioned by elders. He is someone whose knowledge has been tested for accuracy; and whose misconceptions have been removed.

Once the seed is placed within the soil, the first thing that comes out of it are the roots, which then grow deeper and deeper into the earth. And the purpose of those roots is to draw nutrition from the soil, in order to feed the embryo within the seed. Similarly IMAN is the first thing that develops for a believer through the knowledge and guidance of his teacher. That's why IMAN is symbolized by the roots. Just as roots are hidden within the soil, one's IMAN remain hidden within his heart. 

The roots then keep nourishing the embryo, until it develops to a point where it can no longer be contained within its shell, and it sprouts out into the world in the form of a shoot, and starts moving upwards. And this has been explained as its desire and ability to "act". Until now the roots were nourishing the plant, but now it wants to develop leaves and generate its own nutrition through photosynthesis using sunlight. In other words it wants to now not just depend on the roots for its sustenance, it wants to generate its own sustenance.

This entire process symbolizes the spiritual development of a believer. Under the guidance and training of his teacher, the believer's IMAN in Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) and his revelatory propositions keeps growing and becoming strong; until it reaches a point, where he can no longer contain it within his heart. His IMAN burts out on his tongue in the form of praise and the glorification of his master; when then develops into action or the practices of ISLAM. In other words, there comes a time when that belief manifests in the form of action, and he begins a spiritually upward journey towards his master. We talked about how this growth takes place gradually over the period of a lifetime. Just as the growth and maturity of a tree is directly proportional to the growth of its roots, similarly the growth of one's ISLAM is directly proportional to ones IMAN. In fact ISLAM is a mirror of one's IMAN; just as the branches are a mirror of the roots. They both have the exact same form.

So in the last analysis, TAWHEED, IMAN and ISLAM are not 3 separate entities. They're actually different aspects of the same reality. They're not 3 separate children of a parent, they're actually one single child. So Allah begins the verse by saying:
⟪ar-quote:أَلَمْ تَرَ كَيْفَ ضَرَبَ ٱللَّهُ مَثَلًۭا كَلِمَةًۭ طَيِّبَةًۭ كَشَجَرَةٍۢ طَيِّبَةٍ⟫

Have you not seen how Allah sets forth the example of a good word like a good tree? and then he reiterates or re-emphasizes the importance of this example by saying :
⟪ar-quote:وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَالَ لِلنَّاسِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫

And Allah sets forth examples for mankind so that they may remember! And the purpose of this reiteration is to tell us, that don't you see that nothing that exists in its outer forms in this world can exist without its inner conterpart. Every external dimension is always sustained by an inner dimension. Because a tree cannot exist without its roots; a child cannot exist without a mothers womb; body cannot exist without a soul; word cannot exist without a meaning; action cannot exist without intention; ISLAM cannot exist without IMAN.  In other words, ZAAHIR cannot exist without a BAATIN. And more importantly the real value, the real essential meaning is in the BAATIN and not the ZAAHIR. The ZAAHIR merely exists to point to the BAATIN.

3 Levels to existence

The word ZAHIR in the arabic language comes from the word ⟪ar:ظَھَرَ⟫, which means the back; whereas the word BATIN comes from the ⟪ar:بَطَن⟫which means the belly. Now if you look at the back, it is one dimensional; it is flat; it is empty. There is nothing useful on one's back. All the organs in the human body, that keep a person alive, are located where? In the belly! And so the true meaning, the real value of anything will always exist in its inner dimension (in the BATIN), and not the ZAHIR.

So this lower world (DUNIYA) has nothing to sustain it, except by its inner dimension, which is the AAKHIRA. The spiritual world (AKHIRA) stands in relation to this material world (DUNIYA), like the spirit stands in relation to the body. This is why, as long as one sees the spirit manifesting through the body, he find the body pleasing. Because what happens to the body when the soul leaves it? It begins to rot and decay; and we find it displeasing and disgusting. And what's interesting is that a dead animal, on which the name of Allah has not been recited during sacrifice, is forbidden to believers. But that same rotting decaying flesh is not forbidden to dogs, vultures and other scavengers. And so the ones who are focused *only* on this physical and material world, without seeing the hidden force of the spiritual realm animating it; are like these dogs and vultures, that can only feed of the dead. But as MOMINS and believers, we strive to study and seek the hidden (the BATIN) that we see manifesting through the ZAHIR.

Now I want you to keep the analogy of this tree we studied in the back of your minds as we progress. The tree is the outer dimension; the roots are the inner dimension; and the seed is the "essence" or the innermost dimension. In other words, there are three dimensions (or 3 components) to everything in existence, just as we have the physical dimensions of length, breadth and depth. In human beings we have the soul, the body and the intellect. Body is the outer form, intellect is the inner form, and soul is the essence. The body and mind exists because the soul exists. There is a very interesting AYAH in the Quran that explains these 3 levels beautifully. Allah says:

**https://quran.com/7/26**
⟪ar-quote:يَبَنِىٓ آدَمَ قَدْ أَنزَلْنَا عَلَيْكُمْ لِبَاسًۭا يُوَرِى سَوْءَتِكُمْ وَرِيشًۭا⟫
O Children of Adam! We have bestowed clothing upon you to cover yourselves and as an adornment,

⟪ar-quote:وَلِبَاسُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ⟫

and the garment of righteousness, that is better. 

⟪ar-quote:ذَلِكَ مِنْ آيَتِ ٱللَّهِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَذَّكَّرُون⟫

Such are among the signs of Allah, so that they may remember; so that they may be reminded. We just learnt that trees are a consant reminder for us about certain realities; and now Allah is talking about clothing as another constant reminder for us about some other realities. And I want you to pay close attention to this "outside in approach" that is so beautifully explained in this AYAH. Allah says:

⟪ar-quote:يَبَنِىٓ آدَمَ قَدْ أَنزَلْنَا عَلَيْكُمْ لِبَاسًۭا⟫

We have sent down clothing upon you. This is the ZAHIR, just like clothes are our outer aspects. When someone looks at us, the first thing they see is clothes, not our body. Even though in this day and age, we sadly see more skin than clothes. So the AYAH begins by talking about the outer aspect, the ZAHIR. Then it mentions its inner purpose, which is what?
⟪ar-quote:يُوَرِى سَوْءَتِكُمْ وَرِيشًۭا⟫

Hide your ugliness and adorn yourselves. Clothing serves two purposes. What is the primary purpose? ⟪ar:يُوَرِى سَوْءَتِكُمْ⟫, to hide your ugliness. Isn't it interesting that Allah called nakedness "ugly"? Today people are so quick to show their skin to the world; and which sadly many find so attractive - nakedness. Allah said the primary reason I gave you clothing was to hide your ugly nakedness. But then he talks about a secondary purpose. ⟪ar:وَرِيشًۭا⟫, to adorn yourselves. So the second part of the AYAH is talking about the inner dimension of clothing; it's talking about its purpose; it's BAATIN, which is to hide the ugliness of the body and make it look beautiful. Then Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:وَلِبَاسُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ⟫

and the garment of righteousness, that is better. Now here Allah is talking about the "true essence" of  clothing. The purpose of physical clothing, is to remind you of your spiritual clothing. Just like we have a physical need of clothing; just as our body needs physical clothes to hide our ugliness and look beautiful; our souls too needs a garment that can hide its ugliness, and make it look beautiful. And that garment is piety.

What is piety? Generally TAQWA is translated as "fear", which is an inaccurate translation. TAQWA doesn't mean fear, even though it manifests in the form of fear. I want you to imagine that you're standing on the edge of a path, that is laid with thorns. And right on the sides of that path, there are may thorny bushes. So there are thorns on the path itself and on the sides. How will you walk that path? Will you just stroll through it, or will you place every single step with extreme caution? And what'll happen if you don't mind the thorns and just stroll through it carelessly? By the time you reach the other end? Your clothes will be shredded, and your feet will be wounded? So if you can imagine and appreciate this analogy, then this is how Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) explained TAQWA.

It is the constant and unbroken remembrance of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). It is a slaves constant mindfulness about the presence of its master. It is not making a single move; not uttering a single word; not looking at a single thing; not listening to a single sound; not taking a single breadth; without being mindful of the fact, that his master is watching. Piety is what makes every act for the sake of Allah; piety is what makes one extremely conscious of the HALAAL and the HARAAM (the permissible and the forbidden); not because of the item or the act itself; but out of this immense need and desire to constantly please, obey and serve ones master. This is where IMAN and ISLAM now begins to seep into ones character (into ⟪ar:أخلاق⟫). It begins to flow through the speech and the actions of the believer, making everything he does beautiful. It covers up and hides the ugliness of one's passions and desires, and through ones beautiful اخلاق, makes him look beautiful. His company becomes pleasing. And so Allah says:

⟪ar-quote:وَلِبَاسُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ⟫

The garment of piety is the best of all garments. The reason I gave you outward clothing, is for you to first understand its purpose, which is to hide the ugliness of your bodies and adorn it to make it look beautiful. But then also to realize, that just as your body needs clothing, so does your soul. In other words, I gave you the ZAHIR, so you can understand it's pupose (BATIN), and get to its true essence; its essential reality; the innermost dimension (باطن الباطن). And what is that essential reality? To attain piety! How do we achieve piety? Through the knowledge of IMAN and the practices of ISLAM. Practice ISLAM which is the ZAHIR; then get to IMAN which is the BATIN. But then don't just stop there, get to the essential reality of IMAN, which is TAWEED. I want you to see the essence of all existence, which is LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH. That there is nothing except Allah.

So this AYAH is teaching us the 3 levels of knowledge:
1. Clothing which is the outer aspect (⟪ar:ظاہر⟫),
2. Its inner purpose which is to hide ugliness and adorn oneself (⟪ar:باطن⟫),
3. And finally, the inner aspect of that inner dimension (⟪ar:باطن الباطن⟫)  which is to wear the garment of piety (⟪ar:لباس التقوی⟫) towards which the symbol (ریش) "adornment" points. TAQWA or piety, which is the constant mindfulness of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), it provides adornment to the soul in the truest sense.

Now if you look at our existence in this world, the knowledge of the outer aspect of this physical world is at the level of the beasts. So the one who chooses to remain at this level without attempting to understanding its inner aspect, is at the level of such beasts. Because what animals operate on is instinct. They have no intellect. And as we know now, AQL means to restrain. The more AQL a person has the more restrain and control he can exercise; and this is why we see that animals and beasts are incapable of exercising restraint; and they are unable to see a purpose in their creation. The only purpose of their existence is to eat, sleep and procreate. That's all they do. So human beings who fail to see the inner aspects of creation; who fail to see a purpose in their creation, they live in this world like beasts. They eat, sleep, procreate and die.

But the one who chooses to see the inner aspect and the purpose of creation (the باطن) becomes the true descendants of Adam. These are the poeple that in the Islamic tradition are considered "Adamic" or "human". Because faith lies at the essence of true humanity. So this is the second "inner" level that we as believers try to work on.

But then there is a third dimensions, which is the inner dimension of these inner aspects (BATIN ALBATIN). This is the realm and knowledge of angels. So whoever completely acquires this level of knowledge becomes "spiritual" in his nature. His body resembles the humans, but his nature and his character resmebles the angels. These are the people that Allah chooses as his prophets and messengers, and places them as his vicergent (KHALIFA) on the earth, for the guidance of all humanity. These prophets (because they operate on this innermost dimension) they become true spiritual scholar; they become what is called, "the veil of the angels" (⟪ar:حجاب الملائکۃ⟫). We as human beings cannot directly see angles, because they don't posess a body. But through the character and the angelic nature of these prophets, we can come to know what angels are like. Because these prophets by their exalted character, become the exemplar of divine revelation (⟪ar:راموز الوحی⟫). They souls become so powerful that they are then able to absorb divine revelations, and they become (⟪ar:الترجمان الوحی⟫) interpreters of that divine revelation for the children of Adam. Allah gives these messengers the posession of the keys, that open the gates of his paradise and gardens. So now only those who choose to follow them, "willingly", and choose to become like them, can enter those gardens. Allah also gives them complete authority over Hell, such that only those who disobey them will enter it!

So we as human beings are placed between these realms. On one side we have beasts and on the other side we have angles, or these angelic beings in the form of prophets. We exists in between these two extremes with the freedom of choice. And we possess both natures. We have a beasteal nature which is active, as well as the potential for developing and activating our dormant angelic nature. And the tool we've been given is "free will" (أختیار). We've been given the freedom to choose either side. If we move towards the outer aspects which is DUNIYA, we'll become like the beats and end up just like them. If we move towards the inner aspects, we will become like angels and prophets and end up just like them. The choice is entirely up to us

---

<!-- section 11 (id=5785, raw_sort=11): 3 levels Of Knowledge -->

## The Three Levels of Knowledge (ʿIlm al-Yaqīn, ʿAyn al-Yaqīn, Ḥaqq al-Yaqīn)

d

Are all 3 components important?

How do these three components of ZAHIR, BATIN and BATIN AL-BATIN work? How do they corelate with each other? Sydena Jaffar bin Mansoor AlYaman in his book ⟪ar:کتاب العالم والغلام⟫ , gives a beautifully simple example of this concept. He says that everything in this world is known by 3 things:

> — *Image text (from image 022; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/022.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

The first is its name (⟪ar:أسم⟫), because everything has a name, or an identifier.

The second is its specific characteristics (⟪ar:صفات⟫). Everything has certain characteristics that distinguishes it from other things

And the third is its meaning or its true purpose (⟪ar:المعنی⟫) .

He explains that meaning is the real "essence" of a thing. The name simply "belongs" to that thing; and the characteristic only "points" to it. Characteristics simply bridge the gap between the name and the essential meaning. He gives the example, that when someone says “the moon rose.”, his essential meaning is the actual round disk in the sky.  “Moon” is its name, and “Rising” is its specific characteristic. And by the combination of these 2 components (name and characteristics), the third component of meaning can be achieved. Because if someone just said “the moon”, and then stopped, that would have no real meaning. Or if someone just said, “it rose,” that would also be meaningless. It is only when the name, and the specific characteristic are combined, by saying that “the moon rose”, only then the real meaning manifests itself, and what is really being said becomes clear.

So the idea is that only through the combination of the ZAHIR and the BATIN, the third component (of BATIN AlBATIN) can be reached.

There is an AYAH in the Quran in which Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:وَذَرُوا۟ ظَهِرَ ٱلْإِثْمِ وَبَاطِنَهُ⟫

And abandon the outer aspect of the sin, as well as its inner aspect! So what Allah is saying is that the actual entity that needs to be abandoned is "sin". But sin has two aspects. It has an outer aspect and an inner aspect. The outer aspect, or the ZAHIR is flat, it is one dimensional! But behind the sin, or within the belly of the sin (the BATIN) lie the actual reasons and motivations for that offense. And so if you want to remove the sin, you have to work on both. If you just try to stop the act without trying to stop the underlying motivations and temptations, it won't work. If you keep working on the inner reaons, and don't stop committing the act, that won't work either. The only way to make it work, is by working on both, and the third component, which is the actual sin itself will automatically get eliminated.

The third example he gives is of an egg. We know the embryo is formed within the yolk of an egg. The yolk contains the essential meaning. It is the BATIN AL-BATIN. It contains the embryo, and the food that will nourish the embryo as it grows. That yolk is surrounded by the egg white, which provides the medium in which the embryo develops. And they're both covered by an external shell which is a hard protective covering. The shell and the egg white together facilitate the development of the embryo. Just as the ZAHIR and the BATIN facilitate the development of the BATIN AL-BATIN

> — *Image text (from image 023; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/023.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Now if we look at the analogy of the seed that we studied earlier, the seed contains the essential meaning. It contains the embryo. It is the BATIN AL-BATIN. Everything about the tree, what its branches are going to look like, what the tree will be shaped like, its color, its flowers, its fruits, all that information exists within the seed itsef. But what activates and develops that potential? The roots and the plant. The ZAHIR and the BATIN. Roots work under the soil; the plant works on top of the soil; and together they accomplish what? They activate all the potential that was dormant within the seed!

Now the same is true of Allah’s religion. TAWHEED is the seed; it is the embryo; it is the yolk; it is BATIN AL-BATIN. It contains within it the potential of a perfect MOMIN. The spiritual and physical perfection of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and Maulana Ali exists this TAWHEED in a dormant state. And just like the egg yolk has an egg white and a hard shell, TAWHEED has an outer aspect, which are the outward practices of ISLAM; and it has an inner aspect, which is the knowledge of its inner dimensions. And both these components work together to do what? To manifest the true potential of TAWHEED.

So what we're learning here is that only practicing the outward aspects of ISLAM is not enough to experience TAWHEED. Just gaining knowledge of the inward aspects is not enough to experience TAWHEED. Only when the outward practices are combined with its inward knowledge, that's what leads to the experience of TAWHEED. Because there are people who practive ISLAM to perfection, but don't make any effort towards gaining knwoledge; there are people who spend their entire lives gaining knowledge, but they don't perform a single practice; both these people fall short in their experience of TAWHEED. It is only when both are combined, that the beauty of TAWHEED emerges.

---

3 levels of knowldge

So now if you look at ISLAM as the specific religion of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), it also exists in 3 layers. It has an outward aspect which is the ZAHIR; it has an inward aspect which is the BATIN and it has an innermost aspect which is the BATIN AL-BATIN. This is why Imam Jaffar Al-Sadiq (AS) said, “All our affair contains an exoteric (ZAHIR), an esoteric (BATIN), and an esoteric of the esoteric (BATIN Al-BATIN).

> — *Image text (from image 024; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/024.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

The outward form is called SHAREEAH; the inner meanings of that outward form is called TAVEEL; and the innermost reality that the SHAREEAH and TAVEEL work together to manfiest, is called the HAQEEQA. It follows the exact same pattern that we've studied so far. So now if you look at these 7 pillars of ISLAM:

⟪ar:ولایۃ      طھارۃ     صلواۃ     زکواۃ    صوم     حج     جھاد⟫

Each pillar contains these three layers of meaning and practice. The practice itself is the outer "exoteric" form (or the ZAAHIR). The second layer is the inner "esoteric" meaning (or the BATIN). The third layer is the esoteric of the esoteric (BATIN Al-BATIN) which is the innermost layer of reality (called HAQIQAH). So you can think of the practices of SHAREEAH as ISLAM; knowledge of TAVEEL as IMAN. And then ISLAM and IMAN working together to reveal the truth (HAQEEQAH) which is IHSAN (the beatific vision of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala)

SHAREEAH, TAVEEL and HAQEEQAH

Let's take a deeper look at these 3 words, SHAREEAH, TAVEEL and HAQEEQAH.

Shareeah comes from ⟪ar:شارع⟫, which means "road". But ⟪ar:شریعۃ⟫is not just any road. It is a very specific road that leads to water. Imagine the Arab desert, scorching heat, blazing sun, extremely dry weather. What could possible be the greatest of all blessings for an Arab in the desert? Water right? So to them SHAREEAH was a road that lead them to a spring of cool water. 

TAVEEL, comes from the root word AWWAL, which means "first/beginning/origin". So the word TAVEEL means "a return to the beginning/origin"

HAQEEQA comes from the word HAQ, which we know means reality - that which is real.

Now lets link these together to see how they all corelate with each other. Lets begin with SHAREEAH which means a road that leads to a body of spring water. When would one even begin a journey on such a road? When one is thirsty. And the end goal of this journey is to find "that" which quenches thirst. What would happen if one does not find water? He would perish. So In other words, (in a spiritual sense) SHAREEAH is the road to salvation? Now let's talk about the images associated with travelling on a long road in the heat of the sun, especially when you're thirsty. What kind of journey would that be? It would be a struggle! And what happens when you are walking along this path, do you get more thirsty? more tired? 

Now what are the images associated with spring water? Coolness, stillness, tranquility, peace, quenching thirst. That's the knowledge TAVEEL, because water [pure water, drinking water] symbolizes good, beneficial knowledge. Now if you compare the size of a spring, a lake or a river to an ocean, which one is larger? Ocean is exponentially larger than the others, but its water is undrinkable. Ocean symbolizes impure, unclean knowledge - knowledge that is filled with doubts. And what we're learning is that real knowledge is that which is beneficial, that is pure (clear of doubts), that is life-giving, no matter how small its quantity is. It is still better than an oceans worth of knowledge full of doubts and confusions.

Now what's interesting about the word TAVEEL, is the meaning of "return" embedded within the word. What does return suggest? It suggests to go back to the point of origin; it alludes to a home. Because "home" is the point where we begin our day from, and return to at night. So TAVEEL suggests a return or home-coming; return to where we came from. Now notice that both SHAREEAH and TAVEEL, linguistically allude to a journey. SHAREEAH means a road, and the purpose of a road is travel. TAVEEL means "return to the beginning", which suggests journey as well as direction. The direction is towards the origin with an invitation for a journey. So what we're learning here is that TAVEEL is not the destination, it's only a bridge that gets us to the destination. What is that destination? It's HAQEEQAH. This is why TAVEEL is called ⟪ar:جسَر الحقائق⟫, it is a bridge that leads to the reality. You only need a bridge until you get to the destination. Once you reach home, the bride is not longer necessary. In other words, the only purpose of TAVEEL is to get us to the HAQEEQA, the origin, the final destination.

> — *Image text (from image 025; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/025.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Now let's bring this together. The journey began with a thirst, that lead to the physical action, to seek out that, which quenches the thirst. So one begins the journey on the شارع that leads to water. The act of travelling is the outward form of the journey (the ZAHIR). He finally reaches a body of cool spring water and quenches his thirst, which fulfills the true pupose of his journey (the BATIN). So SHAREEAH is the outward form (ZAAHIR), and TAVEEL is the inner form (BATIN). But after one has quenched his thirst through this blessing of water, what becomes the next question? Where did this blessing come from? Now what is spring water? It is water that gushes out of the earth, right? It comes from a particular source. Now what are the images associated with that? Water gusing out from a certain location within the spring and causing ripples on the surface of the water, yes? In other words, if you want to find the source, the point of origin from where that water is coming from, how do you trace your way back to it? Through the ripples, right?

> — *Image text (from image 026; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/026.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

What are some of the characteristics of these ripples.

They're moving outwards from the point of origin. which means if we follow them, we'll have to move inwards towards them

The outer circles are larger and have a larger radius; the inner circles are smaller and condensed. And they keep getting smaller and condenesed as we move inwards. Each circle provides a different context.

Its the same with this knoweldge of TAVEEL or interpretations. For every outer form, there are many different interpretations based on its context. The outer ones are easy to understand, and as you keep moving towards the center, they start getting more and more complex and difficult.

So the imagery here is that we take this difficult journey along this long tiresome road which is SHAREEAH. That road leads you to this spring water, which is symbolized by TAVEEL. What does TAVEEL mean? Return to the origin. What is the origin of the spring? The point where the water is gushing out from. That is HAQEEQAH. 

Now if you apply this to our religion of ISLAM, DAYAM AL-ISLAM are the set of physical practices through which our ISLAM develops. But these practices are tiresome, which are uncomfortable, which are displeasing and require effort like the journey, because it is part of SHAREEAH. But when one understands its inner meanings, it is like reaching the cool body of water and drinking from it; it is revitalizing, it is energizing, it is life giving; it removes the tiredness of the journey; provides peace and tranquility to the soul. This is the knowledge of TAVEEL through which IMAN develops. These are the interpretations and the meanings behind the outward practices. Once we understand these meanings, it removes the discomforts of the ourward practices, and strengthens them; just as roots strengthen the tree. But then the essence of the journey, is in recognizing the source of all of this comfort. This is the knowledge of the innermost realm -  knowledge of the true reality of things. The essence of why the rest came into being. It is the knowledge of HAQEEQA, where we find AL-HAQ (The one that is truly real). This is where we find that  Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) is the source of everything.

So now what this means, is that every pillar, such as SALAAT for example, exists in three states: There is the ZAAHIRI SALAAT, which is the outward practice of SALAAH. Then there is the BATINI SALAAT, which is the interpretations behind every single act of the SALAAH. And this ZAHIR and the BATIN together, point to the one true reality, which is the HAQIQI SALAAT, the knowledge of those realities that gave birth to these spiritual and physical structures in the first place.

---

---

<!-- section 12 (id=5787, raw_sort=12): Taveel examples -->

## Worked Examples of Taʾwīl (Esoteric Exegesis)

Over the last few sessions we've talked about the concept of ZAHR, BATIN and BATIN AlBATIN. ZAHIR is the external form; BATIN is the internal form; and BATIN AL-BATIN is the innermost form; or the essence, the true reality of that entity. The essence contains within it the entire potential of that entity in a dormant or passive state. Once the proper environment and care is provided to that essence, it begins growing and developing, and gradually it starts realizing its potential.

In the language of religion, these 3 levels are termed SHAREEAH, TAVEEL and HAQEEQAH.

SHAREEA is the outer form or all practices; TAVEEL are the interpreations of those outward practices, and together they reveal or realize the true innermost reality of their existence. Allah says in the Quran:

⟪ar-quote:وَمِن كُلِّ شَىْءٍ خَلَقْنَا زَوْجَيْنِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَذَكَّرُونَ⟫

And we have created all "things" in pairs. In other words there is the thing itself (⟪ar:شئی⟫), which operates through 2 forms - the ZAHIR and the BATIN. This is how Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) structured all his creation. That the outer form has to work harmoneously with its inner form, in order to achieve the true potential of its innermost form. In other words, ZAHIR and BATIN must work together to activate what lies dormant in the BATIN AL-BATIN. Just as the roots and the branches work together to activate the potential of the tree. The body and the intellect work together, to realize the true potential of the soul. words and meanings work together to reveal intention. ISLAM and IMAN work together to reveal the beauty of TAWHEED (or EHSAN - the beatific vision of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala)

> — *Image text (from image 027; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/027.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

This concept is geometrically represented in our religion by the shape of a "circle". If you look at a circle, it also has 3 things. Every circle has a center, which is its essence, or its innermost reality (BATIN AL-BATIN). A circle cannot exist without its center. And one circle, can only have one center; it cannot have more than one centers. Every circle has a circumfrence which is its outer boundary; it's ZAHIR. But between the circumfrence of the center; within the belly of the circle, within the BATIN,  you have the radius that contains numerous points. And this is why you can many concentric circles between the center and the circumfrence.

Everything in this physical and spiritual universe exists and functions on this same pattern. So when we come to religion, we find there is one SHAREEAH (the circumfrence of religion); which is a manifestation of one true HAQEEQA (LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH). But between the two, you have many layers of TAVEEL, which are the various interpretations emerging out from the same reality. It is the same reality manifesting itself in various contexts.

Now what's common between the shape of the circumfrence and the center? They're both circles. In other words, the circumfrence is the fully activated potential of the center; just as SHAREEAH is the fully realized form of the HAQEEQAH. It is LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH in action! But what gives the circumfrence its size? The radius! The BATIN! The greater the radius, the larger the circumfrence. In other words, the more one acquires the knowledge of the inner dimensions, the greater one's circle of practice will become. An increase in the knowledge of BATIN will result in an increase in the practce of ZAHIR.

So each and every pillar of ISLAM operates in these 3 layers. Every pillar has an essence (its innermost reality) which gets realized through the knowledge of its inward and outward form. And what's even more interesting, is that these 3 levels of the pillars, correspond to the three faculties of knowledge in the human being.  Each human being has 3 faculties. The outward faculty which are the 5 senses; an inward faculty which is the NAFS AL-NATIQA (the rational soul); and an innermost faculty which is AL-AQL (the combination of heart and intellect). The outward practices of ISLAM is perceived by the external 5 senses of the human being (ZAHIR). The various interpretations of these outward forms are conceptualized through the internal faculties of the rational soul (al-nafs al-natiqah), through the use of memory, imagination, reflection, reason, etc.. And the one true innermost realities (the HAQEEQAH) is perceived and envisioned through AL-AQL (the intellect), which lies is the center of the rational soul. Therefore, to practice the outward form of the pillars, is to worship Allah physically with the body. To practice the inner forms of the pillars is to worship Allah "rationally" with the soul. And to practice the innermost forms of the pillars, is to worship Allah spiritually and intellectually with the heart-intellect.

> — *Image text (from image 028; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/028.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Now if we look at the Quran as a circle, the outermost layer are its words, which are called TANZEEL. These are symbolized by each point, or arc of points on the circumference of the circle. They represent the ZAHIR (the exoteric); these are the literal words of the Quran made up of letters and sounds. TANZEEL comes from the word NAZAL, which means to send down. Linguistically the word implies a descent - from higher ground to lower ground - from a higher source to a lower source.  This is why the words of Quran are called TANZEEL, because they were sent down by the ultimate source.

The radius represents an expression of the esoteric interpretations of the literal words. These are the intermediate levels of TAVEEL of the Qur’an.

The centre represents the esoteric of the esoteric (batin al-batin) which contains the true essence or the HAQEEQAH of revelation - the intentions of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) for his slaves.

So in the final analysis, the circumfrence and the radius exists to point to the singular reality of the center. And this is why Allah created the entire universe in pairs, to point to the one reality that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) is one! He is unique! ⟪ar:قل ھو اللہ احد⟫ . Say He is Allah the unique, and so all creation exists in pairs to reveal the uniqueness of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). The diversity of the creation reveals the singulary and the uniformity of the creator.

---

Harmony of the outer and inner form

Now let's look at an actual example to how the three come together. Allah says in the quran:
⟪ar-quote:وَٱللَّهُ أَنزَلَ مِنَ ٱلسَّمَآءِ مَآءًۭ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ ٱلْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَآ ۚ إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَآيَةًۭ لِّقَوْمٍۢ يَسْمَعُونَ⟫

Allah sent down water from the sky to enliven the earth after it was dead. Indeed in it is a sign for the group that can hear.

The first thing I want you to notice is the word ⟪ar:انزل⟫. Why did Allah use this word? Because he says water comes down from the sky to the earth. Sky is a higher than the earth, so the word ⟪ar:أنزل⟫is more appropriate to describe this sending down of water. What did he send down from the sky? ⟪ar:وَٱللَّهُ أَنزَلَ مِنَ ٱلسَّمَآءِ مَآءًۭ⟫ He sent down Water! Who did he send it down to? ⟪ar:بِهِ ٱلْأَرْضَ⟫ The earth! Why did he send it down? ⟪ar:فَأَحْيَا بِهِ ٱلْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَآ⟫. What does this mean in the physical sense? That the earth was dead, and the sky sent down its water to bring it to life. So again we have 3 things. The outward form which is the sky sending down its water to the earth; the inner form, where the earth absorbs and takes in that water; and the innermost form (the true purpose) of coming to life. And obviously the earth coming to life means it becoming a "source" of life for other living creatures. Plants, vegetation, insects animals etc. The earth becomes a source of life for all living creations through the water that is given to it by the sky. So even at the physical level we can see all three components in this verse.

But now if you apply this same verse in the spiritual realm, each of these entities have a spiritual counter part. Just like the physical sky, there is a spiritual sky; just like the physical earth there is a spiritual earth; just like the physical water there is a spiritual water; and just like physical life, there is a spiritual life.

Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said in a Hadees
⟪ar-quote:اِنَّا اللہ اَسَّسَ دِینَہُ عَلیَ مِثاَلِ خَلقِہِ لِیَستَدِلَّ بِالدِّینِ عَلَی الدُّنیَا ؛ وَ الدُّنیَا عَلَی الدِّین⟫

Indeed Allah founded his religion on the pattern of creation, to provide evidence for his religion through the world; and to provide evidence for the world through his religion. In other words, he created the physical world on the exact same pattern as he created the spiritual world.

So now let's try to understand this verse in the spiritual realm. Let's begin with water. What does physical water symbolize in the spiritual realm? It represents knowledge. Why? Because every attribute that you can think of water in the physical realm, applies to knowledge in the spiritual realm. The first and foremost is that water is life giving; it sustains physical life as we just read in the AYAH. In another verse Allah says,
⟪ar-quote:وَجَعَلْنَا مِنَ ٱلْمَآءِ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ حَىٍّ⟫

We made every living thing with water. So let's compare water to knowledge and see what's in common between the two:

Water cleanses the body of physical impurities; Knowledge cleanses the soul of moral, ethical, social impurities.

Water always flows from top to bottom; Knowledge always comes down from a higher rank of a teacher to the lower rank of a student.

Water takes on the shape of the container it is placed in; Knowledge takes on the attributes of the one who posesses it. If knowledge falls into the hands of a good person, he will use it to create good in the word. If it falls in the hands of an evil person, he will use the same knowledge to bring about destruction. Knowledge is the same drop of pure rain water. If it goes inside a seashell, it will turn into a pearl; if it falls in the mouth of a snake, it will turn into poison. So just like water, knowledge acquires the shape of its container.

As long as water keeps flowing, it remains pure. Once water becomes stagnant, it will cause diseases and breeds insects. Knowledge, as long as it keeps getting passed down from rank to rank remains pure. If one of the rank tries to hoard it - does not share it - chooses to keep it all to himself, tries to controls its access; or if it is prevented from the one who deserves it, it begins breeding evil in society.

Water exists in three states - vapour, liquid and ice; knowledge exists in three states: knowledge of SHAREEAH, knowledge of TAVEEL and knowledge of HAQEEQA.

Water is made up of two components - Hydrogen and Oxygen. All knowledge is made of two components - the sayings of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and the wisdom of Maulana Ali (AS)'s interpretations.

So we can see that there is a perfect corelation between water in the physical realm and knowledge in the spiritual realm. So water is ZAHIR, or the symbol and what it symbolizes is knowledge.

Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:وَٱللَّهُ أَنزَلَ مِنَ ٱلسَّمَآءِ مَآءًۭ⟫

Allah sent down water from the sky. In the spiritual realm the NATIQ symbolized by the sky. He is the sky of the spiritual world. And his WASEE, is his earth. So now if we look at this in our context, Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is the sky and his WASEE Maulana Ali (AS) is his earth. And so what did the sky give to the earth? Water! Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) gave his knowledge to Maulana Ali (AS). Why? To bring the dead earth back to life. Isn't "death" the inactive, or the dormant, or the passive state of life?  So the earth sent down its water to bring the earth to life; Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) gave his knowledge to his WASEE (Maulana Ali) to activate his spiritual potential.

Now think about what the earth does with the rain water? It absorbs all of that water, and nourishes the seeds that are placed within it, by giving it just the right amount for their growth. If the earth gave all of its water to the seeds, the embryo within the seed wouldn't be able to handle it; they would drown! So the earth gives the seeds exactly what they need to grow. We (believers) are the seeds that have been placed within the earth; within the WILAYAH of Maulana Ali AS. And he gives us exactly the right amount of knowledge that we need for our spiritual growth through his various intermediaries۔ So now if we look at this AYAH again in the spiritual realm, Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:وَٱللَّهُ أَنزَلَ مِنَ ٱلسَّمَآءِ مَآءًۭ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ ٱلْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَآ ۚ⟫

And it is Allah who sends down his knowledge from the NATIQ to the WASEE, to activate and bring its dormant potential back to life, so that it can do what it is supposed to do; which is cultivate the souls of the believers that are placed within his care. Just as the earth prepare the seed to one day sprout out, and exist in the ourside world, the knowledge of the WASEE prepares the souls of the believers to live and thrive in after life. And then Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَآيَةًۭ لِّقَوْمٍۢ يَسْمَعُونَ⟫

Indeed in this example are signs for the nation that hears; there are signs pointing to deeper meanings for the group that is not deaf.

So for every ZAHIR; every outer verse of the Quran, there exists various interpreations that lead us to its true reality. I just gave you one interpretation in the context of NATIQ; but in a different context the same symbols represent different meanings. So these symbols (sky, earth, water, life), you can think of these as variables in an equation. Their values change based on context! But what does not change is the outer form of the equation, and its innermost essence.

---

ZABEEHA and AHAD SHAREEF

YAUM AL-GHADEER is arriving soon. This is a day on which believers take AHAD

We know that sacrificing an animal is one of the requirements of HAJJ; and Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) has given us very clear instructions, on how to sacrifice the animal in the name of Allah, and for the sake of Allah. Why do we sacrifice these animals? The one-dimensional answer to that question is "dinner"! To eat the animal. But there is a symbolic representation of that act; which is to end the beastly life of the animal, and to elevate it to rank of humanity, by making it a part of a believer's body. Because it is not just any one sacrificing the animal - it's a believer who's doing it; and he's doing so in the name of Allah and for the sake of Allah, in the exact specific manner prescribed by Allah. In other words, there is a divine consent behind the act.

So the idea behind sacrifice is to bring an end to a lower form of life, in order to begin a new journey towards a higher form of life. Because when we eat the meat of the sacrificed animal, our bodies digest it, and it gets absorbed within our blood stream and gets converts into energy. And a momin's energy is spent in the way of Allah; in the practices of the 7 pillars of Islam. But the animal was not capable of these acts itself, unless and until it was consumed by the believer.

**But this conversion cannot take place, until the animals free will, and beasteal nature is brought to an end, and made subservient to the will of man.**

Syedna Moyyed states, that when one of the Imams was asked about the wisdom behind sacrificing an animal, he explained that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) has made this physical act of sacrifice, a symbol and a sign for certain spiritual realities. And what it symbolizes, is taking the spiritual oath, which we generally refer to as AHAD SHAREEF or ⟪ar:بیعۃ⟫ in Arabic. In other words, sacrificing an animal is the exact same thing, as a believer alleging to the obedience of Imam AS by taking AHAD SHAREEF. In other words, just as the believer sacrifices an animal in the name of Allah; an Imam sacrifices a believer with the blade of AHAD SHAREEF. He puts an end to the believers debased life of desires and passions, and consumes him through this knowledge, teachings and guidance to elevate his soul to the angelic realm. And this is why when a child or an adult takes this oath for the first time in his life, in the spiritual sense, he ends one lower life to begin a higher one.

Now if we start looking at the physical process of sacrifice as dictated by SHAREEAH, the first thing you will notice, is that not every animal is suitable for sacrifice. There are only particular kinds of animals that can be chosen for sacrifice in the name of Allah. These are the goat, the cow, or the camel. Now what is common between all of these animals? The fact that they are naturally subservient to man. These are all humble animals that never harm man, but have been created for his service. They are humble creatures. This is why when you put down a goat, and even though it sees the knife coming, it does not resist. Try sacrificing a lion, and I'm sure very soon you'll see the differnce.

So what this symbolizes, is that not every person is suitable for this divine oath of the IMAM. Not everyone is ready for this angelic journey. Only people who have developed a sense of humility within their souls become eligible for this divine oath.

The next condition for the sacrifice is that the animal must be an adult. You cannot chose a kid or a ram or a calf for sacrifice. It has to be a fully grown animal. That is why we check the teeth to make sure that it has fully matured before we choose the animal. This symbolizes that the person who is about to take AHAD SHAREEF must be mentally and physically mature. This is why parents wait till puberty before they have their children take AHAD SHAREEF. Because the knowledge and the guidance that is coming ahead cannot be handled by immature people. Kids do not possess the determination that is required to remain steadfast, when faced with the challenges of these practices. That's why a person has to be physically as well as intellectualy mature before he can commit to this responsibility.

The next condition for the sacrifice is that the animal should not be defective in its form. This means that you cannot pick an animal that has one eye, or has any body parts missing or in excess. Now if you think about this just from an outward aspect, it does not make much sense. We don't eat the eyes! We don't eat the ears! So what if it has one part missing? It's of no benefit to us anyway right? So what if a goat has 5 legs instead of 4. Good for us, right! More bang for our buck! To understand this you have to undrestand two terms.

> — *Image text (from image 029; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/029.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

GHULOO means to make expensive; and QULOO means to make cheap. How do you make something expensive or cheap? You make something expensive by increasing its price to something it is not worth; and you make it cheap by lowering its price to a value that is not its worth. If I have a pen that is worth $10, and I try to sell it to you for $50, that's غُلُو; and if I try to sell it to you for $1 that's قُلُو. Because justice dictates that I price a thing at the value it deserves. So GHULOO and QULOO are both forms of injustice. So for example MAULANA ALI AS has a certain station in the hierarchy of our religion. Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) saw him fit and worthy to be his successor. This is why he appointed him as his caliph on the day of GHADEER.

من کنت مولاہ فھذا علی مولاہ

Anyone who considered me as their master, from this day forth Ali is his master.

In other words, he set a value for him. And if you want to understand the value of a WASEE, it comes right after the NATIQ in rank. That's how high WASAYAH is priced. Now if you take someone (or three people) who are dirt cheap in the hiearchy of religion, and you over estimate them by placing them in the station of Maulana Ali (AS), that's GHULOO. That is over valuing the worth of certain people who are not worthy of that rank. And when you lower Maulana Ali (AS) to the rank of the 4th caliph, that is QULOO; that is undervaluing the worth of Maulana Ali (AS).

So the act of picking an animal that has no defect, symbolizes choosing a believer, who can properly balance the various ranks that exist in the hierarcy of religion. A person who has doubts, or moral and ethical defects is not eligible for the divine oath.  A person who believes, so what if ABU BAKR, UMAR and USMAN became the caliphs - it's all one and the same thing. It's all one religion. Maulana Ali as the first or the 4th, makes no difference - such a person is not eligible for AHAD SHAREEF. He is an animal that is either missing body parts or has parts in excess of what it should have.

Now that the animal or the believer has been chosen for sacrifice, the actual process of ZABEEHA begins by facing the animal towards the QIBLA. This symbolizes providing the believer with the recognition of his Imam; because IMAM is the one true QIBLA for a believer soul.

After that the animal is fed a few drops of water. You don't dunk the animals head in a bucket! You give it just a bit to wet its throat which reduces the sting of the blade, and makes the transition easier for the animal. This symbolizes educating the believer and making him aware of the importance of the divine oath, through rational and empirical evidences. Water represents knowledge; and so a believer cannot be taken into the divine oath without first being given some basic knowledge of the fundamental principles of religion. The truth needs to be separated from falsehood through knowledge, before a person can take AHAD SHAREEF.

Then another requirement for sacrifice is that the animals jugular be slit with a very sharp knife. You cannot use a blunt knife for ZABEEHA. That violates the entire process. What this symbolizes is that the believers doubts and suspicions should be put to rest, with extremely concrete and powerful arguments that he simply cannot refute. One cannot use flimsy or weak arguements when taking AHAD of a believer.

Once the jugular is cut, the animal is left to bleed out entirely. "Blood" symbolizes doubts and suspicions in the spiritual realm. So with the blade of definitive and concrete proofs, the believers doubts and suspicions are bled out, until he is completely satisified and there is not a single doubt left within his soul.

What happens at this point? The animal convulses! It shakes, not because it's in pain; but because oxygen is no longer reaching the brain. So it starts shaking violently and then becomes still - it becomes completely motionless. This is the believer letting go of all of his doubts. Things he believed all his life; things that were taught to him in school by teachers; things his friends made him believe; he goes through this process of letting go of all of his previous incorrect beliefs. That's not a comfortable process! That's not an easy process! But then what happens? It becomes completely still. Once the process of sacrifice is over, all the animals movements come to a complete stop. It becomes completely subservient to us. It no longer moves until we makes it move. No matter what we do to it from that point on, it does not resits. In other words, it completely submits itself to us. And we then disintegrate it; we separate from it the bad parts, the inedible parts; and we consume the good parts. We make it a part of our bodies! We elevate it from the rank of mass, to the rank of energy, which is then spent in acts of worship ordained by Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala).

This is the believer taking the oath of his IMAM, and putting an end to all of his own movements that were governed and controlled by his desires, passions and love of this world. He submits himself in the hands of the Imam, who then through his knowledge and guidence, removes the bad components from his soul, and consumes the good. Because the MOMIN who has taken AHAD shareef now begins acting like the IMAM; as it he is now a part of the IMAM. He acts like him, speaks like him, thinks like him. The imam helps him achieve these spiritual heights which would never have been possible for it without his gudiance. In other words, by submitting to the IMAM, the believer allows for an incredible spiritual transformation, that makes him desirable to the angels.
