He becomes someone that the angels desire to keep company with.

See if a piece of meat comes on our plate that does not look right, we don't eat it! We toss it aside? Why? Because it didn't look appealing; it didn't look appetizing! It's the same with our souls. If we don't make our souls beautiful with the teachings of our Imams, angels, that are at a higher level from us, won't even touch us. They won't have anything to do with us. So this spiritual transformation is key for our progression, which can only be achieved, not just through the superficial act of AHAD SHAREEF, but by actually working on the teachings of this religion.

So the process of sacrifice is a reminder for our submission to the one who is put in charge over us. To submit our free will to the command of the IMAM, allowing him to transform us into a state that can be consumed by higher forms.

---

Muslims see the intellect as a gift. The AQAL is the greatest of all gifts.  it is the crown of creation!  and a gift should be used for that for which it was intended,  according to the Islamic tradition. 

 now the western civilization looks at the intellect as  something that is cut and dry,  precise,  unfeeling,  insensitive rational and analyzing critical tool. From a Muslim point of view the intellect relates to perception.  and gods REHMA or love and compassion is  the necessary thing to be perceived. the intellect sees things as they truly are.  it is a life that God puts in the heart of the believer  through which people are able to see things as they truly are.  so the intellect is an organ of perception.  so if I am seeing someone suffering and if my intellect  truly understands what that means,  then empathy emerges.  so that is part of the function of the intellect.

Ahad importance

There is a HADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) where a man came to the prophet and asked, who is a witness to your prophethood? He said:
⟪ar:یَشھَدُ لِی کُلَّ حَجَرٍ وَ مَدَرٍ⟫

Every stone and clay is a witness and testifies to my prophethood. Now if you look at this HADEES at face value, it couldn't possibly be true. We don't see stones and pots of clay witnessing the prophet and saying اشھد ان محمد رسول اللہ . So obviously there is more to this HADEES than its literal meaning. So what does it mean?

First of all if you look at anything in this universe, from a dust mote to the tallest mountain; it is surrounded by 6 sides, or 6 directions. Up, down, right, left, front, back. Anything that has physical mass is enclosed from 6 sides; and the thing itself is the 7th entity.

---

Details of the USOOL

Our USOOL Al-DEEN comprise of:
- TAWHEED - the oneness of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala),
- NUBUWWAH (prophethood),
- WASAAYAH (legacy),
- IMAMAH (Imamate)
- QAYAMAH (Resurrection)

In our SULEMANI tradition, all these concepts are encapsulate in one word - WALAYAH! WALAYH is the rubric under which all these other principles are subsumed. And so another way to look at this, is that the ⟪ar:أُصُولَ⟫are the fundamental truths, that are contained within WILAYAH. The ⟪ar:فُرُوع⟫, are the external manifestations of those USOOL, in the form of TAHARAH, SALAAH, ZAKAAT, SAUM, HAJJ and JEHAD.

The idea behind these rituals and spiritual practices, is that they serve as a means by which we can attain the inner comprehension of these theological truths, and realities of faith. The principles of IMAN; the structure of all the revelatory propositions; the mechanics of how the spiritual realm operates, its conditions, its pre-requisites, its subtelties - everything has been embodied within the structure of our Islamic practices. So you can think of it as an outside-in approach. So for example we begin by studying a leaf. We first study its external apprearance. Why is every leaf symmetrical? Why does a leaf have veins? what's the purpose of these veins? What are they deliverying? And then what is the source of that delivery? So the study of the vein leads us to the branches; the branches connect us to the trunk; the trunk takes us to the roots. It takes us into the realm of the that which exists but is unseen. And then the roots connect us with all that exists in its surrounding, which in our metaphore are the articles of faith.

We know that the earth and the roots never change. What lies under the earth never changes. Changes occur in what comes out of the earth. Similarly the USOOL [the principles] of the spiritual realm never change, but the FUROO [the practices] are subject to change in their forms and method, in order to adapt to the changing environment. So for instance, the purpose and the essence of prayer never changes. It's always to connect with our master. But the practice of prayer can change to adapt to every person's unique situation. If you can't stand in prayer, you can sit on a chair and pray. If not, you can lie down on the floor and pray. If not even that, let's say someone is completely paralysed from the neck down, he can simply turn his face to the QIBLA and pray with his eyes. So the external form of prayer can change; but the essence; the USOOL, the reason for prayer never changes.

So now if we look at⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫as a whole, we can see that WILAYAH comprises our IMAAN. It is made up of the knowledge of all the revelatory propositions that the Quran talks about, that are supported by our empirical and rational knowledge. And then ISLAM comprises of the DAYAM, the physical practices that take place in the span of a lifetime. In other words, WILAYAH are the roots, while the remaining 6 practices of ISLAM (TAHARAH, SALAAH, ZAKAAT, SAUM, HAJJ and JEHAD) form the tree.

Comparison of a true believer to a tree

And so what we're learning here is that a true MOMIN is like a good tree; or a good word. His life in this world is like a beautiful tree, or a good word, comprising of both aspects. He has a beautiful ISLAM; that is visible like the branches of a tree, or the letters and symbols of a good word. And that ISLAM is sustained by the roots of his IMAN, that go deep within the earth of the theological principles of TAWHEED. In other words, his IMAN draws its nourishment from TAWHEED in order to sustain his ISLAM.

This is really important to understand, because what happens to a tree that does not have strong roots? It gets uprooted by the weakest wind! Similarly if a person's ISLAM is not strongly rooted in IMAN, it will be uprooted by the smallest tribulation. See, ISLAM is like the ⟪ar:فُرُوع⟫, like the branches of a tree is exposed to the hardships of its environment. It is exposed to all kinds of hardships; heat of the scorching sun, cold of chilly nights, harm from insects. But if the roots are strong, nothing can harm that tree. So if our IMAN is satiated with the nourishment of TAWHEED, the trials and tribulations of this world that our ISLAM is challenged with, become extremely easy to bear. Heaven or hell is never the concern of a true MOMIN. It is ⟪ar:معرفۃ الرَّب⟫, the awareness and the recognition of his master. This is why MAULANA Ali in his supplications would say:
⟪ar-quote:یا الہی ما عبدتک من شوق جنتک ولا من خوف النارک⟫

Oh Allah! I do not worship you out of the enticement of your JANNAH; nor do I worship you out of the fear of hellfire.
⟪ar-quote:بل وجدت مستحق لی العبادۃ فالعبدتک⟫

Indeed I found you worthy of worship, and for that reason alone I worship you!

We've looked at the aspects and characteristics of a good tree and a good word. Now lets talk about their purpose. What is the purpose of a good tree? And what is the purpose of a good word? The primary purpose of a beneficial tree is its fruits; and the primary purpose of a good speech is to convey the intention of the speaker. Are fruits the first thing that show up on a tree? Or are they the last thing that show up? It's always the last thing. Is the intention of the speaker the first thing we get to, or the last? It's the last. We first hear the words, grasp its meanings and then get to the intention of the speaker. And so what is the ultimate purpose of one's ISLAM and IMAN? What is the ultimate fruit of a true believers efforts? It is IHSAAN, the beatific vision of his master. It is finally meeting the beloved.
⟪ar-quote:الدَّواءَ الحُب الأِتِّصَال⟫

The cure of love is meeting the beloved.

And then Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَالَ لِلنَّاسِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ⟫

And Allah sets forth examples for mankind so that they may remember. Because the principles of all revelatory propositions has been placed within the structure of rational and empirical observations. Now are we surrounded by trees? Which means from now on, everytime we see a tree, we should be reminded of the example of a good MOMIN. Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) surrounded us by reminders of who we are supposed to be. Any attribute you find in a good tree, you will find in a good MOMIN.

A tree has two aspects. The first is geared towards it own nourishement and sustenance. A tree is sustained through a constant supply of water; a believer is sustained through a constant supply of beneficial knowledge. Once a tree reaches its maturity, it begins to bear fruits. It gains the ability to nourish others. A believer is one who works on himself (on his own knowledge of TAWHEED), until he reaches maturity and perfection in that realms, and then becomes able to nourish others as well with his knowledge. And a tree does not just nourish humans with its fruits; it also nourishes animals with its leaves; and insects with its branches. A believer does not just benefit other MOMINS and MUSLIMS; he benefits non-muslims and disbelievers as well with his knoweldge and actions. A tree stands in the scorching heat of the sun, and yet provides shade to the one who sit under it. A true MOMIN suffers and endures hardships in order to provide comforts to the people around him. Humans breathe in oxygen and exhale carbon dioxide; while trees breathe in carbon dioxide and exhale oxygen. So a tree absorbs the waste product of others and yet provides good to them. A believer bears and absorbs the evil acts and speech of the ignorant people around him; and returns their evil with good; he returns their harsness with kindness; their painful speech with gentle and kind responses. A tree is predictable and consistent in what it produces. An apple tree will always produce apples, it will never produce mangoes. A mango tree will always produce mango, never oranges. A MOMIN is consistent and predictable in his behavior. People can safely make assumptions about his kindness, his generosity, his courage, the wisdom of his recomemndations. A tree will stand tall in the face of natural calamities; a true believer remains steadfast in the face of all trials and hardships.

<!-- section 13 (id=5790, raw_sort=13): Review of ISLAM -->

## Review of Islām

Meaning of DEEN

Our religion is called ⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫, which is generally translated as the religion of Islam.

The word DEEN in the Arabic language comes from the root word ⟪ar:دَیْن⟫, which has several meanings.

The first variation ⟪ar:دَانَ⟫، ⟪ar:یَدِینُ⟫means "to discpline the soul". Because by its inherent nature, the soul is rebellious. So  ⟪ar:دَانَ⟫، ⟪ar:یَدِینُ⟫mean to tame the soul.

⟪ar:دَانَ⟫is also used to describe a particular type of rain that falls over and over again bringing the dead earth back to life. The earth doesn't become alive just after one rainfall. It takes many many iterations to bring it back to life. Discipline works the same way. The soul doesn't get disciplined after the first attempt. It takes many attempts to slowly and gradually bring it under control. It fails many times, before it succeeds once. So ⟪ar:دَانَ⟫means to gradually discipline the soul, or slowly bring the dead earth back to life.

Another meaning comes from the word  "⟪ar:دَیْن⟫" which means a "debt".

And then there is of course the generic use of the word ⟪ar:دَیْن⟫ which means "a way of life".

So these are the various meanings we find in the root word of ⟪ar:دِین⟫.

Meaning of ISLAM

The next word is ISLAM, which comes from the root word ⟪ar:سَلَمَ⟫which means "submission". Its verbal form is ⟪ar:أَسلَمَ⟫- which means "to submit" or "to surrender". Surrender what? To surrender one's free will, to the will of the creator".

Another derivitive of the word is ⟪ar:سلام⟫which means peace.

⟪ar-quote:يَهْدِى بِهِ ٱللَّهُ مَنِ ٱتَّبَعَ رِضْوَنَهُۥ سُبُلَ ٱلسَّلَمِ⟫

It is by the Quran that Allah guides those who pursue His pleasure to the path of *peace*. ⟪ar:سلام⟫also means "safety"

⟪ar-quote:قُلْنَا يَا نَارُ ! كُونِي بَرْدًا وَسَلَامًا عَلَىٰ إِبْرَاهِيمَ⟫

Allah said, "O fire! become cool and safe upon Ibraheem. So the word ISLAM contains several different meanings. Its primary meaning is of submission, but within that submission, it also contains the meanings of peace and safety. And this is why free will becomes such an important component of ISLAM. It is submission by one's own free will. If the submission happens out of compulsion, or force, or fear; if the component of peace and safety is lost, then it's no longer ISLAM in the true sense of the word.  This why Allah says:

⟪ar-quote:لَآ إِكْرَاهَ فِى ٱلدِّينِ⟫

There is no compulsion in DEEN

⟪ar-quote:قَد تَّبَيَّنَ ٱلرُّشْدُ مِنَ ٱلْغَىِّ⟫

⟪ar:رشد⟫in Arabic means "rationality" or "reason". From that we get the meaning of the "right way", "the correct path". رشد also means to ripen or reach maturity.   ⟪ar:غی⟫on the other hand comes from the root word ⟪ar:غوی⟫which means seduction, temptation, enticement. It also means a "snare or a trap".  So imagine a path that is laid with landmines under the surface. But on the top you see these beautiful flowers with amazing colors and fragrance. Such a path would be called ⟪ar:غی⟫. Because you will get enticed by the beauty of the flowers but when you move towards it, you'll be blown to bits. Now imagine someone actually making it safely to the other end of the path, and he marks out the path of safety for you. He draws out a line on that path, that if you walk on this line you will be safe. That line of safety would be called ⟪ar:رشد⟫in Arabic. Now messengers are people that have safely made it across this path of landmines. And they've marked out the path of safety for us, and this is why one of the titles of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is ⟪ar:الرَّشید⟫. The one who guides to the right way; the one who guides through reason and rationalle; the one who brings to maturity.

So Allah says:

⟪ar-quote:لَآ إِكْرَاهَ فِى ٱلدِّينِ... قَد تَّبَيَّنَ ٱلرُّشْدُ مِنَ ٱلْغَىِّ⟫

There is no compulsion in religion. The path of reason and rationality has been clearly identified and separated, from the path laid with traps of entincement, seductions, and temptations. Now its up to you. You choose the spots where you wish to step. So inherent with the meaning of  ⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫, is a willing submission. This particular submission or surrender, cannot be unwilling, forceful, or compulsive in nature.

And so now, based on all these linguistic nuances, if you combine both the words DEEN and ISLAM together, they generate some very interesting meanings.  Allah says

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ ٱلدِّينَ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلْإِسْلَمُ⟫

Indeed the DEEN of Allah has always been AL-ISLAM. So ⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫, can now mean, to discipline one's soul for submission. To train the soul through a self-governed process of disciplinary actions to slowly and gradually making is subservient to the will of Allah. 

In the context of peace and safety, ⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫, it can mean to submit the soul to Allah, in order to find peace and tranquility. It can also mean to submit the soul to Allah, in order to to become safe from the dangers (the traps of desires, passions and temptation) of this life.
Another meaning that comes out from this combination, is to bring the dead soul back to life; because ⟪ar:دَانَ⟫is a rain that brings the dead earth back to life. So ⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫, can also mean to bring the dead soul back to life, through the act of submission. But the most interesting concept is the context of ⟪ar:دَیْن⟫, which means debt. This idea, that we have been blessed with innumerable gifts by our creator for which we owe him a willing debt of submission. And he reminds us of this debt in the Quran by saying:

⟪ar-quote:أَفَغَيْرَ دِينِ ٱللَّهِ يَبْغُونَ⟫

Do they seek other than the DEEN of Allah? Do they seek something other than the repayment of this debt that they owe Allah?

⟪ar-quote:وَلَهُ  أَسْلَمَ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ طَوْعًۭا وَكَرْهًۭا⟫

While all creatures in the heaven and the earth have bowed down to him in submission, willingly or unwillingly. In this verse he mentions two kinds of submissions. A willing submission, and an unwilling submission. Because the word ⟪ar:أسْلَمَ⟫ is also used for "death", which is the final and ultimate submission - ⟪ar:أسْلَمَ نَفسُہُ⟫ He surrendered or submitted his soul; he give up the ghost. Allah says to his beloved messenger in the Quran:

⟪ar-quote:وَمَا جَعَلْنَا لِبَشَرٍۢ مِّن قَبْلِكَ ٱلْخُلْدَ⟫

And We did not grant eternity to any man before you

⟪ar-quote:أَفَإِي۟ن مِّتَّ فَهُمُ ٱلْخَلِدُونَ؟⟫

And if someone like you is going to die, what makes them think they will remain forever?
⟪ar-quote:كُلُّ نَفْسٍۢ ذَآئِقَةُ ٱلْمَوْتِ.....  وَنَبْلُوكُم بِٱلشَّرِّ وَٱلْخَيْرِ فِتْنَة وَإِلَيْنَا تُرْجَعُونَ⟫

Every soul will taste death. And We test you with evil and with good as trial, and to us you will be returned.

So the idea is, that for every living creature, there is an appointed time, when its final submission is going to take place. And that is going to be an unwilling submission. So during this short span of life, we have a choice. We can either choose to discipline our souls; we can choose to breadth life into our souls; by freely, willingly, and peacefully submitting it to the commands of our master. We can choose the path of ⟪ar:رشد⟫, or we can choose the path of ⟪ar:غوی⟫- the path of enticement and temptations of this world. But either way, that final moment is coming when we will all be stripped of our choice; and we will have to surrender this soul to our master. Allah says in Surah WAQIAH

⟪ar-quote:فَلَوْلَآ إِذَا بَلَغَتِ ٱلْحُلْقُومَ⟫

When the soul reaches your throat

⟪ar-quote:وَأَنتُمْ حِينَئِذٍۢ تَنظُرُونَ⟫

and you are watching this process taking place. Make it go back! Allah challenges us, "If you are the one in control, then make it go back! Make this process stop!". And then he says:

⟪ar-quote:وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنكُمْ وَلَكِن لَّا تُبْصِرُونَ⟫

We are closer to your soul than you are, but you do not see it. In other words, death is right around the corner but you're not mindful of it. You are in a state of constant delusion. You think you have a lot of time. We make plans for what we'll be doing when we're 80; and yet we don't know if tonight is the night that we will have to sleep in a our graves. Because all those who died in their 20s and 30s - they had long term goals. They had plans! Many of them woke up in the morning, completely unaware of the fact, that they will never return to their beds again.

So just within the words of ⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫ , we find the true essential meanings that lie hidden within the practices of ISLAM. So now if someone asks us, what is ⟪ar:دین الاسلام⟫? We can say:

ISLAM is to gradually discipline the soul; ISLAM is to slowly bring the dead soul back to life, through a willing, peaceful and complete submission to the will Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), in order to find peace, tranquility and safety. And this willing submission needs to take place in this short gap that we call life, before that ultimate moment arrives, when all of creation will "have" to submit to its creator willingly or unwillingly. Those who have already submitted their souls will find the process of death extremely easy. But those who chose to remain arrogant, will now find this submission extremely painful.

Because ISLAM, ultimately is an "experience". People think ISLAM is an action. Yes! It is a practice! But what comes out of every action? An experience! When you go on vacations and holidays, its an "act". There is a lot of action involved in making that holiday happen! But what do you return with? You return with an experience!And so we practice the "acts" of ISLAM our entire lives, in order to return with an "experience", that takes place at the moment of our death.

Now an experience can be of two types. You can have a divine experience, or you can have a demonic experience. What's the difference?

A demonic experience is "always" accompanied with an expansion of the self. In other words, the act is a very exciting and joyful experience. But then it always ends in despair; in guilt; in pain; in shame. On the contrary, a true spiritual experience is exactly the opposite. The initial experience is always incredible "constriction and fear and dread"; but then it is followed by a sense of expansion of the self. It ends in immense happiness and pleasure.

And now if measure ISLAM against this criteria, it begins with a constriction. The life of a MUSLIM, who has submitted his soul to Allah, he experiences immesnse constriction; immense restrictions; a fear of potential loss. Because the path of ISLAM is binding, it is very restrictive. Don't do this, don't do that; don't eat this; don't drink that; don't watch that; don't think that; don't say that; don't think that. Pray 5 times a day; Give your money in charity; fast 30 days in a year - all very constricting acts. Life is a long wide path, but we're asked to carefully walk this extremely fine line of RUSHD that has been drawn for us. It is extremely restrictive. But when this life ends by the hands of the ultimate suppressor! Death! It ends in an incredible expansion with immense pleasure. Death becomes a beautiful thing for the believer. The path widens up! Imam Jaffar AsSadiq AS, pointed to his throat and said, "When the soul of a believer reaches here, he feels immense happiness". In other words, the soul hasn't even left the body yet, and the believer begins experiencing the pleasures of the divine realm.

Now on the other hand, if you leave the path of ISLAM, this world begins with an incredible amount of joy and pleasure. The joy of fulfilling desires, of temptations; physical pleasures; sensual sensation; vanity; looking good; physical comforts. The world beings with an incredible expansion of the self; because it offers a demonic experience. And by definition, a demonic experience begins with an expansion of the soul. But at the moment of death, it ends in an extremely constricted and painful experience.

And this is why, if you look at the experience of JANNAH in the Quran, you find no restrictions

⟪ar-quote:كُلُوا۟ وَٱشْرَبُوا۟ مِن رِّزْقِ ٱللَّهِ⟫

Eat and drink of that which Allah has provided for you

⟪ar-quote:لَا يَسْمَعُونَ فِيهَا لَغْوًۭا وَلَا تَأْثِيمًا إِلَّا قِيلًۭا سَلَمًۭا سَلَمًۭا ‎⟫

You will not hear any sinful speech , except that of peace and trangquility

⟪ar-quote:هُمْ وَأَزْوَجُهُمْ فِى ظِلَلٍ عَلَى ٱلْأَرَآئِكِ مُتَّكِـُٔونَ ... لَهُمْ فِيهَا فَكِهَةٌۭ وَلَهُم مَّا يَدَّعُونَ ‎⟫

They will have whatever fruits they desire, and everything they ask for.

JANNAH is described as limitless freedom. You never find the word "don't" or "can't" with the experiences of JANNAH in the Quran. On the other hand, if you look at how hell is described. It is extreme constrictions; complete restrictions

⟪ar-quote:يُرِيدُونَ أَن يَخْرُجُوا۟ مِنَ ٱلنَّارِ وَمَا هُم بِخَرِجِينَ مِنْهَا ۖ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌۭ مُّقِيمٌۭ ‎⟫

They will long to get out of the Fire, but they will never be able to, and for them will be a lasting torment

⟪ar-quote:وَتَرَى ٱلْمُجْرِمِينَ يَوْمَئِذٍۢ مُّقَرَّنِينَ فِى ٱلْأَصْفَادِ ‎⟫

And you will see the criminals on that Day, bound together in chains

⟪ar-quote:سَرَابِيلُهُم مِّن قَطِرَانٍۢ وَتَغْشَىٰ وُجُوهَهُمُ ٱلنَّارُ⟫

Their garments will be of tar, and their faces will be covered with fire

So hellfire is described as a place of incredible restrictions. Another thing that's very interesting, is that in the Quran, the life of a believer is described as hard work (practices of Islam, making difficult choices), but the afterlife is described as complete relaxation. You won't find any work or practices described for the believer in the Quran. On the other hand, the life of a disbeliever, is described as entertainment and distraction

⟪ar-quote:وَمَا الْحَيَاةُ الدُّنْيَا إِلَّا لَعِبٌ وَلَهْوٌ⟫

And what is the life of this world except amusement and distraction? But the afterlife of a disbeliever is described as torment and painful focus. Because it's not like they'll ever get used to the pain and be able to ignore it. And they're desribed as constantly working to get out of their miserable states. Constantly trying to escape the hellfire and angels pushing them back into it.

In other words to follow DEEN AL-ISLAM, is a choice. It is a choice to willingly and rationality (using the intellect) choose this path of restriction and constriction; and to give up our whims and desires in submission to the will of Allah, in order to achieve complete freedom in the next life. To practice ISLAM in this world in order to gain its rewards in the form of a divine experience in the next world. And to not follow ISLAM is also a conscious rational choice. It is to choose the freedom, the vain pleasures, the amusements and distractions of this world, in order to have a painful experience in the afterlife.

There is a HADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in which he says, "Pay the worker his due before the sweat of his labour dries up". Now if we just take this HADEES literally, then there is nothing special about this statement. Any man of average intelligence and basic decency already knows that you should pay a person his due after he has completed his work. So then if an average person can tell us this, then why do we need a prophet for this kind of advise. The thing is that there is a not a single word that the propeth (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) has ever said, that is not filled with profound wisdoms. What he meant by that statement, that "Pay the worker his due before the sweat of his labour dries up". The worker is the believer! And the work he has done is his practices of Islam. His sweat is essence of his work that is now part of his soul. So even before his soul leaves his body at the time of death; in other words, before his sweat dries up, he is given the rewards of his labour. He begins experiencing the pleasures of the afterlife. It is that immense expansion that he feels as a reward of a life time of servitude to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). Because he gets to experience the divine presence.

And this is exactly what we find in the study of the prophet's seerah. His journey began with extreme constriction. All kinds of restrictions; all kinds of obstacles in his path. Dealing with disbelievers, polytheists. People calling him a poet, a magician; people calling him insane. Even when the first revelation came to him, he described it as extreme constriction. He said Jibraeel AS squeezed me 3 times, and the squeeze was so hard that he said he felt his ribs would break.

But how did his journey of prophethood end? It ended in ⟪ar:معراج⟫. It ended in the beautific vision of  Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). It ended in immense expansion!

---

Islam as the religion of all prophets

So this is ISLAM at a very personal level. But when you zoom out at a more general level; in terms of its message of guidance; ISLAM takes on two more meanings.

ISLAM as the universal religion of all prophets. Allah says in the Quran:

**(http://quran.com/2/133)**

⟪ar-quote:أَمْ كُنتُمْ شُهَدَآءَ إِذْ حَضَرَ يَعْقُوبَ ٱلْمَوْتُ إِذْ قَالَ لِبَنِيهِ مَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِنۢ بَعْدِى⟪ar-quote:؟⟫⟫

Were you witnesses when death came to Yaqoob? Behold! He said to his sons, what will you worship after me?

⟪ar-quote:قَالُوا۟ نَعْبُدُ إِلَهَكَ وَإِلَهَ آبَآئِكَ إِبْرَهِۦمَ وَإِسْمَعِيلَ وَإِسْحَقَ إِلَهًۭا وَحِدًۭا⟫

They said we shall worship your god and the god of your fathers of Ibrahim, Ismaeel and Ishaq. And then they say:

⟪ar-quote:وَنَحْنُ لَهُۥ مُسْلِمُونَ⟫

We are all on Muslims!

So what's being emphasized in this verse, is that Islam is also the religion of IBRAHEEM, ISMAEEL and ISHAQ (AS). Because what they're saying in this verse is that we will submit and surrender our will to your god, and the god of those who went before you, and we are Muslims! Similarly, there is another verse

**http://quran.com/5/111**

⟪ar-quote:وَإِذْ أَوْحَيْتُ إِلَى ٱلْحَوَارِيِّۦنَ أَنْ آمِنُوا۟ بِى وَبِرَسُولِى.....⟫

And behold! I inspired the disciples to have faith in me and my messenger, 

⟪ar-quote:قَالُوٓا۟ آمَنَّا وَٱشْهَدْ بِأَنَّنَا مُسْلِمُونَ⟫

and they said we have faith; and we bear witness that we bow to Allah as Muslims. The disciples (the HAWARIYYEEN) mentioned in this verse, are the disciples of Jesus, but they're saying we have faith and we bow down to Allah as MUSLIMS. So here again what is being emphasized, is the idea that Jesus and his disciples were all on the path of ISLAM. ISLAM is an unbroken chain of guidance. ISLAM is not something new.

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ ٱلدِّينَ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلْإِسْلَمُ⟫

Indeed the DEEN of Allah has always been AL-ISLAM. Our prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) did not see himself as bringing a "new" religion. He really saw himself as the renewer of all previous traditions.

And this is why AL-ISLAM has 7 letters. Each letter represents one of the 7 NUTAQA that have been sent for the guidance of humanity across the span of time. So the letter ALIF sybolizes ADAM (AS), LAAM sybolizes NOOH (AS), the next ALIF symbolizes IBRAHEEM (AS), SEEN symbolizes MOOSA (AS), LAAM sybolizes EISA (AS), ALIF symbolizes our beloved prophet MUHAMMAD (PBUH), and the last MEEM represents the one who is going to come in the future, and that is QAIM (AS).

So that's the first meaning in the generic sense - ISLAM as an unbroken chain of guidance from the beginning of time.

Islam specifically as the religion of Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)

And then there is also the meaning of ISLAM being specifically the religion of Muhammad Mustafa (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). Allah says:

> — *Image text (from image 031; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/031.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

On this day, I have "perfected" your religion for you, and I have "completed" my blessings upon you and approved ISLAM as your DEEN. And so, just as the word AL-ISLAM begins with the letter ALIF and is completed and perfected by the letter MEEM; the DEEN of Allah that began with the ALIF of ADAM AS, has now been perfected and completed by the MEEM of Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam).

From a practical stand point, ISLAM is made up of 7 components which are also called the 7 pillars of ISLAM. These are the 7 physical practices of

⟪ar-quote:ولایۃ، طھارۃ ، صلواۃ، زکواۃ، صوم، حج، جھاد⟫

And we will begin looking at each one of these in detail InshaAllah

<!-- section 14 (id=5792, raw_sort=14): Review of IMAN -->

## Review of Īmān

EMAN

In the previous session we looked at the various linguistic meanings of the word ISLAM. It comes from the root word ⟪ar:سَلَمَ⟫which means to submit. Another meaning of the word comes from the word ⟪ar:سلام⟫, which means peace. So baked within the meaning of the word ISLAM is not just submission, but "peaceful" submission; "voluntary" submission. Now the next word is IMAN, which comes from the root word ⟪ar:أَمَنْ⟫. And ⟪ar:أَمَنْ⟫ means "safety". Now its interesting that "safety" is inherently associated with "peace". You cannot have peace until you are safe. Peace is a natural consequence of safety. So you need to have ⟪ar:امن⟫in order to have ⟪ar:سلام⟫; just as you need IMAN in order to have ISLAM. If you do not believe in Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), you are not going to practice Islam. So this relationship between ISLAM and IMAN, even at the linguistic level is quite fascinating.

If we study these words grammatically, ISLAM and IMAN are both nouns. What's their verbal forms? The verbal form for ⟪ar:السلام⟫is ⟪ar:أَسلَمَ⟫ ; and the verbal form for ⟪ar:ایمان⟫is ⟪ar:أٓمَنَ⟫. And they're both from the 4th form of the verb. Each noun in arabic has 15 verbal forms. And every form adds a linguistic nuance to the meaning of the word.

So for example, if you look at the word for "action" in Arabic, the word is ⟪ar:فعل⟫, which means "action".

Its first verbal form is, ⟪ar:فَعَلَ⟫, which means "to act".

The second form is ⟪ar:فَعَّلَ⟫, which means "to make someone else act".

The third is ⟪ar:فاعَلَ⟫, which describes "someone else doing an act".

The fourth form is ⟪ar:أَفعَلَ⟫, which means to cause an act to happen.

And so ⟪ar:أَسلَمَ⟫and ⟪ar:أٓمَنَ⟫are both from this 4th form of the verb ⟪ar:أَفعَلَ⟫. And so ⟪ar:أَسلَمَ⟫grammatically mean, "to make submission happen". And ⟪ar:أٓمَنَ⟫means to "make safety happen". How do you make submission happen? Through the 7 pillars of Islam.

⟪ar:ولایۃ ، طھارۃ، صلواۃ، زکواۃ، صوم، حج، جھاد⟫

When we practice these 7 pillars pillars of Islam, we are literally "making" submission happen. 

And how do you make ⟪ar:أٓمَنَ⟫or safety happen? By believing in the 7 articles of faith, which are: 1. Allah
2. his angels
3. the divine books
4. the messengers
5. the day of judgment
6. heaven and
7. hell

By believeing in these 7 articles of faith, we are literally creating safety for us. We are making safety happen - in this world and in the hereafter. So both components have a conceptual meaning, and they both have a practical application. The conceptual meaning of ISLAM, is willing and peaceful submission. It's application is through the practice of the 7 pillars of ISLAM. The conceptual meaning of IMAN, is achieving safety. And the practical application of it is rationally and intellectually convincing the soul about the existence of these 7 articles of faith.

---

Syedna Qazi Noman (QR) in his book ⟪ar:دعائم الاسلام⟫ quotes ⟪ar:امام جعفر الصادق علیہ السلام⟫who definee EMAN as a combination of 3 things:

⟪ar-quote:تَصدِیقُ بِالِجنَان ؛ وَ قَولُ بِالِّسَان ؛ وَعَمَلُ بِالأَرکَان⟫

EMAN is to testify with the heart; to articulate with the tongue; and to act with the limbs.

In other words, there are 3 conditions for each of these 7 articles of faith. So if we take the first article, which is belief in Allah, within just this one article, we will find 3 requirements or conditions. The first is ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫ ; to testify with the heart for the glory and majesty of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). The second is ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫ , to articulate that belief through speech. By verbally glorifying Allah, and revealing his magnificence with the tongue. And the third is ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫ , which is to get the limbs involved. In other words, once you've witnessed the glory and majesty of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), don't just talk about it; manifest that belief and speech through physical action.

So each article then necessitates 3 conditions. It requires an evolution if you will. There is a process of growth in IMAN. The first stage is silent belief (⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫); the second it verbal declaration of that belief (⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫); and the third and final one is the physical demonstration of that belief and declaration through physical action (⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫).

If we examine the 2nd article of faith, which is "belief in the angels", again it has 3 components or 3 stages. To witness and testify with the heart, that these are indeed superior creatures that are constantly in submission to their master. Then to praise those traits with the tongue, and then to strive, and to make an effort to adopt and develop those angelic characteristics within the self. And the same applies to the rest which we'll look at in detail in future sessions, InshaAllah.

---

### تصدیق بالجنان

Next I want to take a closer look at these 3 components. The first is (⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫), which is normally translated as "to testify with the heart".  ⟪ar:تصدیق⟫comes from the root word ⟪ar:صدق⟫ which means "truth". ⟪ar:تصدیق⟫is its verbal form, which means "to verify a truth". How do you verify a truth? Through empirical and rational observations, right? You either "saw" or "heard" something; or you rationally deduced something through logic by your familiarity of the emperical observations associated with that rationalle. You know fire emits smoke, so when you see smoke coming out of a building, you know that the building is on fire. So ⟪ar:تصدیق⟫has to do with empirical and rational observations.

The next word is ⟪ar:جنان⟫, which comes from the root word JIN. And the word JIN means "hidden" or "concealed". For example ⟪ar:الَّیلُ جَنَّ عَلَیہِ⟫, the night concealed or covered everything. So now what ⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫ essentially means, is "to verify the truth about that which is hidden". And as you know, all these 7 articles of faith are hidden from the 5 senses. We cannot see Allah, we cannot see his angels, we've never met his messengers, we never saw them revealing the books, we cannot see hell or heaven, and no one has seen the day of judgment take place. So all these articles of faith are hidden from us; and yet in every single prayer, we testify in the TASHAHHUD:

⟪ar-quote:الجنۃ حق و النار حق⟫۔۔⟪ar-quote:و الموت حق والبعث حق⟫

Heaven is real; hellfire is real; death is real; rising from the dead is real

⟪ar-quote:والمیزان حق والصراط حق⟫

The scale of deeds is real; the path is real;  

⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:و ان الساعۃ آتیۃُ لا ریب فیہ⟫⟫

And without a doubt, the final moment is coming.

⟪ar-quote:وان اللہ یبعث من فی القبور⟫

And on that day, Allah will raise everyone from their graves.

The word ⟪ar:تشھد⟫comes from the word SHAHADAH which actually means 2 things. It means "to witness" and it also means "to testify". If you haven't witnessed an event, and you testify for it, that's considered a false testimony. It's considered a lie. So if we just believe in Allah, the angels, his messengers, his books, the day of judgment, only because our parents said so; or the manaseeb or duaat said so; then that's not a true SHAHADAH. Because you have not witnessed it for yourself - rationally - intellectually. And so if you're testifying for something that you haven't actually witnessed, then that is a false testimony.

So (⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫) means to verify and testify for all that is hidden. How do you do that? Through knowledge (علم). Knowledge of what? Knowledge of this universe (the عالم). Allah has created this universe as empirical and rational proofs of his existence. And so what this study of the ⟪ar:عالم⟫enables us to do, is to rationally and intellectually witness Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala).

*I've done an entire session on each of these components which I'll upload for you*

But just understand for now that the first component of EMAN (⟪ar:تصدیق بالجنان⟫), is about acquiring knowledge of the unseen, through the study of this seen universe.

---

### قول بالسان

The second component is ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫, which means to articulate with the tongue. Once the heart has witnessed and testified, for these realities of faith, through knowledge; the tongue must now unveil that hidden belief through speech.  ⟪ar:لسان⟫in Arabic means two things. It means "tongue", and it also means "language". So ⟪ar:قول بالسان⟫ means to "speak with the tongue" or "to articulate through language". Speech is the first manifestation of one's belief. It's a declaration of one's belief.

When you loves someone, what's the next step? You express that love - you reveal that emotion; you "make it known" through speech. All parents love their children; but that love also needs to be declared and made known to the child through words - "I love you!". So that's the second component. We can see this phenomenon take place between lovers in this world. Love begins with an affection in the heart; and then it reaches a point where it has to be declared. It works the same way with Allah. One cannot experience divine love unless and until one has experienced worldly love. But then there is a difference between love and lust. But the problem is that in this day and age, we confuse lust with love and love with lust. InshaAllah we'll talk about love in detail when we study WALAYAH.

### عمل بالارکان

The third is,  ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫. To physically "act" on that which you believe in, and what you declare. In other words, if you love me, and you say you love me, now show it to me! Show it to me through your actions. The word ⟪ar:عمل⟫ means "action", and ⟪ar:أرکان⟫ is the plural of ⟪ar:رکن⟫which means "support". ⟪ar:رکن⟫is the thing that supports you. That's why one of the meanings of ⟪ar:رکن⟫is also "pillar", becaue pillars are used for support. They support the weight of the roof. And so ⟪ar:عمل بالارکان⟫means to "act with the limbs"; because limbs (arms and legs) are what support us in carrying out all of our taks. We rely on them!

Now what's interesting is that the first component was about knowledge. And the arabic word for knowledge is ⟪ar:علم⟫. This third component is about action; and the arabic word for action is ⟪ar:عمل⟫. And they're both made up of the same 3 letters. AIN LAAM and MEEM. And numerically, they both weigh 140.  AIN is 70, LAAM is 30 and MEEM is 40. That adds up to 140. So the idea of IMAN, is to balance the first component of ⟪ar:علم⟫, perfectly, with the third component of ⟪ar:عمل⟫. That's why both words share the same letters and have the same numerical weight. In other words, action must balance out knowledge; and knowledge must balance out action. And what connects the two together, is speech. Because speech becomes a witness between belief and action.

So let's say you invite me to your house and you serve dinner for me. And you tell me I specially prepared this meal for you. How do I know you're speaking the truth? Maybe you just served me left overs from last night - but you presented it really well, making it look fresh. So even though I will believe you, there is no physical evidence for that particular intention. But when you specifically declare you intention by saying that "I would like you to come over for dinner tonight and cooking your favorite dish for you"; and when I come over and enjoy that meal, I know your action matched your intention. But how did I come to know of it? Through what you declared! So speech then becomes a witness connecting the hidden with the seen.

---

When you tell me that you want to learn, you're expressing a hidden intentions through speech. All I hear are your words. But I don't know what lies hidden in your heart. You may be telling the truth or you may be lying. But when you take out the time to regularly and consistently attend the sessions; you are essentially balancing out your intention with action. You prove your intention through action. But what made that intention known? Your commitment to attend the sessions.

---

Now what underlies both these terms is TAWHEED; which is also termed EHSAN. And the concept of TAWHEED is seeing Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) in everything. Seeing the majesty and the glory of Allah manifest through everthing in existence - to the point that - ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ . There is no ILAH except Allah. There is nothing in creation that does not manifest the existence of Allah. So TAWHEED is where DEEN begins. TAWHEED is the seed that contains the entire structure of the tree in a dormant or passive form. ISLAM and IMAN is the growth and development of that essence.

> — *Image text (from image 032; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/032.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

<!-- section 15 (id=6794, raw_sort=15): Review of Pillars -->

## Review of the Pillars

According to the book DAYAM Al-ISLAM, there are 7 pillars of Islam. There is no mention of the word "pillars" in the Quran directly. But if you collect all the ⟪ar:أحکامات⟫(the commandments) of the Quran, they will fall into one of these 7 categories. And this is exactly what ⟪ar:سیدنا قاضی نعمان قس⟫, did in his book DAYAM Al-ISLAM. And he did not write this book out of his own volition. Just to give you a little background info about this book, the IMAM of that time, Maulana ⟪ar:امام المعز لدین اللہ⟫ commanded him to write this book. And the reason he asked him to do so, is because by that time, a lot of innovation had crept into ISLAM. There were a ridiculous number of false AHADEES that were being quoted, and attributed to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam).

So one day when Syedna Qazi Noman (QR) came to visit the IMAM (AS), the IMAM recited this Hadees of Rasul Allah(SAWAS) that:

⟪ar-quote:اذا اَظھَرتَ البِدعَ فی اُمَّتِی، فَلْیُظھَرَ العالمُ عِلمُہ⟫

Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said: When you see innovations appearing within my community, then it is obligatory on the scholar to reveal his knowledge. After reciting this HADEES, IMAM (AS) said to Syedna Qazi Noman, that by "scholar" Rasul Allah(SAWAS) meant people like you! And then he commanded him to write this book with the goal to separate truth from falsehood. And so what ⟪ar:سیدنا قاضی نعمان قس⟫did in this book was, he took all the valid AHADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and left out all the innovated ones; thus separating truth from falsehood. And when he completed the book, he presented it to IMAM MOIZ (AS), who then read every single word of it, before sanctioning it for his people. And then he addressed the people and said, "Whoever follows even the 40th portion of this book, I guarantee JANNAH for that person!". And so from that point on, this book became a constitutional book for MOMINEEN. And just to give you an idea of the importance of this book; one of the later IMAMs,  IMAM ALI-ZAAHIR (AS) commanded the people of his time to memorize this book by heart. And then he gave out huge rewards to those who did actually memorize the book.

So as I said, in this book, Syedna Qazi Noman categorizes all the ⟪ar:أحکامات⟫all the commandments of Allah into 7 distinct practices:

Wilayah, Taharah, Salaat, Zakaat, Saum, Hajj, Jehad;

But what I find really interesting, is that he named this book DAYAM Al-ISLAM, "The *Pillars* Of Islam". The Arabic word for a single pillar is ⟪ar:دعامۃ⟫; and its plural is ⟪ar:دعائم⟫.  Why would he call it pillars? What is the wisdom, behind calling these practices, "pillars" as opposed to something else. So let's first understand that. What do these practices have in common with pillars?

Generally we think, he called these 7 practices "pillars" because they are "essential" to Islam; because pillars are essential to the integrity of a structure. And that is absolutely true! But there's a lot more to it than just that. So let's first study the word pillar in the context of a structure to understand the subtle meanings in calling these practices pillars.

And you have to keep in mind that what I'm about to share is very idealistic in nature. In life we face this distinction between what is ideal and what is practical. So its OK if these teachings do not apply perfectly in our lives; or we feel we're practically incapable of practicing ISLAM a certain way. The importance of understanding any ideal scenario is to be able to align ourselves with that ideal, as closely as possible. Because we're studying the theory behind concepts in these sessions - we're studying the "rules", and there are always exceptions to the rules.

So let's look at concept of pillars to appreciate these practices. When we think of pillars, what image comes to mind? We imagine these tall vertical structures when he hear the word "pillar". So, right off the bat there is this idea that pillars are something that are on the vertical plain. They have an upward motion to them; because we always construct pillars from the ground up. In other words, it is something that is heavenly directed. They're reaching towards God.

What else do we know about pillars? They're used for constructing something. Pillars don't have a value just by themselves, unless they're used in some sort of a construction context; like building a house or a school or something. So if Syedna Qazi Noman is calling these practices "pillars", then obviously the building, or the structure they're supporting is "Islam". Hence the name: DAYAM Al-ISLAM. So there is a relationship between these practices and ISLAM. Now let's explore what that relationship is.

When constructing a building, are pillars placed randomly, or are they placed strategically? Pillars are always placed strategically. This is the first thing we find in common with the practices of ISLAM. Each practice (like pillars) is strategically placed with the life span of a believer. The pillars of TAHARAH and SALAAT are placed 5 times a day at the very least. Pillars of SAUM and ZAKAAT are placed once every year. The pillar of HAJJ is placed once in a lifetime. JEHAD is a conditional practice, that only becomes obligatory if and when the IMAM commands us to do so. So we see that each of these 6 pillars are very stratigically placed  during the lifespan of a believer. The seventh one is WALAYAH, which very interestingly, applies to every single waking moment of a believer. And we'll begin taking a closer look at this soon InshaAllah. WILAYAH is considered more a part of the foundation, than a pillar. Which brings me to my next question.

What are these pillars built upon? They're built upon a foundation. Without a foundation, pillars will not be able to bear the weight of the structure. The more solid the foundation is, the steadier the pillars will stand; and the more steady the pillars are, the more stable the building will be. So there is a direct relationship of "integrity" between these components. Now what is the foundation of the building of ISLAM? It is our creedal formula of ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ (There is no god but Allah). ISLAM stands upon the foundation of TAWHEED.

How do you put a foundation in place? You first dig a deep empty hole and then you fill it with concrete. And this is really fascinating, because the first part of our creedal formula is LA ILAHA - which represents an emptying out of the self (TAHANNUS). It represents emptying the soul of all false gods. Removing the false god of ego; of pride; of arrogance; of greed; of lust. Removing the love of this world; removing the slavery of material posessions. And then filling it with ILLA ALLAH! Filling the heart with the love of the divine presence; filling it with the love of his messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam); filling it with the love of Maulana Ali (AS); filling it with the love of the IMAMS, the DUAAT, the MANASEEB. And only after this foundation is properly set, one can start constructing the pillars of these practices on top of it.

Now in a physical structure, how do you determine if there is a crack in the foundation? You can't see it, because it's under the flooring of the house. How does a cracked foundation manifest itself to us? Through the cracks in the walls. When the foundation is cracked, you'll notice a big crack appearing on the walls; and that usually indicates that the soil under the foundation has shifted. Now you can patch up that wall all you want; but sooner or later, the crack is going to show up again. Why? Because the wall is not the problem? Where's the problem? It's in the foundation.

And its the exact same process with ISLAM. When we are not inclinded or internally motivated towards these practices; or we find ourselves not taking them seriously; In other words, when we begin to see cracks in the walls of our ISLAM, what do we do? What do we constantly try to work on? On the practice itself! I need to be more disciplined. I need to force myself to do SALAAT! I need to force myself to do ROZA. Does that work for a while? Sure! But does it last? No! Eventually we all revert back to the same lifestyles. And then soon enough, we start noticing the cracks in the wall once again, and we repeat this same vicious cycle over and over again. Why doesn't it work? Because the walls are not the problem! Where's the problem? It's in our knowlege of  LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH! Once the heart is properly emptied out with LA ILAHA, and filled with the divine presence of ILLA ALLAH, the practices automatically fall in place. It become impossible "not" to practice ISLAM. It becomes unthinkable to miss a prayer no matter what the situation in life is. So what we're learning here, is that the pillars of practices are constructed on a solid foundation; a deep understanding of the principles of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH.

Another very prominent fact about a pillar, is that once they are constructed, they cannot be moved from their place. If you decided to redecorate the house, you can tear down walls and other auxiliary structures. That's easy! It will have little, to no effect on the main structure. But if you take down a pillar, you will impact the stability of the entire building. In other words, if I'm walking in a house and I come against a pillar, I will have to walk around it; the pillar will not move for me. So the idea is, that when we encouter these pillars of practices of ISLAM; we will have to make the necessary adjustments. When it is time for SALAAT, I will have to adjust my schedule to accommodate it; SALAAT will not adjust itself for me. When the month of Ramadan comes, I have to structure my day, my life around it. It is not going to be the other way round.

Now once the foundation is set, and the pillars have been constructucted on top of it, what's the next thing we need to complete the structure? The roof! That's what necessitated all this other construction in the first place. That's the final goal! We have this common expression that we use all the time, "to put a roof on one's head". And that expression comes from the understanding that the roof or the ceiling is the final goal of a structure. We never say, "To put a floor under on'es feet", or "put pillars to one's side". No! The expression goes, "to put a roof on one's head". Now what's the direction of the placement of the roof? The direction for the pillars, was from the ground up; what's the direction for the roof? The roof or ceiling is always downward. It comes from the top and sits on top of the pillars. So the idea is, that once these practices of Islam are firmly established, and grounded in the foundation of TAWHEED; security, safety and protection come from Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), and it sits on top of these pillars of practice, thus completing the house of ISLAM. **This is why, one of the meanings of the word ISLAM is safety**. Because just as the resident feels safe within the walls of his house; a believer feels safe within this structure of ISLAM. And once he feels safe, what does he do? He submits! He willingly and happily submit to the safety of that house. We'll take it! Where do I sign? right? He goes into submission mode. **And this is why******another meaning of the word ISLAM is willing submission.****And once the person has submitted to the safety of this structure, what did we say is the natural outcome of safety? Peace! **This is why, another meaning of the word ISLAM is also peace. SubhanAllah! You have to appreciate the beauty and the wisdom behind calling these practices, pillars! SubhanAllah!**
And so what we're learning here, is that a "true" MUSLIM, is the one who literally submits to the protection and the safety of his master; that comes as a result of these solid pillars of practice that he has constructed over a deep seeded understanding of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH!

> — *Image text (from image 033; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/033.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Now once a house is built on these solid structures, does the external, climatic conditions matter to the person living in that house? No! No matter what kinds of winds are blowing outside, the person inside the house remains safe; and his heart and mind remains at peace, knowing that the mercy and love of Allah sits on top of these pillars that he has built. But if the pillars are weak, and the foundation is cracked, then does the person have good reason to fear what's happening outside? Absolutely! And this is why as soon as the social, political, or religious climate changes, you'll see certain people get extremely perturbed by it; and you'll see others completely at peace. And what you'll find, is that the one's who are disturbed by these changes, are the ones who have not constructed these pillars of practices, or they have a major flaw in their foundation of TAWHEED. So as soon as the external environment changes, their pillars begin shaking. But those who have built solid pillars upon a solid concrete foundation, they remain completely at peace, regardless of what's happening outside. Our beloved prophets life; Maulana Ali's life; Maulatina Fatima, Hassan (AS)'s life is a proof of this fact. Karbala is living proof of the fact, that when the foundation is strong, and the pillars are stable, no external calamity can disturb the heart. The body can be destroyed; it can be crushed; but the heart *always" remains at peace; if feels safe and it holds on to the unbroken submission to its master.

<!-- section 16 (id=5773, raw_sort=16): One who says LA ILAH enters paradise -->

## Whoever Says 'Lā Ilāha illā Allāh' Enters the Garden (the Hadith)

The first pillar of Islam is WALAYAH; and it comes from the root word WILA. But before we study the linguistica meanings of this word, I want to give you a general sense of this term. Because that will really help us appreciate the beauty of this term like nothing else.

"WALAYAH", according to our SULEMANI theology, is considered to be not so much a pillar, but rather a part of the foundation itself. WALAYAH stems directly from the SHAHADAH itself. So if the practices of TAHARAH, SALAAT, ZAKAAT, SAUH, HAJJ, JEHAD are the body of ISLAM, WALAYAH is its soul. It is what brings these practices to life. If you compare it to the structure of a tree, WALAYAH would be the trunk. You canot have branches, leaves, or fruits without a trunk. A trunk is what holds everything else in place. WALAYAH works exactly the same way. It holds the other practices in place; it nourishes them; feeds them and keeps them alive. In a construction project, think of it like the footings built on top of a foundation.

Today, when we look around us, we see a dead ISLAM. We find these so-called Muslims, praying 5 times a day; fasting every single day of the year; and committing horrendous acts in the name of ISLAM. But even in our personal lives we find this disconnect between the letter of the law and the spirit of the law. How many times do we practice ISLAM perfectly on the outside; but internally we're simply going through the motions. There's no heart in our prayers. There's no understanding of what we're doing and why we're doing it. And we're all guilty of this, including myself. And one of the reasons for that, is because we're missing this "essential" component of WALAYAH in our practice.

If you remember, in my explanation of ISLAM, I shared with you the TAVEEL of the verse in which Allah explains the 7 stages of development for an embryo:
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ خَلَقْنَا ٱلنُّطْفَةَ عَلَقَةًۭ فَخَلَقْنَا ٱلْعَلَقَةَ مُضْغَةًۭ فَخَلَقْنَا ٱلْمُضْغَةَ عِظَمًۭا فَكَسَوْنَا ٱلْعِظَمَ لَحْمًۭا⟫

We made the sperm into a clinging clot, and the clot into a lump of flesh, and the lump of flesh into bones; and we covered the bones with flesh; and then he says
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ أَنشَأْنَهُ خَلْقًا آخَرَ⟫

And then we gave it the final form. And from the story of ADAM (AS), we know that final form is the soul. Because the last thing Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) did in the story of ADAM (AS) is that he breathed his soul into him.

And I explained to you earlier, that in one TAVEEL, in one particular context, the embryo that is being mentioned here is ISLAM itself. He's explaining the development of ISLAM through the stages of the 6 messengers - ADAM, NOOH, IBRAHEEM, MOOSA, EISA and Rasul Allah(⟪ar:سلام علیھم اجمعین⟫) . And then I said that QAYAM (AS) is the 7th and the soul, who will bring this child of ISLAM to life.

In another context, in another TAVEEL, this same verse also refers to the 6 stages of development of one's ISLAM, through the 6 practices of the pillars of ISLAM. SO NUTFAH symbolizes TAHARAH; ALAQAH symbolizes SALAAT; MUDGHA symbolizes ZAKAAT; IZAAM symbolizes FASTING; flesh symbolizes HAJJ. And WALAYAH symbolizes the 7th and the final component of soul.

Now if you think about a still born baby, that has completed all the previous 6 stages of deveopment, are the hands and feet and eyes and ears of any benefit to that dead child? They're not! Even though they are fully developed, they are of no use to it. Because it's lacking the essential component of "soul" that brings these other components to life. And so an ISLAM, even when it is perfect in its outward practices of TSZSHJ, it is still useless without the essential component of WILAYAH. That ISLAM is like a still-born baby. Completely developed; perfect in its outward form and yet of no use to the one practicing it; because it has no soul. There is no connection with the divine. There is no internal knowledge to sustain and bring to life teh outward practices.

There is a HADEES of the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) where he said:

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ دخل الجنۃ⟫

The one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH has entered the paradise. People said, "that's really easy!". So we basically just have to recite the words and paradise is ours! To which the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) replied

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ⟫

Whoever says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH "with sincerity" will enter paradise. People asked:

⟪ar-quote:وما أِخلاصُھا یا رسول اللہ؟⟫

What is the sincerity of this testimony? He said:

⟪ar-quote:معرفۃ حُدُودِھا و أداء حقوقھا⟫

The recognition of its boundaries and the fulfillment of its rights.

Now if you look at the word HUDOOD, it comes from the word HADD, which means a definition. A HADD is what de-fines; or makes finite. We as human beings, we cannot operate in the realm of infinity. Things have to be broken down for us in order for them to be accessible. When we work, we need our tasks "defined" for us; when we play, we need the rules of the game "defined"; When we read a book, we require the "definition" of chapters; of paragraphs; of sentences; of words; of letters. Human beings simply cannot operate without a definition. We need to have an understanding of its beginning, its middle and its end. When we go on holidays and vacations, we need to choose a location; a spot. This is معرفۃ حُدُودِھا. Recognizing or understanding the boundaries. And boundaries, by their nature de-fines; it confines; it restrains! Now what is the Arabic word for restraint? It's ⟪ar:عقل⟫. The word AQALA as you all know by now, means to restrain. Restrain to what? To the set boundary! To the set definition. So AQL (intellect) works in boundaries; it works in de-fined spaces. Now what's interesting, is that as soon as the rules for a task are defined; the rules of transgressions get defined as well. In other words, as soon as I understand what it is that I need to do, I also come to know, what I'm *not* supposed to do. If I am bound within the confines of time, so for example, if I have to pickup my daughter from school at 3, I cannot pick her up at 2; and I cannot pick her up at 4. I have to operate within the boundaries of that definition set by the school.

And this brings us to the next term: ⟪ar:و أداء حقوقھا⟫. Once the boundaries have been defined, the next step is the fulfillment of their rights. Once the HADD (the limits) of work is defined, in the form of tasks, the next step is to execute those taks within their defined boundaries. There is not concept of "think outside the box" when it comes to religion. Because outside the box, lies the world of ambiguity; the world of innovations or بدعۃ. And if you remember why ⟪ar:امام المعز علیہ السلام⟫ , commanded سیدنا قاضی نعمان to write the book of DAYAM AL-ISLAM, it was to cure the problems of innovation. This is why the book was written, to define the boundaries. Because religion by its essence is "medicine" for the soul. And every medicine has a very specific, very clearly defined dozage that has to be taken at clearly defined time intervals.

So once the rules of the game are defined, the next step is to operate within the boundaries of those set rules. If you operate outside of those boundaries, what's that called? it's called "cheating". When reading a book, we have to go through the defined sequence of chapters - one after the other. If we just randomly start reading the chapters, the content will make absolutely no sense.

Now Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said ⟪ar:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ دخل الجنۃ⟫, he essentially set the boundaries; he defined the rules for JANNAH; the do's and don'ts for paradise. And what is that HADD? What is that boundary? LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH. If you look at the numeric weight of the word HADD, it is made up of 2 letters - HA and DAAL, and the numerical weight of this word is 12  (8 + 4 = 12). And if you count the letters of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH they're also exactly 12. So even from a numerical perspective we find this perfect equivalence between the two.

But then he further clarified by saying: ⟪ar:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ⟫; the one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH with sincerity will enter JANNAH; and then he further defined sincerity as two things: ⟪ar:معرفۃ حُدُودِھا و أداء حقوقھا⟫. To understand and realize its boundaries; its definitions; and to fulfill their rights. And this sincerity is where WALAYAH comes into play. Because what the definition does, is that creates ranks. They create a structure; and a certain organization in religion. It creates ⟪ar:مراتب الحدود⟫ . It creates ranks of stations within religion. You can imagine them as concentric circles. Each circle has it's own radius, that defines its areas of operation. Each individual rank has a certain specific definition of purpose. This is what he can and cannot do.

So for instance, a MANSOOB is specific rank with specific authorities (he's a circle with a specific radius). A DAI is another rank with a larger radius. A DAI can do everything a MANSOOB can do, and more. But a MANSOOB does not have certain authorities that a DAI has. Similarly a DAI has restrictions opposed on him by his rank. He cannot do what an IMAM can do. And then an IMAM is confined in the sense that he can't do what a WASEE can do; and the WASEE is restricted to the confines of his rank. He cannot do what a NATIQ can do. So for instance, a NATIQ is commanded by Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) to reveal and establish the outer aspects of his religion. But a WASEE is tasked with the responsibility of explaining the inner meanings of those outer aspects. So Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) was tasked with developing and establishing the SHAREEAH; and Maulana Ali was tasked with explaining its esoteric meanings. It's not like the messenger did not know the inner meanings; or Maulana Ali could not have established the outer aspects. They could have. But if they did that, they would be trangressing their defined boundaries. And this transgression is the ultimate recipie for chaos. Analyze at any problem historically, and you'll find this to be true. Wherever you find chaos; you'll find violation of this principle. It's a problem in معرفۃُ الحد or a problem with أدَّءُ الحق. They do not understand their job responsibilities - because they were placed in a rank they did not deserve or they covetted or usurped a rank they were not worthy of. Or they are simply not executing those responsbilities properly. And this is why I personally find Hazrat Ibraheem Sahab's statement so accurate, when he says: "In my opinion, a HADD is the one who remains and operates in his limits".

Returning back to the HADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), what he's essentially saying, is that if you want to enter the physical JANNAH, recognize the boundaries of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH and operate within them. What are these boundaries? Everything that the SHAREEAH dictates.

The boundaries of HALAAL and HARAAM

The boundaries of TAHARAH. What are the things that make a person unclean; and how to restore the self back to its pure state.

The understanding of the timings of SALAAT. The factors that establish SALAAT and those that break them. Understanding how do proper RUKU and how to do a correct SAJDAH. How should the hands be placed in relation to the head etc. To understand all these details of each body part in relation to the other body parts and then to execute them properly.

Same thing with ZAKAAT. What is ZAKAAT? How much gets due on money in the span of a year? To understand what's the difference between ZAKAAT of money; ZAKAAT on gold; ZAKAAT on land and cattle etc. and then to execute it within those boundaries. To not fall short. Same with SAUM, HAJJ and JEHAD. The details of the do's and don'ts that they entail. Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said that if you learn them, understand these boundaries, and operate within them, you will earn the physical JANNAH; which is the paradise of ISLAM. It is the comfort of safety and the peace of mind and heart that ISLAM offers. Because in ancient Arabia, as soon as one became MUSLIMS, all the rules of brotherhood applied to him. He can no longer be attacked. His house, his family; his material posessions; all of it fall under the protection of SHAREEAH law. Just be becoming MUSLIM he becomes entitled to the comforts and protections; or peace and safety of ISLAM.

ISLAM is a single dimension; EMAN is multi-dimensional

But then, in relation to this physical paradise of ISLAM, there is another paradise of IMAN. This is what is called BATINI JANNAH; or the spiritual paradise. And these two heavens are what Allah refers to in SURAH REHMAN. In s reminding us of all his favors and blessings, he says

⟪ar-quote:وَلِمَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ جَنَّتَانِ⟫

for the one who fears the standing before his master, there are two Gardens.

And what he's referring to is the garden of ISLAM and the garden of IMAN. In parallel to the submission for the physical practices of ISLAM, there is also a submission to spiritual ranks. Just as you cannot achieve the physical JANNAH without submitting to these physical practices; you cannot achieve the spritual JANNAH without submitting to these spiritual ranks. Because they are the ones who hold the knowledge of the "why" behind the SHAREEAH. Because if you think about it, within the outward physical structure of every single practice, you'll find an automatic inherent question of "why". So if we just take the example of SALAAT, there are very clear instructions about the importance of the "timings" of SALAAT. And for the one who has intellect, the first question that raises is, "why". Why is the initial time preferred over a later time? Not the superficial answer to that question is, because SALAAT is a call from Allah! And so when a master calls, it is perferred for the slave to answer that call immediately. If that's true, then why is the preferred time for ISHA later during the night? Because when it comes to ISHA, the later you pray it, the more preferrable it is. So how come in this instance, it is better to delay in answering the master's call? Why is there only 3 rakaat in MAGHRIB and 4 RAKAAT in ISHA? If we accept the superficial answer that because the time of MAGHRIB is short, while the time for ISHA is longer, then how come there are only 2 RAKAAT for FAJR? Because there is lot of time between FAJR and sunrise. Why should the fingers be spread out on the knee during RUKU, but joined together during SAJDAH? If you carefully study the outward practices of SHAREEAH, they are constantly challenging the intellectual with the question Why?!

And that's where the BATINI or the spiritual JANNAH comes into play. Because these practices are deliberately constructed this way, in order to push the intellectuals towards seeking answers. Where can we find those answers? In the spiritual JANNAH, which is the paradise of these spiritual ranks who provide us with this knowlege. So now here we have a different undrestanding of معرفۃ حُدُودِھا و أداء حقوقھا. The understanding of the authorities, power and knowledge of each rank. The understanding that a MANSOOB can deliver only a certain amount of knowledge. But there is a higher rank above him of a DAI, who possesses greater and higher forms of the same knowledge. And then on top of him is an IMAM who posesses even greater and higher forms of knowledge. Understanding their ranks, the authorities they have; the kinds and levels of knowledge each posesses; understanding what enabled them to achieve that rank; all of this is معرفۃ حُدُودِھا. And then to understand that by virtue of them being higher in rank, and for their favors and gift of knowledge that they give us, they now have a right on us. To understand that we owe them an allegience. To understand that each rank has a certain praise, and each rank is owed a certain gratitude.

For example, I am sharing with you all these beautiful pearls of wisdoms about our DEEN. Where did I get this knowledge from? From my teachers. So if you feel a sense of gratitude towards me, that gratitude is not complete unless and until you are also grateful to my teacher. Because had he not given me his knowledge, I would not have been able to share it with you. But then who did he learn from? The MANASEEB! Who did they learn from? The DUAAT? Who did they learn from? The IMAMs! Who did they learn from? The AWSIYA! Who did they learn from? The NUTAQA! Who did they learn from? JIBRAEEL AS. Who did he learn from Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala).

And so this is the wisdom in the HADEES, that:

من قال لا الہ الا اللہ دخل الجنۃ

The one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH has entered the paradise. So simply reciting the words LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH with the tongue, entitles one to the physical JANNAH. To the physical practices and the comforts and security of ISLAM. But then ISLAM is single dimensional. It operates on a single plane.

من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ

Whoever says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH "with sincerity" will enter paradise. People asked:

وما أِخلاصُھا یا رسول اللہ؟

What is the sincerity of this testimony? He said:

معرفۃ حُدُودِھا و أداء حقوقھا

The recognition of its boundaries and the fulfillment of its rights.

<!-- section 17 (id=6797, raw_sort=17): Childish vs Childlike -->

## Childish Versus Childlike — Distinguishing Immaturity from Innocence

In the previous session we looked at the HADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in which he defined the criteria of entering JANNAH. He said:
⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ دخل الجنۃ⟫

The one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH has entered the paradise. And then he clarified that statement further by saying:
⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ⟫
Whoever says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH sincerely will enter paradise. And when he was asked:

⟪ar-quote:وما أِخلاصُھا یا رسول اللہ؟⟫

What is the sincerity of this testimony? He replied

⟪ar-quote:معرفۃ حُدُودِھا و أداء حقوقھا⟫

The recognition of its boundaries and the fulfillment of its rights. And I explained both these terms in detail in the previous session.

> — *Image text (from image 034; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/034.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Now both of these statements talk about entering JANNAH. The word JANNAH has several meanings. The most common translation you'll find in the Quran for JANNAH, is "garden". Now why did Allah use the word garden? What is the most defining characteristic of a garden? What makes a garden beautiful? Its order and organization, right? That's the difference between a garden and a jungle. Everything is chaotic in a jungle, whereas in a garden, everything is in its proper place. Trees are where they're supposed to be; flowers os similar kinds are grouped together; the water fountain is right in the middle, right? Now if you look at the definition of the word "justice", that's exactly what that word means. Justice is to put things in their proper place.
⟪ar-quote:وَضَئاَ شَئیٍ حَقَّ مَحَلِّہ⟫

In other words, the design and structure of a garden, is an illustration of the word justice. That's the structure! What's the human experience of a garden? When you're in a beautiful garden, what do you experience? Peace and comfort! A garden is a place of rest and relaxation. In other words when there is justice; when things are organized in the way they're supposed to be, there is peace and comfort.

With the understanding of this definition of the word JANNAH, let's look at the prophet's HADEES again: ⟪ar:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ⟫; The one who rejects all false gods; the one who refuses to surrender to his false gods of passions and temptations; and accepts Allah as his one and only deity,⟪ar:دخل الجنۃ⟫, he enters into a state of peace and comfort. He moves out of the chaotic jungle of this DUNIYA, and enters into a spiritual system that is characterized by order and justice, resulting in peace and harmony.

And then he continues to say: ⟪ar:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ⟫; the one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH with ⟪ar:اخلاص⟫, enters JANNAH. Now if you look at both these statements, the only word that is different between the two, is the word ⟪ar:اخلاص⟫. And ⟪ar:اخلاص⟫comes from the root word ⟪ar:خَلُص⟫, which means something that is absolutely pure. This word ⟪ar:خالص⟫is also used in Urdu, which means the same thing - absolutely pure. The English word "pure" comes from the Latin word "purus", which means unmixed or unalloyed; something that is in its original natural state. So Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) by highlighting this "pure and sincere" form of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH, is also suggesting, that there is also an impure form of that statement. Now the word "impure" comes from the latin word "impurus", which means mixed with offensive matter, or tainted. Isn't that interesting?

So this is the idea, that we're all born with this nature pure state of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH within our hearts; But then as life continues, that purity or that innocense gets tainted; it gets contaminated with the lust of this DUNIYA; with the lust of material posessions; lust of status; lust of position and power. But these impurities are all things that we acquire later in life. Immorality is something that we acquire later in life; just as we acquire morality. They're both acquired.

Morality and faith
