Now what's really interesting, is that if you look at the nature of morality and compare it to faith, you'll find them to be extremely close in their essence. In the same way, if you compare the nature of immorality and the nature of disbelief, you'll see that they too, are also extremely similar.

> — *Image text (from image 035; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/035.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

DUAAT have explained that all good morals: being generous, courageous, being upright, being noble, being forbearing, being clement, patient; they all stem from a modest regard for the self. All good morals are based on humility of the self, and a high regard for the other. You'll find all good morals to altruistic in nature. And this is why one of the highest state in self-purification in ISLAM, is to overcome one's own selfishness. Because we cannot truly love someone else, unless and until we've overcome our own selfishness. Allah says in the Quran:
⟪ar-quote:ِلا یؤمنُ ا حدُکُم حَتّٰی یُحِبَّ لاخِیِہِ ما یُحبُ لنَفسِہ⟫

None of you can be true believers, until you loves for your brother what you love for yourself. In other words, this altruism; this capability of recognizing the other person's value; this ability of never believing that I "actually know" the reality of the other; while having a much lower estimation of oneself, is what really lies at the heart of morality. This is how we preceive morality in the ISLAMIC sense.

Now when we look at faith, it is exactly the same thing. Because in the context of ⟪ar:ایمان⟫, Allah is the *other*. ⟪ar:ایمان⟫in relation to morality, is having a lower estimation for the self, and a higher estimation for the "other", in this case the "other" being Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). Because Allah has rights on us. He is the one who has given us everything that we have. And because of his generosity, we owe it to him, that we give his command a higer estimation, than we give our desires and our temptations. Because just as we are constantly observing *his* world (which is this universe that he has created for us); Just as we are constantly observing his world, he is also observing "our" world. Just as we are constantly witnessing what he did for us, he is constantly witnessing what we're doing for him. That's why one of the names of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) is ⟪ar:الشھید⟫(The witness). SubhanAllah! So faith and morality are very very close together in meaning.

On the other hand, if you look at poor character; at the heart of all immorality, is a grandizement of the self; looking down upon others. This is a trait that is extremely similar to disbelief. Because ⟪ar:کفر⟫or disbelief is a blatant rejection of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) and his existence. It is looking down upon the majesty and the beauty of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). It is a denial and refusal, for all the good that he has done for us. So we see that bad character and disbelief, they often go hand-in-hand.

Now in this world, we find Muslims (believers) with an extremely bad character; and we find disbelivers who possess an extremely moral character. So in that particular respect, that disbeliever, with a high moral character, is literally standing at the gates of faith; while this believer of a wretched character, is standing at the doors of damnation and perdition. The disbeliever is closer to stepping into faith, because his heart is already aligned to what he's being called to. And the believer having an immoral character, is much closer to losing his faith, because his heart stands in opposition to what the religion is calling him to. So you can see how deeply morality is connected with faith; and how strongly immorality is connected with disbelief.

And this is why in the Quran, when Allah talks about the enemies of the prophet, what does he always talk about? Whether it is a Meccan SURAH or a Medani Surah; what does he always talk about? He talks about their bad character! How they are proud and arrogant.
⟪ar-quote:أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ۔۔۔ فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ۔۔ وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ⟫

How they repulse the orphan. How they break their word. How they break their covenants. Why? Because at the root of disbelief is bad character. So this connection between good character and faith is really very important to understand. And this is why when we want to measure our own personal faith, we always need to measure it in the light of our character. If our character is flawed, then our faith is also not going to be where it ought to be. Because bad character is the greatest impurity there is; and it stands in direct opposition to our natural disposition (our FITRA). Part of our natural disposition is the knowledge of good and evil. One of the greatest spiritual joys; one of the greatest spiritual ecstasy's in life, is doing good for others. Rational human beings derive immense pleasure from good; and we also experience great pain and guilt and regret from evil.

Children born on FITRA

And so the HADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) alludes to a return; a journey from impurity back to purity. Because every child is created with this natural diposition called FITRA. And this FITRA is everything that is pure. A child is born with perfect moral character. There is a another very famous HADEES in which Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said:

⟪ar-quote:مَا مِنْ مَوْلُودٍ إِلَّا يُولَدُ عَلَى الْفِطْرَةِ⟫

There is not a single child; that is not born upon this pure state "Fitrah"; of natural disposition

⟪ar-quote:فَأَبَوَاهُ يُهَوِّدَانِهِ وَيُنَصِّرَانِهِ وَيُمَجِّسَانِهِ⟫

It is then his parents (in other words, the external influences) that make him a Jew, Christian or a Zoroastrian.

In other words, the flaws in our character is something that we develop over time - by the influences of our enivonrment. It is an impurity that we acquire later in life through nurture, and by the influences of the company we keep. But if you look at the original state of a child, it is extremely pure. You smile at a child, and it will smile back at you. You look at it in anger and it will start crying. And when i say child, I mean those very initial years from birth to about 3 - 4 years of age. That's the age in which every single child, unanimously demonstrates its FITRAH.

A child will never lie. It is impossible to make a child lie. It just doesn't know how to.

A child will exhibit "perfect" belief. When you tell a child that there is no god but Allah, He is the sole creator of the universe; and the child will have absolutely no problem in believing that. He'll believe it without the shred of a doubt. He's not going to ask for empirical and rational evidence. He'll believe absolutely. No one has a more staunch belief than a child.

You tell a child that Allah is merciful; he loves you; he loves you more than his parents, the child will believe that. He will accept it! He will accept it and not let go of that belief in the most trying of situations. The child will find some reason to prove that concept true. No matter how illogical the statement appears to us. Because in the childs world-view, Allah is merciful.

A child will never blame Allah for its suffering; because it has no doubts about the love of Allah that was taught to him by its parents. I have read and heard from people, that the best display of this is in cancer wards for children. When they find out that they have cancer, they don't blame Allah for it. Parents will cry and complain: How could you do this to my child? Where is your mercy? Where is your love? But the child will never complain. It will accept the divine will without any problems. SubhanAllah!

Now if you teach a child, the inverse of these thigns - if you teach it that there is no Allah, or that he is cruel; they will believe that too. And they'll believe it just as strongly. Because acceptance and surrender, is part of a childs natural disposition. It's part of its FITRAH. Whether you teach it good, or you teach it bad, the child will take it, and exhibit a perfect, unshaking conviction for it! Because surrender and submission to a higer source (parents in this case) is part of its FITRAH.

Every child is selfless in its pure state. A child will always be happy to share its toys with others kids.

A child exhibits perfect obedence and servitude in its pure state. You ask a child to bring you a glass of water, it'll run to do it for you, a 100 times in a row, with a big smile on its face. The child will never say, "Go get it yourself! I'm not your servant!".

I child will always forgive; and it will forgive instantly and unconditionally, no matter how many times the parents mess up. The child will never keep count of how many times it has forgiven the parent. And once the child forgives, that event is completely erased from his memory as far that person is concerned. It's like the event never happened. You'll never see a child who keeps bringing up the past and holding it against you.

A child will never over-eat - no matter how delicious the food is, it'll stop eating or drinking as soon as it is satisifed. You give a child the choice between alcohol and milk, and 10 out of 10 times the child will choose milk.

These is all a manifestations of its pure angelic state. Fear is also a condition of FITRA. A child gets scared when the parent becomes angry. Because fear is part of its primordial nature.

Now how does a child learn? We know that children learn more from pure "observation" than they learn from anything else. Children are much more in the sensory world, than they are in the world of meaning. The word or a child in Arabic, GHULAAM, it means "to lust". And lust is associated with the senses. So a child operates in the sensory world. This doesn't mean that children don't understand things; but their dominant mode is sensory. This is why why a baby is always grasping at things, tasting them, touching things, putting them in their mouth. And the reason why they do that, is because they're literally training themselves. They are getting themselves accustomed to this world. That's their way of studying this world. They are wiring up their internal program, like when you boot up a computer. And all of this is a preparation, to become knowers of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) through the study of the sensory. Because Allah created this ⟪ar:عالم⟫so that human beings can study it through their empirical and rational observations, and come to know of him. And so a child perfectly manifests this quality by its FITRAH. Because we have all come from a realm of pure unadultrated "meaning", and we've been born into this sensory world. So now we have to get accustomed to the sensory stuff as well. We have to get back to that meaning, through the sensory. And this is why in their initial pure state, children accept Allah so easily. Because is part of their FITRAH to see things in black and white. And we've all had that experience, where a child will point out to a reality in the most simplest forms; whereas you and I will see that exact same reality in a very complicated fashion.

So children are born with a deeply spiritual nature that wants to seek out Allah. They did this experiment on young infants, where they threw a ball behind the child to see how it reacts. And in every case the child turned around and tried to find the source of that sound. Who taught that infant that when a ball is dropped it makes a sound? Who taught the child that the sound of the ball dropping is an effect that was generated by a cause. Why is the child turning its head in order to try and seek out the source of that sound? It's all part of its FITRAH to know that the existence of this world has a "cause". There is an ultimate source that "caused" this universe to come into existence. SubhanAllah! Look at the perfection of Allah's design! AllahuAkbar!

But then children are also extremely beasteal  in nature. This is where we get the difference between a "child-like" behavior and a "childish" behavior. We have these two words to describe both natures of children. Childish is a very negative trait; where as childlike, is a very positive trait. Its a summation of all the angelic beauty of children. It comprises of the innocence and the pure nature of children. This is why Rasul Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) would smell new born babies and said that they reminded him of the fragrance of paradise. But then the beast like aspects also have to be dealt with; where it begins manifesting the traits of the ego; in the form of selfishness. Me, Me, Me! Me, myself and I. That's where the deviation from that pure state begins to occur. But that is extremely important as well.

Because as a childs ego begins to develop, the very first word that it really comes in contact with, is the word "No". "Denial" or "rejection" is the very first thing that children deeply connect with. And that's really interesting because our creedal formula LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH also begins with a denial. It begins with a rejection. It begins with the word LA. Because we do need to get a handle on rejecting and denying false gods, before we can affirm and accept the one true God. And so this is all part of the childs humanizing process. This is where knowledge and education comes into play; to teach children how to balance negation with affirmation.

Now with that understanding, if we revisit the HADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in which he says that every child is born on this natural disposition of FITRA.

⟪ar-quote:مَا مِنْ مَوْلُودٍ إِلَّا يُولَدُ عَلَى الْفِطْرَةِ⟫

What he's saying is that every single child, in its original, "pure" state, manifests all characteristics of a perfect believer. But the thing is, that a childs belief is based purely on faith! right? The conviction of a child is purely based on its faith and trust in its parents. That belief is not backed up by any intellectual or rational evidence. In other words, it can be argued that the child does not know any better. Which is absolutely true. This is why Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said:

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ دخل الجنۃ⟫

The one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH has entered the paradise. And what's so beautiful about this HADEES, is that it does not exclude the people who operate on this initial state of child-like behavior. It does not exclude the people who operate purely based on blind faith. Because not every individual has the capacity, or the luxury of intellectual reasoning. All human beings have an intellect, but not everyone gets the environment; the conditions; the nurturing; the knowledge and education, that is required for the growth and development of their intellects. So this HADEES accepts all these people who are operating on a staunch belief, based simply on the teachings of their elders. Realizing the weakness of their intellects, they put their entire faith in the religious ranks of our HUDOOD, MANSOOB, DUAAT and IMAMS. The fulfill their obligations; they pray 5 times a day, fast the month of Ramada, pay their ZAKAAT; they fulfill all the 7 religious practices without asking why, adn that is perfectly acceptable by Allah.

But then, this level of blind faith, is nevertheless a lower form JANNAH. It is a lower form of comfort for the intellectual. There is a different, it's a lower form for "us" because we consider ourselves to be intellectuals, but it is not necessarily a lower form for them. You understand? They are exactly where they're supposed to be. For example if you look at a child who drinks milk, and compare it to something like BIRYANI, obviously from our perspective, the formula is not all that appetizing compared to BIRYANI. But the child is absolutely fine with it. The child is not crying about why I can't have BIRYANI. And a parent will never feed their new born baby BIRYANI, because they know the child won't be able to handle it. So when we talk about lower and higer forms, you have to keep in mind, it's subjective. So blind faith is a lower form of practice; not to the one practicing it; but to the intellectual who knows he is capable of so much more

In Sufism, they call a spiritually immature person a child, even if the person is physically an adult and 80 years old. It doesn't matter. Ghazali once wrote a book titled ⟪ar:یا ایھا الولد⟫,  Oh my child! And he wrote it to a man who was well into his forties; because he considered him spiritually immature. And this certainly applies to our times as well, because a lot of believers today are spiritual children. Now what's interesting, is that both "fear" and "reward" are tactics that work with children. You give a child the hope for the reward, or a fear for punishment, and the child will fall into line. And this is why when you study the Quran, you find all these descriptions of paradise and hellfire. Because it is speaking to a bunch of people who are in this infantile state. They respond to those kinds of incentives. And also if you study the descriptions of this lower paradise, you'll find it talks about comforts that are related to the sensory world. Pleasures of fruits and taste, beautiful fragrant flowers; people leaning on soft cushions

⟪ar-quote:مُتَّكِـِٔينَ عَلَىٰ رَفْرَفٍ خُضْرٍۢ وَعَبْقَرِىٍّ حِسَانٍۢ⟫

Reclining on green cushions and rich beautiful mattresses. Because this is what a child finds attractive.

But in the true sense of our tradition, this type of JANNAH is not the desired goal for the intellectuals. Because for the intellectuals, there is this second form, a higher level of JANNAH, which is geared towards this idea of free will. Acts that are not slavish in nature; that are done out of fear. Acts that are not done as a trade. I'll do this, if you do that for me. I'll pray 5 times, if you give me paradise. Our tradition is primarily based on what's called ⟪ar:عبادۃ الاحرار⟫ (Worship of free men). This is why Maulana Ali would say in his prayers:

⟪ar-quote:یا الہی ما عبدتک من شوق جنتک⟫

Oh Allah! I do not worship you out of the enticement of your JANNAH;

⟪ar-quote:ولا خوفٍ⟪ar-quote:من⟫ النَّارک⟫

nor do I worship you out of the fear of hellfire.

⟪ar-quote:بل وجدت مستحق لی العبادۃ فالعبدتک⟫

I certainly found you worthy of my worship, and for that reason alone I worship you!

So these are acts that are not based on hopes of reward; nor are they done out of fear of punishment. These are acts that are done "purely" for the love of Allah. And this is where we find the second part of the HADEES that contains the word IKHLAS.

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ⟫

Whoever says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH sincerely will enter paradise. Whoever purifies this KALIMA, is the one that will enter JANNAH. And how is this purification achieved?

⟪ar-quote:معرفۃ حُدُودِھا⟫

Recognizing its limits - understanding its scope of influence

⟪ar-quote:و أداء حقوقھا⟫

and then fulfilling its rights, by practicing within the prescribed boundaries.

And these are "pure"acts committed by free people. And this purification is actually a return, to that same, original, pure, "child-like" behaviour, through the employment of the intellect. This is the certainty (the kind of purity) that is achieved through knowledge; and the goal is now to return to that child-like nature of FITRAH that we were created upon. In other words, as infants, we exhibited all the angelic traits of a believer; but we did it without understand. The goal now is to return to that same pure state once again, but this time with belief and a conviction that is backed up by knowledge and intellectual reasoning. To once again become "child-like" in our nature even as adults. To give up our "childish" behaviours. Because there are a lot of adults, who are constantly operating at this childish level. And that is the meaning of purifying our LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH.

As infants, we were born in the "pure" state of FITRAH, where we loved unconditionally. But that's because we didn't know any better. IKHLAAS, is to now return to that same unconditional love with the knowledge and recognition of the divine. As children, we shared our things with other. We were exteremely generous in that "pure" natural state. IKHLAAS, is to now return to that same level of generosity, but this time with the knowledge and the recognition of the divine. As children, we were incredibly forgiving. IKHLAAS, is to now return to that same state of being forgiving with the knowledge of the divine. And this is

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ⟫

Whoever says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH sincerely will enter paradise. This level of JANNAH is a entirely different plain of operation. It is a completely different kind of world; and its comforts are of a much higher form than the previous one. And if you study the descriptions of this second level of paradise, you'll see that it is characterised by beautiful scenaries. Rivers flowing under beautiful gardens!

⟪ar-quote:أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ⟫

For them are gardens under which rivers will flow

⟪ar-quote:لَا يَسْمَعُونَ فِيهَا لَغْوًۭا وَلَا تَأْثِيمًا ۔۔۔ إِلَّا قِيلًۭا سَلَمًۭا سَلَمًۭا⟫

They will hear no useless speech, except messages of peace and safety

These are all descriptions of spiritual pleasures; as opposed to the prevoius ones, that were descriptions of purely physical pleasures. Because a spiritually mature person will always prefer serenity, tranquility and peace of mind over physical pleasures. right?

---

<!-- section 18 (id=6798, raw_sort=18): TAVEEL OF SURAH TEEN -->

## Taʾwīl of Sūrat al-Tīn (Q95)

In the previous session we looked at one of the interpretation of the HADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in which he explained the criteria for entering JANNAH; which in the Quranic sense means "gardens". He said:
⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ دخل الجنۃ⟫

The one who says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH enters the garden. Then he said

⟪ar-quote:من قال لا الہ الا اللہ مخلصاً دخل الجنۃ⟫

Whoever says LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH sincerely enters the garden. And I explained that the spiritual experiences of JANNAH are related to peace, comfort and tranquility. It has to do with the feeling of being satisfied and content. And that level of satisfaction is achieved through ⟪ar:معرفۃ حُدُودِھا و أداء حقوقھا⟫. It is to gain the knowledge and awareness of the parameters and boundaries of LA ILAHA ILLA ALLAH and then to act within the constraints of those boundaries.

Today what I'd like to do is to share with you an experience of this JANNAH (of this spiritual comfort), which is attained through the understanding and comprehension of meaning. We're going to look at the interpreation of SURAH AL-TEEN; which is the 95th SURAH of the Quran. This SURAH begins with Allah taking 4 oaths.

Significance of an oath?

> — *Image text (from image 036; citation unverified)*
  (image preserved at ../images/036.png)
  *Note:* AUTONOMOUS_STUB — placeholder sidecar. The chapter is sealed with needs_human_review=true. Human reviewer to revisit and replace with a real classification.

Now oaths are a very interesting topic in the Quran. And before we proceed, its really important to have a clear understanding of why Allah takes oaths in the Quran.

Let's think about why we take oaths. When do we take an oath? When do we, as human beings, feel the need to swear by something? DUAAT explain that an oath is taken for two reasons. The first is when you are not being believed. When someone doesn't believe what we're saying, we are compelled to swear by someone or something. The second reason for taking an oath, is to make a promise. Like for example in courts, when a witness is sworn in by saying - "I swear to tell the truth, the whole truth and nothing but the truth..." Those are the two reasons, why we generally take an oath. Either we are **not**being believed, and we want to other person to believe us; or we need to make a firm promise or a commitment.

Now the ancient arabs had a third reason for taking oaths. When they wanted to grab someones attention in order to say something really important, they would preceed their statement by an oath. And the more emphasis they needed to put on their statement; the more they wanted to grab people's attention, the more oaths they would tack on before they said what they needed to say. So think of it like when we highlight a line or a paragraph in a book. The highlighter they used for speech were oaths. So that's the first thing to understand. The reason we take an oath, or swear by things is to make someone believe; to make a firm commitment or a promise; or to grab people's attention and put emphasis on what is being said.

The next thing to understand, is the object of the oath itself. The thing or the person one is swearing by. What kind of object is used for swearing? or what kind of person is sworn by? You always swear by "someone or something" that is noble, honorable, extremely valuable; or someone that is very close to your heart. If you swear by something of no value or if you swear by a stranger that you don't really care about, then the oath does not hold any importance. So for example if I say, "I swear by all the mosquitoes in my house; or I swear by the garbage man truck that comes every Thursday; I swear on the life of this serial killer, to tell the truth, the whole truth and nothing but the truth", you're not going to have much confidence in what I have to say, right? Why is that? Because I'm swearing by things which I do not really consider to be valuable. So that's the second thing. The object of the oath must be noble, respectable, valuable, of high importance in the eyes of the person taking the oath.

The third question is, what purpose does the object of the oath serve? When one swears by something, what they're essentially doing, is that they are either making that object a "witness" for their statement, or they're using that object as "evidence" for the statement they're about to make. So in a court when someone swears by the Quran, he's essentially making the Quran a witness the testimony he is about to make. If he's telling the truth, the Quran will testify in his favor on the last day; and if he's lying, the same Quran will testify against him on the final day. And the jury accepts that testimony, because they understand that the Quran holds a great deal of value in a Muslims eyes. If a Jew swears by the Quran, its not going to be the same thing. So the object of the oath becomes a witness for the testimony that is being made.

Similarly, the objects of an oath is also used as "evidence" for the statement that is being made. Especially in ancient arabia! So for example, when an Arab wanted to catch the attention of the audience, he would swear by something. He'd say, for instance, "I swear by the sun!". And everybody would stop what they're doing and gather around. Because they understood that the sun is an extremely important, extremely valuable thing. So it would immediately grab their attention; because they understood what's coming next must also be very important. And the person taking the oath, would then use the sun as evidence for what he's about to say. So he'd say something like, "I swear by the sun! Acquiring knowledge is obligatory on all Muslims". Why use the sun as evidence? What's the relationship of sun and knowledge? Sun is bright! It is life giving! It is powerful, and it is absolutely essential for life! And so is knowledge! Knowledge is luminous; it gives spiritual life; it is powerful; like the sun. And so when the ancient Arab would take an oath, they would use an object as evidence, that was somehow closesly related to the statement they were about to make. Because these Arabs had a superior form of imagination, remember? So they would easily be able to connect the two things together. So just as the existence of the sun is essential to life, acquiring knowledge is obligatory on all Muslims. You understand?

OK. So now we understand the reason for an oath, the value and the purpose of the object that is being sworn upon. The last thing to note, is the "person" who is taking the oath. Depending on the one taking the oath, there is a certain value associated with the oath. If a criminal is taking an oath, there is a certain value associated with his oath; which obviously is quite low. If a common man is taking an oath, it has a certain value. If a well known, famous man is taking an oath, it associates a different value to the statement he is about to make. If a king is taking an oath, it holds a completely different value. If a prophet is taking an oath, it's an even more esteemed event. Now what if Allah is taking an oath? What if the creator of this universe, our creator is taking an oath? What value would you place on his statement?

Does he even need to take an oath? Let's say we're talking to our Hazrat Ibraheem Sahab (عطا اللہ بقاہ). And he's trying to tell us something very important. He says, I swear by the Quran, I'm telling you the truth. How would we react? Hazrat Sahab please! You don't need to swear by anything. Of course I believe what you're saying! Now why do we have that reaction? Because he is an extremely honorable man, in a very dignified position. He is not someone we would associate lies and decipt with. And so we would not require him to take an oath if he's telling us something. But then if he does take an oath, it really grabs our attention doesn't it? We would naturally take what he has to say very very seriously. You understand? So if we place a MANSOOB's oath in such high regard, what's the value of a DAI's oath? What's the value of a prophet's oath? What's the value of the oath, when an IMAM takes it, when Maulana Ali (AS) takes it; when Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) takes it? It would be absolutely invaluable! Completely priceless isn't it? And yet these are all creations of Allah. And so if we place such high value on the oaths of creations based on their nobility and honor, what kind of importance, and what level of attention should be required, when Allah himself takes an oath? Because what we're learning is that the value of an oath is directly proportional to the value of the one taking the oath. So how valuable is a statement, for which Allah himself takes an oath? And not just one oath, but 4 oaths. That's something I want all of us to really become mindful of.

OK. So let's go over this once again. The reason for taking an oath is (1) to make someone believe (2) to make a commitment or a promise (3) to emphasize and stress the importance of what is about to be said. The object of the oath must be something valuable, noble and honorable to the one taking the oath, and can be used as evidence or witness before the audience. And then finally the nobility and the virtue of the one taking the oath, that proportionally magnifies the value and the importance of the statement that is about to be made.

So SURAH TEEN begins with Allah taking an oath. He swears by 4 things:
⟪ar-quote:وَٱلتِّينِ وَٱلزَّيْتُونِ⟫

I swear by the fig and the olive
⟪ar-quote:وَطُورِ سِينِينَ⟫

and I swear by mount sinai
⟪ar-quote:وَهَذَا ٱلْبَلَدِ ٱلْأَمِينِ⟫

And I swear by this city of safety. Which city is he talking about? The city of Mecca that the prophet is living in. Who's taking the oaths? Allah is! So right off the bat, the value of the oath, the value of objects that are being sworn upon, and the statement that is about to be made, all get magnified exponentially. Why is he taking an oath? Because an oath is taken when one is not being believed. Allah is the one who is not being believed, so he is taking an oath. Oath is used for making a commitment and a promise. Allah is making a certain promise and a commitment in this SURAH (which we'll look at shortly); and finally, an oath is used to create emphasis in the statement that follows; and the objects of the oath are used as witness and evidence to support the statement that is being made.

Now let's look at what is actually being said? Remember, oaths are used to highlight content. So the subject matter that comes after the oaths is what Allah wants to draw our attention to and take very seriously. And what is that?
⟪ar-quote:لَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ فِىٓ أَحْسَنِ تَقْوِيمٍۢ ‎⟫

Indeed we created man in the best stature.
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ رَدَدْنَهُ أَسْفَلَ سَفِلِينَ ‎⟫

And then we reduced him to the lowest of the low.
⟪ar-quote:إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ فَلَهُمْ أَجْرٌ غَيْرُ مَمْنُونٍۢ ‎⟫

Except those who believe and do righteous deeds. These are the people that shall have a reward without an end. This statement is a promise or a commitment. He is specifying the exceptions to the rule. He created man in the best possible form; but then because of their sins and evil deeds, they get reduced to the lowest of states, ⟪ar:(⟫⟪ar:إِلَّا⟫*except*⟪ar:)⟫ for a particular group of people. Who are these people?
⟪ar:ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ⟫
Those who have faith, those who believe and do good deeds. And then he promises

⟪ar:فَلَهُمْ أَجْرٌ غَيْرُ مَمْنُونٍۢ ‎⟫

They shall have a reward that is never going to end. And in order to say all of this, what does he present as evidence? and what does he make a witness? 4 things: The fig, the olive, Mount Sinai and the city of Mecca. And then he asks us human beings a question.
⟪ar-quote:فَمَا يُكَذِّبُكَ بَعْدُ بِٱلدِّينِ⟫

Then what causes you to deny the DEEN! What causes you to deny religion? What's stopping you from repaying this debt of gratitude that you owe Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala)? Why do you reject this way of life? Why do you reject this spiritual discipline? What do you reject this rain that can bring your dead souls back to life? All meanings of the word DEEN, remember?
⟪ar-quote:أَلَيْسَ ٱللَّهُ بِأَحْكَمِ ٱلْحَكِمِينَ⟫

Isn't Allah the best of all judges?

---

Outer Level of JANNAH

Now let's look at the connection of these 4 objects with the statement that Allah is making. What have figs, olives, mount Sinai and the city of Mecca have to do with man being created in the best posture?

The first thing to note is that all the objects of oath are noble and valuable objects. The first two items are fruits that have to do with sustenance, and the next two are locations that have to do with residence. We know that figs and olives both have a high nutritional value. And if you look at the second pair, Mount Sinai is the place where Moosa AS met Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) for the first time; and the city of Mecca, is obviously the city that houses the messenger and the KABA. So Allah is swearing by 2 categories which are essential to human survival; sustenance and dwelling.

But then if you look at the items mentioned in each category, Allah is covering both ends of the spectrums. Even though the first two are fruits, and they both have a high nutritional value, they're both opposite in tastes. Figs are sweet, whereas olives are bitter. Similarly if you look at mount Sinai and the city of Mecca, they're both places of dwelling, but one is a mountain and the other is a city (leveled ground). For the ancient Arabs when someone speaks this way, mentioning two ends of a spectrum, everything in between is automatically implied. So Allah is swearing by the sustenance he has provided man using two opposite tastes (thus implying all tastes in between); and two different places of dwelling (implying all the gradients in between).

And the statement his is making, is what? ⟪ar:لَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ فِىٓ أَحْسَنِ تَقْوِيمٍۢ ‎⟫

Indeed we created man in the best form. Because as opposed to animals, we enjoy taste and we live in proper homes, whether we build them in citites or in mountains. Allah has given man a "form" that enables him to do that. TAQWEEM comes from QAAMA, means to stand up straight. Allah distinguised man by creating him in this vertical upright position; whereas every other creature in this world is created with its face stooped down. If we were bent on our backs like animals, would we have been able to pluck olives and figs from a tree? or build the houses we live in? No! So you can see the relationship of the objects that are being sworn upon with the statement that is being made. So Allah is using these 4 things as evidence and proof in this life, to make the statement, that he created man in the best of forms and yet he chooses to fall to the lowest of stations by his disobedience to Allah.

But then on the day of judgment, these 4 things will become Allah's witness, and testify "for", or "against" us. For the one who believes and does good deeds, when they are being given uncountable rewards, these 4 things will serve as witnesses of Allah and testify. "Indeed! Allah did promise you this reward in return for your belief and good deeds. So now enjoy!". On the other hand, for the one being thrown in hellfire, these same 4 things will be a witness and testify, "Indeed! Allah did warn you about this in the world. He did say that he will reduce you to the worst of the worse stations if you sinned. You should have listened!". Also, if you think about the descriptions of hellfire, what are the two things that are described? food and dwelling! JANNAH and JAHANNUM are both locations. One describes beautiful delicious fruits; the other describes painful and torturous foods, like throns and blood and boiling water. So we can see how perfectly these objects of oath relate to what is being said. SubhanAllah!

---

Now let's take it from the top. Allah is taking an oath of 4 noble things, using them as evidence in this life, and a witness in the after life

⟪ar-quote:وَٱلتِّينِ وَٱلزَّيْتُونِ۔۔۔ ⟪ar-quote:وَطُورِ سِينِينَ۔۔۔⟪ar-quote:وَهَذَا ٱلْبَلَدِ ٱلْأَمِينِ⟫⟫⟫

I swear by the fig and the olive, and by mount sinai and the city of Mecca. Using these as evidence, he makes a statement:

⟪ar:لَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ فِىٓ أَحْسَنِ تَقْوِيمٍۢ ‎⟫

We created man in the best of forms. He then warns us of the depths to which human beings are capable of falling:

⟪ar:ثُمَّ رَدَدْنَهُ أَسْفَلَ سَفِلِينَ ‎⟫

And we reduced him to the lowest of the low states. How do you protect yourself from falling to these depts?

⟪ar:إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ فَلَهُمْ أَجْرٌ غَيْرُ مَمْنُونٍۢ ‎⟫

Except the ones who believe and do good deeds, for them will be a never ending reward.

So these are the parameters and boundaries that Allah defined. And how do we create sincerity?

⟪ar-quote:معرفۃ حُدُودِھا و أداء حقوقھا⟫

We recognize its boundaries. We understand what it means to believe, how we exhibit faith; we learn what good deeds are; and then we act upon it. We put this knowledge into action.

---

Inner Level of JANNAH

Everything I explained to you is a general, surface level understanding of these verses; that all scholars in the Muslim UMMAH share. And obviously there is nothing wrong with any of it. Any Muslim who has faith in Allah and does good deeds, is fulfilling his obligations, all of his acts are completely acceptable by Allah.

But in our SULEMANI tradition. By virtue of being on ⟪ar:صراط المستقیم⟫ , the one true path; and having been blessed with access to the incredible knowledge of IMAMs and DUATS, we are truly blessed to have some incredible interpreations of these AYATS in the form of TAVEEL and HAQAIQ. ⟪ar:سیدنا مؤید قدس اللہ روحہ و نور ضریحہ⟫is one of those amazing DUAATS.  In one of his MAJAALIS (which are known as ⟪ar:مجالس مؤیدۃ⟫), he tells us about this man who came to ⟪ar:امام جعفر الصادق علیہ السلام⟫ and asked him about the meaning of this same SURAH that I just explained.

He said, "YA IMAM! I have some doubts about this SURAH, and I have come to you, seeking your guidance in putting those doubts to rest." He asks the IMAM, "Why did Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) swear by these fruits? Even though I understand their nutritional benefits, they're still food items, that are either eaten, or they are thrown away. If they're eaten they turn into feaces and are excreted from the body; and when they're not eaten, they simply rot and get spoilt. The objects of the oaths are things that are precious and valuable to the one taking the oath. So I don't understand why these fruits would be valuable to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). And then why these particular fruits? Aren't all other fruits valuable the same way? So then what is so special about figs and olives that Allah chose them to swear by?

SYEDNA MOYYED writes, that the first thing IMAM JAFFAR ASSADIQ AS does, is that he makes this man promise that he will not share this knowledge with undeserving people. He takes AHAD of this man. And this is a demonstration of the fact that TAVEEL is not shared with people who are not under the oath of an IMAM. Because this knowledge has to be earned; it is extremely valuable and precious and is not just handed out to those who are undeserving of it.

After taking this mans AHAD, ⟪ar:امام جعفر الصادق علیہ السلام⟫ says, "You asked, why did Allah swear by fruits! Because in your understanting, fruits are something that are consumed and excreted; or they are discarded away to rot; and this certainly holds true for physical fruit. But in comparison to these physical fruits, are the spiritual fruits of JANNAH, that no matter how much take from them, they do not lose their quantity, and if you do not take advantage of them they do not change their structure - rather they constantly keep growing and developing in their beauty and taste. And these heavenly fruits are the messengers of Allah, that no matter how much knowledge and benefit you extract and consume from them, they never reduce in their knowledge! They are like lamps, which can light up hundreds and thousands of other lamps, without diminishing their own luminosity and brightness". Then he said, "Think about what a fruit is? Isn't it the essence and the best part of the entire tree? Similarly these prophets are the essence and the best creations of all of humanity. This is why they have been compared to fruits! So the fig is ADAM (AS) and the olive is NOOH (AS)"

The man says: "Why did Allah symbolize ADAM (AS) with the fig, and NOOH (AS) with the olive?" IMAM (AS) replied, "The reason ADAM (AS) was symbolized by the fig, is because normally in the life cycle of a tree, certain signs manifest before the fruits show up on the branches. For examples the leaves and flowers develop first and then the fruit appears. But figs are different, in that they directly manifest as fruits on the branches, without any prior signs. Now if you compare that to human beings, all human beings have to go through a gradual development process in their mothers womb, before than can exist in this world. But ADAM (AS) was unnaturally, and directly created from the earth without undergoing these prior stages - just as the fig shows up without its preceeding signs. This is why Allah has compared him to the fig.

The man then asked: "Why did Allah symbolize NOOH (AS) with the olive? The IMAM replied, "First understand the difference between figs and olives. Figs are sweet, whereas olives are bitter. The fig is eaten along with its seeds, whereas the seed of an olive is discarded. And if you compare the actual amount of these fruits that are eaten, the fruit of an olive is much smaller in comparison to the fruit of a fig. ADAM (AS) was created within the sweetness of JANNAH; whereas NOOH (AS) was created within the bitterness of this earth. And when ADAM was sent down for the guidance of humanity, his teachings were readily and fully accepted by his children, except for one. But when it came to NOOH (AS), he faced a tremendous amount of opposition; and he was discarded by his people, like the seed of an olive is discarded. Very few people accepted him and believed in his teachings, just as the fruit of an olive that is consumed, is much less in comparion to other fruits".

Then he said, "The olive not only symbolizes NOOH (AS), it also symbolizes IBRAHEEM (AS). Because when you consider the fruit of the olive, it is not eaten as much, as it is used for extracting olive oil. And the extracted oil is the true essence of the fruit, which is used far and wide. And the reason it symbolizes IBRAHEEM (AS), is because he is the true essence of NOOH (AS)'s teachings, who came from the progeny of NOOH (AS). And just as olive oil is used far more, in comparison to the fruit itself, the teachings of IBRAHEEM (AS) were accepted and spread far and wide in comparison to the teachings of NOOH (AS). So in reality, Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) swore by two of his great prophets - NOOH (AS) as well as IBRAHEEM (AS), when he swore by the olive"

The man asked, "What does the oath of Mount Sinai signify?". IMAM (AS) replied that Mount Sinai is the place of MOOSA (AS)'s supplications. It is also the place where he was chosen and given the burden of prophethood. So the mountain symbolizes MOOAS (AS). But then just as in the case of the olive, there is another personality that is hidden with this symbol, and that is EIAS (AS). In SURAH ALMOMINOON Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:وَشَجَرَةًۭ تَخْرُجُ مِن طُورِ سَيْنَآءَ تَنۢبُتُ بِٱلدُّهْنِ وَصِبْغٍۢ لِّلْآكِلِينَ⟫
And a tree that springs forth from Mount Sinai, that grows oil, and relish for the eaters.

Mount Sinai is MOOSA (AS), and this tree, that sprang forth from Mount Sinai, is EISA (AS). Because if you study the SHAREEAH of EISA (AS), it is an explaination and a clarification of MOOSA (AS) teachings. And this is why the AYAH says: ⟪ar:وَشَجَرَةًۭ تَخْرُجُ مِن طُورِ سَيْنَآءَ⟫ ; A tree that springs forth from Mount Sinai, ⟪ar:تَنۢبُتُ بِٱلدُّهْنِ⟫and grows oil. We know that no tree directly grows oil. There's a entire process that goes into extracting oil from a fruit. And so what the tree symbolizes is EISA (AS), who explains the true essence (the oil), the hidden interpretations and the esoteric meanings of the teachings of the gospel TAWRAIT that was revealed on MOOSA (AS). This is why EISA (AS) is the tree that grows oil. So by taking an oath of ⟪ar:وَطُورِ سِينِينَ⟫,  Allah is actually taking an oath of two prophets, MOOSA (AS) in the clear sense, and EISA (AS) in the hidden sense, because EISA (AS) delivered the hidden meanings and wisdoms behind MOOSA (AS)'s teachings.

The man said, "By the continuation of meanings that you have explained so far, I assume ⟪ar:بلد الامین⟫ , the city of safety, symbolizes Muhammad Mustafa (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)". IMAM (AS) replied, "That is correct! the city of safety indeed symbolizes the final messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)". Mecca is the final QIBLA (the direction) of Allah, that revoked all preivous directions. In this very city Allah constructed the first house that was ever built
⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ أَوَّلَ بَيْتٍۢ وُضِعَ لِلنَّاسِ لَلَّذِى بِبَكَّةَ مُبَارَكًۭا وَهُدًۭى لِّلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫
Indeed, the first House appointed for mankind was that at *Bakkah*, full of blessing, and a guidance for all worlds. And then Allah made this city the place of dewelling for his final messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). So indeed this city symbolizes Prophet Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). But just like the previous two examples, this symbol also represents another personality; and that is QAYAM (AS). Because the final hour of QAYAMAH began with the coming of the final messenger. That is why he is called the "final" messenger, because with him began the end of time. He is the first sign of QAYAMAH. It is said in a HADEES, that Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) joined the index fingers of both his hands and said:

⟪ar-quote:بَعَثتَنِی وَالسَّاعَۃَ کَھَاتَینِ⟫

I and the final hour were sent together like this. And this is why Allah calls it the city of peace. The city of Mecca symbolizes the messenger, and safety symbolizes QAYAM (AS). Because on the day of judgment a believer who followed the SHAREEAH of the final messenger, will find safety. He will be safe from the terrors of the hellfire. This is why Allah swears:

⟪ar-quote:وَهَذَا ٱلْبَلَدِ ٱلْأَمِينِ⟫

And I swear by this city of safety. So within this AYAH, Allah swore by the two great personalities: Muhammad Mustafa (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and QAYAM (AS).

So now if we look at this SURAH again

⟪ar-quote:وَٱلتِّينِ وَٱلزَّيْتُونِ۔۔۔ ⟪ar-quote:وَطُورِ سِينِينَ۔۔۔⟪ar-quote:وَهَذَا ٱلْبَلَدِ ٱلْأَمِينِ⟫⟫⟫

I swear by ADAM, NOOH, IBRAHEEM, MOOSA, EISA, MUHAMMAD and QAYAM (علیھم الصلواۃ و السلام). After swearing by these 7 esteemed personalities, Allah says:

⟪ar-quote:لَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ فِىٓ أَحْسَنِ تَقْوِيمٍۢ ‎⟫
We have indeed created man in the best stature. The word TAQWEEM comes from the word QAWWAMA, which means "to raise; to give shape or to create form". Because it is these 7 NUTAQA that give form to, and shape the religion of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). And so Allah uses these 7 personalities as evidence for his claim, that he created man with the potential of immense perfection. And what is the proof and evidence of that human potential? These 7 personalities, who are the true Caliphs; the true representatives of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) on this earth. They manifest that "perfection" of man, to which angels were commanded to prostrate.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ رَدَدْنَهُ أَسْفَلَ سَفِلِينَ ‎⟫

And then we reduced him to the lowest of the low. Who are these people? The ones who stand in opposition to these messengers. The one's who battled and fought against them, hurt them, destoryed their homes and family; those who disobeyed them; mocked them; made fun of them. Being among such people, and being one of them, is being reduced to the lowest of the low states.

⟪ar-quote:إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ⟫

Except the believers who do righteous deeds. What are righteous deeds? Acts that are in accordance and in obedience to the teachings of these 7 messengers.

⟪ar-quote:فَلَهُمْ أَجْرٌ غَيْرُ مَمْنُونٍۢ ‎⟫

For them will be a reward that will have no limits. For them will be a knowledge and an awareness of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) that will have no bounds.

So what you're feeling now is the experinece of JANNAH.

---

What is the wisdom of hiding these oaths?

After IMAM (AS) explained the TAVEEL of these verses, the man said, YA IMAN, you have convinced me without a doubt that these are indeed magnificent oaths! And indeed these personalities are worthy of being sweared upon by Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). I just have one question left. Why did Allah hide these symbolized personalities within these symbols? Why did he not swear by them openly so that everyone could easily understand what he was swearing by? What is the wisdom in hiding these meanings behind these symbols?

The IMAM replied, "Hiding these lofty meanings behind these symbols contain the same wisdom, as in hiding grains within their covers; and hiding fruits within their skins contain. The reason why Allah hid the flesh of the fruit under its thick skin is so that insects and other animals could not reach the fruits. Because these fruits were primarly created for man and no one else. And so there were protected in covers so only he could benefit from it. And so Allah hid his lofty meanings behind the symbols of the Quran so that only the "real" human beings; that possess the real "adamic" nature, and not just his form, can benefit from these meanings. Because if these lofty meanings reached into the hands of undeserving and biased people, they would corrupt it. They would add their own speculations and biases to these meanings and ruin them. And so Allah protected them and hid them in symbols, so that only the deserving ones gain access to it.

Another wisdom behind this masking, was so that the true IMAM could be easily identified by his knowledge. And their virtue would manifest itself against pretenders and ignorant people. So that when they are put to the test against those that have usurped their rights, their magnificence and glory can become evident; and the people of truth are separated out from the liars.

⟪ar-quote:فَلَيَعْلَمَنَّ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ صَدَقُوا۟ وَلَيَعْلَمَنَّ ٱلْكَذِبِينَ⟫

And Allah will certainly make known those who are true, and will certainly make known those who are liars,.

<!-- section 19 (id=6796, raw_sort=19): Friendship and love -->

## Friendship and Love (in the Iḥsān Mode)

So both these things HAD and HAQ - definition and

Love begins with friendship

The philosopher Aristotle said, “In poverty and other misfortunes of life, true friends are a sure refuge. They keep the young out of mischief; they comfort and aid the old in their weakness, and they incite those in the prime of life to noble deeds.” 

A friend could put one on the path of success and salvation; and a friend can put one on the path of destruction.

Genuine friendships have become difficult to form. They have become harder to make. Today the world has moved to words virtual friendship. And we have become so enslaved to our phones that just for us to have a 20 minute conversation without checking our phones or emails has become almost impossible. And so the more connected we have become to our devices the less connected we have become to each other. We are not able to have genuine real connections with each other. These devices are really cool but they have started to own us. We don't really have a life outside of them. You know how people who have asthma they have to take an inhaler every few minutes, because they have a problem in breathing. It has become exactly like that for phones.

I need Wi-Fi! I need Wi-Fi. Is there Wi-Fi in here? How can there not be Wi-Fi in here? So we gasp for Wi-Fi just as we gasp for breath. And as sad as it is this is what we have been reduced to.

We can go into this conversation with two mindsets. The first is that what kind of friends we should look for - that's the first kind of mindset that we can have when having this conversation. But that's a selfish way of looking at things according to the Quran. The correct way of looking at this conversation is, what kind of friend should you be. Not what kind of friends you should have but what kind of friend you should be to others. And when you become the right kind of friend to others; Allah will put the right kind people in your path.

There are at least 10 words used in the Koran for different kinds of friends. 10 different terms. And each of them has its own nuances, and how God brings it up in different verses. So today I want to walk through some of these terms, and for us to understand how God uses these terms in teh Quran. What is God have to say about these kinds of friends.

WALEE

The first of those friends is WALEE. This word in the Arabic language comes from MUWALAT which is a kind of protection; someone who takes care of your matters; a friend that in some sense when trouble comes he can guard you . He can handle your situation. So a WALI is used for a strong friend. One of the names of God is WALI

للَّهُ وَلِىُّ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟

Allah is the WALI of those who believe. He is a protective friend to those who believe.

وَلَا تَسْتَوِى ٱلْحَسَنَةُ وَلَا ٱلسَّيِّئَةُ ۚ ٱدْفَعْ بِٱلَّتِى هِىَ أَحْسَنُ فَإِذَا ٱلَّذِى بَيْنَكَ وَبَيْنَهُۥ عَدَوَةٌۭ كَأَنَّهُۥ وَلِىٌّ حَمِيمٌۭ

The good deed and the evil deed cannot be equal. Repel with one which is better, then verily! he, between whom and you there was enmity, as though he was a close friend.

even if between you and someone else there is animosity. You're talking to them and they are responding with the most aggressive language

Act with him as if he is looking out for you. HAMEEM comes from HUMMAH which is fever - it is used for intense heat. And this is used to describe the intimacy of friendship - when you are that close with someone that is a heat in your friendship. There is a closeness and intimacy and that friendship. I'm not talking about in the romantic sense. I'm talking about it in the sense that you feeling so strongly to words someone that it heats you up. This is the idea of HAMEEM in the Arabic sense.

And HAMEEM BTW is another word for friend. A friend then when you are with them you feel warm inside; you feel comfortable. That's called a HAMEEM. And the Quran is saying that you have to be like that to words someone who is being aggressive towards you.

ٱللَّهُ وَلِىُّ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ يُخْرِجُهُم مِّنَ ٱلظُّلُمَتِ إِلَى ٱلنُّورِ

7:196

إِنَّ وَلِۦِّىَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِى نَزَّلَ ٱلْكِتَبَ ۖ وَهُوَ يَتَوَلَّى ٱلصَّلِحِينَ ‎

12:101

رَبِّ قَدْ آتَيْتَنِى مِنَ ٱلْمُلْكِ وَعَلَّمْتَنِى مِن تَأْوِيلِ ٱلْأَحَادِيثِ ۚ فَاطِرَ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ أَنتَ وَلِىِّۦ فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَٱلْآخِرَةِ ۖ تَوَفَّنِى مُسْلِمًۭا وَأَلْحِقْنِى بِٱلصَّلِحِينَ

SADEEQ

The second kind of friend is a SADEEQ. SADEEQ comes from SIDQ which means truthfulness. SADEEQ is actually a very genuine friend. What that means is that you are friends with someone for no reason, except a genuine intention. In other words you are not friends with them because being friends with them will make you feel more popular at school or work. That if you're friends with them other people will think more highly of you. Or there really rich and you desire to get some advantage out of that. In other words you are not friends with them for an agenda. When your friendship has no strings attached it's true and genuine - you are friends with them for who they are - not because for the things they own, or the status they have, not for the artificial and superficial stuff. But if you have a genuine friendship without all of these things, then that is truly SADAQA. True genuine friendship, no matter what. So whether you're having a good day or a bad day, whether you're poor or rich, a SADEEQ is going to be a SADEEQ. They are going to be there for you. And one of the hardest thing to have in life is a SADEEQ. You can have people that you chat with her gossip with, that's easy. But having a SADEEQ is really difficult. These are the kinds of friends that never give up on you no matter how many times you fail.

Do not be brutal just honest

الصَّدِیقُکَ مَن صَدَقَت؛ لا مَن صَدَّقَ

Your friend is someone who is true to you; who is honest with you; not just someone who befriends you. Not just someone who is friendly with you.

In other words when you are falling off they are honest with you, and they say listen! I care about you. I don't want you to do this because I believe this is going to hurt you. And whatever it takes, no matter what the consequences you are genuinely honest with your friend. This is not about just agreeing with friend knowing well that the path he is chosen is going to lead to its destruction. They're not afraid that if you say something to them or they say something to you, the friendship will come to an end. So I don't want to say anything because he might get really upset.

On the day of judgment there are some people on the wrong side of the fence. They are heading towards the hellfire. Allah says about them in the Quran

وَمَآ أَضَلَّنَآ إِلَّا ٱلْمُجْرِمُونَ

So they're saying it is not our fault that we are going to hell. It is not our fault that we are in trouble in Judgment Day, it is criminals that misled us. Bad people misled us. Now who are these people?

فَمَا لَنَا مِن شَفِعِينَ

We have nobody on our site to make a case for us. SAHIFI is someone who likes you and when you are getting in trouble they stand in the way and say no no no no no... He's good. He's okay. Like imagine you're in trouble with the principal, and the teacher comes in and says... No he's a good student don't worry about it I'll take care of it. Thats شفاعۃ . They are saying, today nobody is coming to back us up. Nobody has our back today. And then they say

وَلَا صَدِيقٍ حَمِيمٍۢ

This is the only time the word SADEEQ is used like that directly in the Quran. They say today we have no true friends that are close to us; we have no loving close friends today. SubhanAllah! And by saying this, Allah is saying, that the converse is also true. The people on the wrong side will complain that we have no close friends today; and the people on the right side of Judgment Day, and they will have a close friend to back them up which is the SHAFAQ of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) . May God qualify all of us for that.

And there's another thing here. Why do we lose friends? Because we are honest to them and they don't want to hear that. And they can do that, but a SADEEQ does not give up on them. A SADEEQ still remains truthful. So friendships can be painful in this world; but you still do not give up on them. And then they become eternal friendships in the AKHIRA.

SAAHIB

This is a very comprehensive word in the Koran for friend. SAHIB could be used in the most casual sense for people that you are sitting next to want to train; or on a journey. You are on a train traveling to a certain destination and there is this guy sitting next to you for the next four hours, technically he can be called your SAHIB. So this word can also be used for some very casual acquaintance.

But if you spend a lifetime with someone that is also your SAHIB. But there is one thing that is generally common for someone who is a SAHIB.

SAHIB is someone who means well for you. They want something good for you. So if there is a problem they tried to help in whatever capacity they can. The more they know you the more they can help. The more genuinely concerned they are going to be. One of the names of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in the Quran is SAHIB

وَمَا صَاحِبُكُم بِمَجْنُونٍۢ

Your companion is not insane. Because he has had SUHBA with him. He spent a lot of time with themAnd he is actually concerned about them. He cares for them. He's not giving them a message to dominate them. He's giving them a message because it is good for them. NOOH AS when he was delivering his message said>

قَالَ يَقَوْمِ إِنِّى لَكُمْ نَذِيرٌۭ مُّبِينٌ

He said: "O my people! Verily, I am a plain warner to you,

I am warning you for your sake. LAKUM there - the TAQDEEM of it- is for IKHTISAAS and IHTIMAAM as they say in NAHU in Arabic. The point of that is that I'm specially looking out for you, not for myself. That's why I am giving you this message. Thats a SAHIB.

Concept of SAHIB at a societal level. - celebrate normalcy - don't create fake standards of living - being responsible citizen

can't be your friend because you have iphone 6 and I have iphone 7

It’s a cheap bag. It's GUCCI. It  was on sale for 800 - thousand. That shows you're not a concerned person

WALIJA

This term occurs once in the Quran. WALEEJA which comes from the verb WALAJA. And WALAJA YALIJOO in Arabic means to penetrate deeply. Allah says

يَعْلَمُ مَا يَلِجُ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ وَمَا يَخْرُجُ مِنْهَا

he knows what's goes into the earth and what comes out of it.

So WALEEJA is a friend who is all up in your business. They know all about what is going on in your life. And they are deeply involved in your affairs. You trust them so much that you can share anything with them. And you don't you share with them there actually involved. Now this is a very special kind of friendship. It is not a typical friendship. It is not someone you are nice to, or you sometimes hang out with, or you text back and forth. This is a very close form of friendship and very rare to find in this day and age. This is someone that you can trust with your bank account. This is someone you can trust with your children. This is someone you can trust in any affair of your life. These are people you give signed blank checks to because you're traveling for a month. I'm traveling for a couple of months please write out these checks for my bills or whatever. And you don't have to think twice about it. You would not at all worry about it. This kind of friendship is extremely rare today. And Allah made it a condition in the Quran that you can only have this level of friendship with a fellow believer. Allah says

أَمْ حَسِبْتُمْ أَن تُتْرَكُوا۟

Do you think that you shall be left alone

وَلَمَّا يَعْلَمِ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ جَهَدُوا۟ مِنكُمْ

while Allah has not yet tested those among you who have striven hard and fought

وَلَمْ يَتَّخِذُوا۟ مِن دُونِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا رَسُولِهِۦ وَلَا ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَلِيجَةًۭ ۚ

and have not taken Walîjah besides Allah and His Messenger, and the believers

What does that mean? Allah is calling himself a WALEEJ to us. You and I will go through trials and Allah will test to see how deeply is God involved in your most important personal matters. What is his role in your family decisions? What is his role in the kind of financial decisions that you make? The kind of business decisions that you make? The kind of career and education decisions you make? What is his role in your life? Is he a WALEEJ to you ? Do you have that kind of friendship with Allah are not? Then he added the messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) . How much do you consult the legacy of your prophet in the most personal matters of our lives? When you and I are having trouble in life, how much do we consult the life of the Prophet in his example? When you and I are having trouble with friends, how much do we consult the advice of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) ? How deeply involved is he in our most intimate matters? see today when we talk about the SUNNAH of the messager, we celebrate and we emphasize the most outwardly aspects of the SUNNAH. SUNNAH prayer before the FARD prayer; SUNNAH of keeping a beard; SUNNAH of being the first to say SALAAM. The SUNNAH of these mannerisms and this ettiquets that we learn from our beloved messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). But in many aspects these are still public and outwardly. But the most intimate matters of yours, the most internal matters, should I get into this financial transaction? Should I buy these clothes at this price or not? Should I go with my friends and do this thing that they're all doing? Should I just go with them? Have I involved the messenger and those? where is the SUNNAH in those matter? Even in the ways we talk; in the ways we carry ourselves. The way we talk to each other is so messed up. There is no SUNNAH in it.

Today there is no respect for the elder. There is no humility in communicating with each other or interacting with each other. Allah is telling us in the Quran that you have to be a WALI and a HAMEEM to an enemy. We cannot even be that way to each other. We start beating each other up over the head with evidence when we disagree with each other; just to put them down .

And then finally he includes other believers of being WALEEJA. If you find Allah intimately connected in your life; and you find the teachings of the Prophet intimately connected in your personal life; then Allah will give you the best kind of believers in your life. He will give you the gift of those kinds of friends that you can trust to the depths of your personal lives. And what a gift that is to have.. Because trust is something that is completely disappeared in our day and age. We cannot trust anyone today. We cannot trust the people that we work with; we cannot trust our friends. This kind of trust is gone from our lives. And Allah(Azza Wa Jal) is giving us the secret to finding those kinds of friends, if you let Allah in; if you let his messenger in (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) ; then the next step will be that God will give us true believers like that.

BITAANA

Another kind of friendship is BITAANA - it comes from BATAN. What does BATAN mean? Stomach. BATAANA is actually a friend who keeps your secrets. So the other one was involved in all your personal matters, this one keeps you secrets. When you tell them about something personal that happened today in your life, you can trust them to take that secret to their graves.

Today when you try to do that, when you tell someone a secret and ask them not to tell anyone else, they put you on speaker, and they begin texting it to their friends. Hey listen up! Don't tell anyone but you know what?! That is not a BITAANA. We all have friends who have a very light stomach, they just cannot keep a secret.

يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ لَا تَتَّخِذُوا۟ بِطَانَةًۭ مِّن دُونِكُمْ لَا يَأْلُونَكُمْ خَبَالًۭا وَدُّوا۟ مَا عَنِتُّمْ

O you who believe! Take not as Bitanah those outside your religion since they will not fail to do their best to corrupt you

Don't take secret keepers other than yourselves, meaning believers. This is actually the context of the battle of UHAD from AALe IMRAN. Batle of UHAD is a difficult military situation for the Muslims. There different communities that live in MEDINA such as Christians and Jews. Some of them they knew are cooperating with the disbelievers. So in that context Allah said Look! Don't tell your secrets to your Jewish and Christian friends, because you don't know who's going to spy on you in the state of war. So just be careful, because a lot of them are not going to leave any stone unturned; and they want the things that will harm you. And Allah is not talking about everyone, he's talking about those who have that propensity; who have the potential to harm you like that. So just be on the careful side in that context.

In this context we are finding a state of war and tense situation where intelligence leaking can cause lives. So one might casually talk and say, that yeah I met the prophet today, and he's going to be at this place under that tree at this time. For you it might not be a big deal. But for someone who is trying to assassinate the messenger this is gold. And maybe the person that you shared the secret would does not directly continue harm; but then maybe the one he speaks with does intend to harm. So it can perpetuate like that. So keep your close secrets to the closest among you. That's the idea.

Maulana ALi said: don't share your secrets - don't facebook your problems.

Quran also talks about BAD FRIENDS

KHAZOOL

The first bad friend that the Quran talks about is called KHAZOOL. KHAZALA in Arabic is close to the meaning of خضع  deception. KHAZOOL is a friend who only acts like your friend, until the moment of truth. And then you see their true colors. So they were with you and they were just like you; and they were right by your side when times were convenient. But then when times became tough, all of a sudden they disappear on you. And you were relying on them to be there for you but then there are nowhere to be found. This kind of friend is called KHAZOOL. And this is صیغۃ مبالغہ . So this is not just any ordinary deception, this is the extreme kind of deception. an extremely disappointing friend who leaves you hanging at the worst possible time. And this actually is the description in the Quran of SHAYTAN

وَكَانَ ٱلشَّيْطَنُ لِلْإِنسَنِ خَذُولًۭا

SHAYTAN is a KHAZOOL to the human being.  Why is ALlah saying that? Because man he is going to act like your friend in this life. He's going to make you get into things and he will convince you that it is for your own good; and it is for your own entertainment. He will make you watch movies and watch filth. He will make you buy stuff; he will make you go places; he will make you say things; he will make you build the wrong kinds of friendships; all of it, and you will think that life is good! I am living it up. This is all KHAZAL. Because when you get to Judgment Day he is nowhere to be found. When Judgment Day comes around he says, Look! Hey hey hey! I'm not an authority over you, and you are not an authority over me, so let's just enjoy the barbecue together. That's what is going to send Judgment Day. This is KHAZOOL> and we have to ask ourselves, are we this kind of people? Are we the kind of friends who desert and abandon our friends in their time of need? Oh you called, I didn't even know. Yeah! you knew! But you were KHAZOOLING it. Don't be that kind of friend. If you're going to be a friend with someone, be a reliable person. Reliability is an important quality and friendship. And not being reliable is one of the easiest ways to lose friends. You have some really good friends in your life, and you do not want to mess that up because of your irresponsibilities - because you weren't doing your part and that friendship. SubhanAllah!

KHADAN

This is a friend that you are attracted to - boyfriend or girlfriend. That's KHADAL. A friend that you will have the possibility of being attracted to. And it does not necessarily mean physical attraction, it can also mean intellectual attraction; or spiritual attraction. This is the friend that you obsess about.

مُحْصَنَتٍ غَيْرَ مُسَفِحَتٍۢ وَلَا مُتَّخِذَتِ أَخْدَانٍۢ ۚ

The women that should be qualified to get married.

The kind of women that men should try to marry our women that are MUHSINAAT. You're bringing them into the protection of your family. You want to start a family with them. That is the first thing you should look for in a girl when you want to get married. Is this a girl that I want to have a family with? Does she have the values that I want to pass down to my children? Will she be a good mother? Is she good to her own mother? The she has family values? And family qualities herself? If you are going to rebel against your parents for her and she is going to rebel against her parents for you, then you know what? Life is going to be an Indian movie for a short while, but then you are going to have the most miserable life because you don't have the most fundamental values of what it means to be in a family. What it means to have loyalty to people that have raised you. That if taken care of you.

We have this fluffy stupid idea of what love means. First of. Watching Indian movies for God sake. Stop! Please! How many times can you watch people running around a tree? Enough! And these movies are now getting filthier and filthier.

Look for a woman that is going to start a family with you. And she's not just there to get your lust out of the way. You just don't think she's cute or sexy or whatever. I'm going to marry her because she's so beautiful. I can't stop thinking about her.

Just because you have raging hormones and you are daydreaming about girls and things like that, it does not mean that you are in love. It just means that you have not control the temptations. And because of that you are ruining someone's life. You are ruining an entire family. Do you realize what you're doing? When you call it love? You tell me, if she was 50 pounds fatter, would you still be in love? If she had her face burnt off, would you still love her? She still do same person? It's the same soul within that body? If she was a burnt victim or something< would you still love her? Or would you fall in love with somebody else all of a sudden? And if you cannot answer that question honestly, then you are not in love. You're just hormonal. That's all you are. This is what we have done to relationships that are supposed to be beautiful. Marriage is supposed to be a beautiful relationship. It is supposed to be a lifelong relationship. But because you are constantly watching all of these models on TV, and women that are just throwing themselves at men, he developed his delusional concept of what it means to have love in your life. our profit came, to free this world of this nonsense. Because we have a more mature understanding of what it means to have love in our lives.

I'm not saying you should not marry for love; or you should not be attracted to another person. All of this things are fine. But there is a certain level of decency that you need to exhibit before that. And if you're okay with talking to a girl like that, then you should be okay with some guy talking to your sister that way. You would not be okay with that. Not if you had an ounce of decency left inside you.

QAREEN

The next kind of friend is a QAREEN, which is a very cool type of friend. QARAN is actually used in Arabic for a rope that is used to hold two camels together. That's called QARAN. When two camels are standing side-by-side and you tie them with one single rope, that rope is called QARAN. So QAREEN is someone who is always side-by-side with you. If one moves, the other one is forced to move. They're always moving together. So the friend that you are always hanging out with; you're always on the phone with them; you're always on their Facebook; you're constantly with this person; you become happy he becomes happy; he becomes sad you become sad. This is a QAREEN. And QAREEN is also someone that you have a lot in common with. Because you cannot tie two camels together where one is very tall and the other is very short. You have to have some equivalence. You cannot tie two camels together in which one is really fast and the other is really slow. You understand? So a QAREEN is someone that you share a brain with. You think like them they think like you. That relationship is a QAREEN. Now you can have a good QAREEN, and you can have a really bad QAREEN too. Allah talks about a guy who made it to Jannah and says

37:51  - study

قَالَ قَآئِلٌۭ مِّنْهُمْ إِنِّى كَانَ لِى قَرِينٌۭ

I used to have a friend I always hung out with

I don't see him in paradise. And then he finds out that he is in hell. And then he remembers how his friendship broke off. Because his friends started making fun of the AKHIRA; started living the life. And this man says that I can still be a friend to you but I can no longer be a QAREEN for you. I can be in everything with you. You're going to parties, you're doing drugs drinking alcohol; your womanizing; your watching filth that I cannot be part of. But I still care about you, and I'm still going to try to stay in touch. And the next time I go eat some PIZZA I'll invite you. Because I'm not giving up on you. But I cannot be QAREEN anymore. These are all the different nuances of friendship. So he says, Thank God I did not stick with you. You'll almost throw me off the cliff. Had I stuck with you, you would have eventually convinced me to do the kinds of horrible and evil things that you do. It would have been inevitable. And what we're learning now is that the people of paradise were almost people of hellfire. There are some people in paradise that were almost people of hellfire - and the only thing that saved them was that they gave up certain kinds of friends. In a certain way. They gave up certain kind of company.

BEST FRIENDS YOU CAN HAVE AND THE BEST FRIENDS YOU CAN BE. These are the two most beautiful kinds of friendships described in the QURAN. So let's begin with KHULLA

KAHLEEL

Allah describes KHALEEL as

أَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوٓا۟ أَنفِقُوا۟ مِمَّا رَزَقْنَكُم مِّن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِىَ يَوْمٌۭ لَّا بَيْعٌۭ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌۭ وَلَا شَفَعَةٌۭ ۗ وَٱلْكَفِرُونَ هُمُ ٱلظَّلِمُونَ

Be cautious of the day when nobody will benefit anybody else; nobody will pay off anybody's else's debts; you will not have any friendships that day.

Another word that comes from the same root word is KHILAL. When something goes to something. Like when you floss, and you put that floss in between your teeth, that is KHILAL in arabic. So KHALEEL is someone whose friendship penetrates deep within your heart. You have a deep-seated love for a friend that you care about and you miss so much when you're not with them. Thats a KHALEEL. Like you are always thinking about them. And you wish that you were back with them. That kind of a friend is a KHALEEL. And this is again a very rare kind of friendship.
