And this is the kind of friendship that Allah(Azza Wa Jal) had with IBRAHEEM AS

وَٱتَّخَذَ ٱللَّهُ إِبْرَهِيمَ خَلِيلًۭا

He was a KHALEEL to IBRAHEEM AS.

He also says :

ٱلْأَخِلَّآءُ يَوْمَئِذٍۭ بَعْضُهُمْ لِبَعْضٍ عَدُوٌّ إِلَّا ٱلْمُتَّقِينَ

That really close friends, who had so much love for each other; Judgment Day comes and they are enemies to each other. The only exception there is ALMUTAQEEN, the pious ones. And this is grammatically a very strong form of exception - which means that the only possible exception to that is people who protected themselves from making the wrong kinds of friends. Everyone else that you think you are best friends with, as this in America Thats my DAWG! That kind of friend, when Judgment Day comes along there no longer your friend.

In other words make your friends based on how conscious they are of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). Based on how responsible they are to their religion.

The day of judgment comes around and the wrongdoer says

وَيَوْمَ يَعَضُّ ٱلظَّالِمُ عَلَىٰ يَدَيْهِ يَقُولُ يَلَيْتَنِى ٱتَّخَذْتُ مَعَ ٱلرَّسُولِ سَبِيلًۭا

he is chewing on his hands biting it in frustration and saying، if only I took on a path alongside the messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). The word SABEEL as a path, is a very beautiful illustration of a lifestyle. If I only had a lifestyle that is along side, parallel to, the lifestyle of the messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). And the thing about a path is that when you are walking it, you will find particular kinds of travelers with you on that path. Every road has different kinds of cars. You can't have every car on every road. So when you take one road he will find certain kinds of cars on that road. When you're on a plane you'll find only certain kinds of passengers on that flight. When you're on the path of religion, their only certain kinds of people that one that destination that you seek. And those of the friends that you need to end up making. This is a really powerful verse in the Quran because the next verse says:

يَوَيْلَتَىٰ لَيْتَنِى لَمْ أَتَّخِذْ فُلَانًا خَلِيلًۭا

I don't know if there's any other verse in the Quran that has more despair in it than this one. Because it combines two words of regret together

يَوَيْلَتَىٰ لَيْتَنِى

this is exaggerated HASRAH. On top of that LAYTANEE which ismore HASRA. The word HASRA means regret. This verse is one of the AYAH filled with most regret. And what is it about? I wish I did not take this guy is a friend.

 لَمْ أَتَّخِذْ فُلَانًا خَلِيلًۭا

and what's so interesting is that the versus actually saying, I wish I did not take so and so is my friend. KHALEEL is someone that you have a lot of love for. And if you have so much love for them you would know their name right? But Judgment Day comes and you have so much regret; and the hate fills your heart so much you cannot even remember the name. So the verse says FULANAN KHALEELA. That is the kind of regret this person has.

When you lay a certain sport you will also make friends that play that same particular sport. When you play a certain videogame, you'll find other people playing the same videogame, you'll make friends with them. We make friends based on proximity especially around our interests. People who are interested in the things that we are interested in, we end up making closer and closer friends with, and the bond strengthens. This is why teammates are usually close friends. Now this is the kind of friendship that is being described when the man says مع الرسول . That I only took up a path that is alongside the messenger. If you are really into something for the sake of God, you join an organization, you help a project that is trying to do something to help society. That's doing something to help people; that's doing something to teach people religion. In other words you are trying to facilitate any good project . And the friendships that you make on this path, will end up being the closest friends you have on the day of judgment, because it was done under the shade of ALLAH. Because you came together for the sake of Allah. Because you wanted to be a part of the legacy of the messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam).

RAFEEQ

RAFEEQ in Arabic comes from RIFQA or RIFQ and it means comfort. MIRFIQAH is the pillow that you place behind your back when it's hurting. Also the small cushions on the couch, they're also called MIRFAQ. Because you lean on them and put your pressure on them and help you relax.

A RAFEEQ is a friend that when you are stressed out. When youre in trouble; when you are having a hard time - going to them is comforting. They're like a pillow that you can lean on any time. And by the way when people are reclining on a pillow are they sitting formally or informally ? informally. The relaxed. This is a friend you don't have to act a certain way in front of them. You don't have to be super formal, you don't have to constantly watch what you say. These are the people that you can chill with - you can completely be yourself - that's a RAFEEQ

وَمَن يُطِعِ ٱللَّهَ وَٱلرَّسُولَ فَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ مَعَ ٱلَّذِينَ أَنْعَمَ ٱللَّهُ عَلَيْهِم مِّنَ ٱلنَّبِيِّۦنَ وَٱلصِّدِّيقِينَ وَٱلشُّهَدَآءِ وَٱلصَّلِحِينَ ۚ وَحَسُنَ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ رَفِيقًۭا

Those who obey God and obey the prophet, they will receive special favors from God. They will be counted among which categories and have the company of prophets, those who confirmed the truth in the prophets; those who die for the sake of God; and good people. SALIHEEN. And at the end of it it says

What an awesome group of friends these people are.

Can you imagine being comfortable around Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)? And not being nervous? Can you imagine being comfortable around Maulan Ali and IMAMS?

And so even in this world we can find people that we can be comfortable around; that we can be ourselves around; we don't have to be fake around them. We don't need to constantly try to impress them. We can be with these people and they are SALIHEEN, they're good people. That's a gift of God.

In Surah ANKABOOT (Makki Surah).

A lot of young companions were there, who lost their friends. Parents didn't want to talk to them anymore; friends didn't want to talk to them anymore; they were getting bycotted only because they were Muslims. And what we learn from that passage is that when you decide to take a turn towards God, chances are you will be boycotted by your friends. Chances are you will lose friends along the way; chances are people will not want to hang out with you anymore. You used to hang out with your friends and do all kinds of things with them, now you say I cannot do that; I don't want to go there; I don't want to do this. I'd rather not watch that. What happened? You are okay with that last month? Yeah well that was last month. I'm not like that anymore. Yeah right! Comeon! really?! And then the try to reel you back in.

But you stop yourself and say no I cannot do that anymore. So they're going to say you are no longer fun to hang out with and they will cut you out. So even though you do not give up on them they will give up on you. And that can make you really depressed. The first thing that happens when you begin getting serious about Allah's religion, you start losing friends. Friends are really important thing in life. They are extremely valuable.

So Allah says as a consolation to these companions were losing their friends and even families in some cases. He says

وَٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ لَنُدْخِلَنَّهُمْ فِى ٱلصَّلِحِينَ

People who have faith and do good things I will absolutely enter them; I will certainly inject them into the company of the righteous. I just said, that one of the gifts from God is that you will find friends that are righteous. And if you ask yourself how it my going to get those friends? In this verse he tells us. He says, I can see you have lost friends. I can see you are getting boycotted; I can see that you are getting isolated. You continue to believe in me and do the right thing, and you watch! I will put you in the middle of really good people. I will do that for you.   لَنُدْخِلَنَّهُمْ فِى ٱلصَّلِحِينَ

یعنی فی الدنیا والآخرۃ

He will enter you in the company of good people in this world and the afterlife. What more can we ask for?

[84] The first thing the scholar said to him by way of setting forth the first principles of the manifest intermediaries (⟪ar:الاسباب الظاھرۃ⟫) and the beginning of their creation. He said:    

‘Allah is the **Originator**of things and the **Giver**of their existence (⟪ar:أن اللہ مبدع الاشیا و مکونھا⟫). He created them, and then initiated them without precedence, such that no prior entity served as a model for the later. On the contrary, He is the First of every first (⟪ar:ھو اول کل اول⟫) and the inheritor of every existence. He initiated His creation from a Light, with three words branching from that light.
1. The first of those words was His will (⟪ar:ارادۃ⟫)
2. From the will derived His command (⟪ar:الأمر⟫)
3. From the command came His saying to whatever He wishes “Be!,” so it became (⟪ar:کن فیکون⟫).

So the beginning of all creation was by Allah’s **will**of a **command,**executed through His **words**. (⟪ar:أرادۃ، أمر بالقول⟫)

| تصدیق بالجنان | قول بالسان | عمل بالارکان |
| باطن الباطن | باطن | ظاہر |

[85] ‘Now from those initial three words (⟪ar:أرادۃ، أمر بالقول⟫) there came the command, “**Be!**,” (**⟪ar:کن⟫**) which comprises of two letters and “**so it came to be**” (**⟪ar:فیکون⟫**), which comprises of five more letters. Hence those seven letters became the root-principles from which seven things were derived. From the Light was created the air (⟪ar:خلق من النور الھوا⟫), which was the first of those, singular and without any pair, unique among all things in its mixing and encompassing them, but not being encompassed by any of them. Thus it symbolically points to the One who has no like unto Him (⟪ar:لیس کمثلہ شئی⟫). Next from those three words came the water (⟪ar:الما⟫),  the darkness (⟪ar:ظلمۃ⟫) and the light (⟪ar:نور⟫)—the light of the heavens and the earth. Then He created from the water smoke (⟪ar:دخان⟫); from the darkness He created the thickness of the mud (⟪ar:تکاثف الحما⟫) and from the light He created fire (⟪ar:النار⟫).
